Typhoon Reaches Taiwan; 江海 Area Affected, Winds Strengthen, and Showers 20

(Nanjing) According to the Central Meteorological Bureau, the typhoon discovered over the Luzon Sea on the 17th reached the northeast sea of Taiwan on the afternoon of the 21st. Its location is 125 degrees east longitude and 24 degrees north latitude, moving north-northwest at a slow speed. The downstream of the Yangtze River and the coastal area of the East China Sea have been affected. The winds have strengthened, and there are showers. The showers in 本京 on the 21st were caused by the effects. (Central News Agency dispatch, 21st)

Scattered Bandits Fleeing in Tongxian 21

(Tianjin) Tongxian Telephone, more than 700 remnants of Liu Guitang's bandits were found in the Sanhe and Xiashun areas of Tongxian. On the 20th, the county magistrate of Tongxian, Cao Zhen, in coordination with the Sanhe local militia and police team, surrounded them. The bandits were unsupported, crossed the North Canal, and fled to the vicinity of the Thirteen Tombs in Changping County. The Jiji Special Commissioner's Office has telegraphed the First Special Police Brigade to intercept them. (Special dispatch, 21st)

(Beiping) Tongxian Telephone, last night, 70 to 80 bandits in plain clothes boarded grain transport ships and landed on the county border, fleeing to the war zone. (Special dispatch, 21st)

(Tianjin) Wen'an County, hundreds of bandits are hiding in the reed ponds and looting everywhere. On the 21st, a regiment of the 141st Division's Song Kentang's troops rushed to encircle them. The bandits resisted in the reed pond, and the officers and soldiers are besieging them. (Special dispatch, 21st)

(Beiping) The bandits discovered at Fengju Bridge in Tongxian, numbering about 40, have been routed by the local militia and have fled into Daxing County. (Special dispatch, 21st)

(Tianjin) Tongxian Telephone, at 6:30 AM on the morning of the 20th, more than 80 bandits in plain clothes suddenly looted several shops in Wanlai Shaoguo, outside the North Gate of the town of Majuqiao, and fled to Daxing County. The Daxing Security Corps has rushed to Dahongmen to intercept them. (Special dispatch, 21st)

(Tianjin) A large group of bandits has been discovered at the border of Tianjin and Jinghai counties, cutting off land and water transportation. On the 21st, a fierce battle broke out with the police and militia near the Duliu River. Many police and militia were injured. The Tianjin Garrison Security Headquarters has specially ordered two companies of the Yangliuqing garrison to rush to suppress them. (Special dispatch, 21st)

Japanese Kwantung Army Developing North China; Scheduled to Hold Second Meeting 22

(Beiping) The Japanese Kwantung Army previously convened a meeting in Changchun of military attachés stationed in China to discuss issues such as developing industries in North China and establishing a North China Cotton Association. Sakai, the chief of staff of the Japanese Garrison in Tianjin, Takahashi, the military attaché of the embassy, and Yiwo, the director of the Japanese Special Affairs Agency in Yuguan, who participated in the meeting, have all returned to their posts from Changchun. Regarding the development of North China's industries, Banxing, the deputy chief of staff of the Kwantung Army, Shimomura, the director of the First Section, Ishimoto, the director of the Second Section, Harada, the director of the Third Section, Kono, Yanagida, Shiozawa, and Yoshioka are continuing to be responsible for the matter. It is reported that the Japanese Kwantung Army is inviting Japanese capitalists to participate in the development of North China's industries and will also discuss everything with the South Manchuria Railway. A second discussion meeting is scheduled to be held in Dalian on the 17th of next month, and military attachés stationed in China will be invited to attend. (Special dispatch, 21st)

(Beiping) As the Hebei-Chahar issue has come to an end, the Japanese side will focus on economic cooperation and the development of North China's resources in its future work with China. When the Japanese Ministry of the Army makes a major reshuffle in August, it will pay special attention to this economic work. Based on this intention, the Ministry of the Army will also greatly reshuffle the military attachés stationed in North China in order to achieve practical results in handling affairs. After the reshuffle of the military attachés in North China, the Japanese side will start to carry out economic work in North China. (Special dispatch, 21st)

Achievements of the Guangdong Army in Suppressing Bandits 23

(Guangzhou) Today, the authorities released statistics on the Guangdong Army's suppression of bandits and communists. In the past two and a half years, there were a total of 402 engagements. The number of communists and bandits killed totaled 2,152, the number wounded totaled 11,006, the number captured totaled 1,353, the number who surrendered totaled 321, and the spoils of war included 1,770 rifles and 6,385 rounds of ammunition. In addition, 378 kidnapped individuals were rescued. (Reuters dispatch from the 21st)

Yin Rugeng Returns to Beiping from Tianjin 25

Lloyd George's New Deal Not Adopted - British Government States Reasons - Vague Content Obstructs Revival and Progress - Policy Toward Russia Ignores its Fundamental Development - Assisting China Should Consider Trade Relations 34

(London) The government today released a document of 16,000 words, detailing the reasons why the government refused to adopt the "New Deal" proposed by former Prime Minister Lloyd George. The government gave a considered response to each point in George's memorandum, pointing out that George's proposals were broad and mediocre, and stated that several points would hinder the national revival and progress that was already underway. It also stated that the general purpose of George's plan was the same as the government's, but the question was whether the methods he proposed were appropriate. Finance should not be an obstacle to any sound plan, but George's proposed prosperity loan of £250 million would greatly disrupt finances and have a tightening effect. George's estimates for reducing unemployment were purely speculative and had no real value. George's proposals for public works lacked details and budgets. To say that there are large-scale jobs that have not been discovered before that can accommodate a large number of unemployed people is just fantasy. George's agricultural proposals are the key to his plan, but this is a dangerous and uncertain attempt, which, even if feasible, would require paying the price of a non-natural increase in food prices, damaging British Empire trade and its relations, making export trade more difficult, and causing more unemployment among the industrial population. George's proposals for reorganizing industry are too vague and, if implemented, would not reduce unemployment. George's suggestions for developing overseas trade are disappointing and unhelpful. George's public works procedures did not have any new and good suggestions, and his proposals for a National Development Bureau and a special small cabinet were also unacceptable. George's suggestions regarding Soviet Russia seem to ignore the fundamental development of Soviet Russia. If George's proposals regarding China were implemented, China's exports to the UK would be reduced by more than one-third. As for the issue of assisting China, the British government often consults with other relevant countries and pays attention to it. Therefore, Britain sent Sir Ross to China to investigate its economic situation. British trade with China can be expected to expand, but George's belief that there is no limit to this expansion can be said to be ignoring all the facts today. The government's document concludes that the work that the government has already done and plans to do can at least prove to be better than George's proposals. (Reuters dispatch from the 21st)

(New York) In the past 24 hours, a heat wave ravaged the eastern half of the United States, causing thirty-five deaths. The temperature in Chicago yesterday reached 95 degrees, and seven people died from heatstroke. Nine people died in New England, mostly from electrocution. Today, the temperature in South Bend, Indiana reached 101 degrees in the shade. (Reuters dispatch, 20th)

(New York) New York today has strong winds and heavy rain, and many streets are flooded. Therefore, weekend sports such as baseball games have been suspended. (Reuters dispatch, 20th)

Large Batch of Silver Shipped from London to the US 52

(New York) The Harding President arrived here today with 4,887,000 ounces of silver. It is said that the Ministry of Finance purchased 50 million helmets of silver in London two weeks ago to prevent the collapse of silver prices. The first batch of this silver arrived today, and the second batch is 5.6 million ounces, which will be shipped from Washington. The ship departed on the 18th. (Kokumin dispatch, 20th)

Discovery of Ancient School Ruins in Syria 53

(Paris) French archaeologist Barro discovered the relics of a school from 3,000 years BC while excavating underground terraces near Abu Kamal, Syria. The area was a place rich in culture and history 2,000 years ago, and its cities were built by the Hittites. Ancient Egyptian historical records state that the Hittites were brilliant in scholarship, surpassing Babylon and Egypt. This excavation further confirms this. Barro discovered the relics of a heavenly palace at that time. The Hittite palace was several kilometers around, and the defense works were very strong. It was later captured and burned to the ground by the Babylonian king. However, even today, the ruins can still be found by excavating underground. In addition, the ruins of an ancient school were also discovered, with classrooms and podiums where the youth of the city were educated at that time. As for the architecture of the palace, its richness, beauty, and comfort were unmatched by the Middle Ages. The streets in the city were vertical and horizontal, intersecting at right angles. The houses had wide staircases, and there were cellars for storing food. The drainage system was also very complete. River water was poured into the city through ditches to provide for the residents. Most of the houses also had washrooms with ceramic bathtubs. (Havas dispatch, 21st)

If they do not seek to relocate as soon as possible, not only will the outside world misunderstand that the power plant is neglecting its duties, but also the lives and security of the citizens will be difficult to guarantee. Therefore, they specially requested the Construction Committee to send a letter to the Military Affairs Commission, ordering various military agencies in the city to relocate the lines that have been hung as soon as possible in order to clarify responsibilities and avoid future troubles. Public Announcement: Full Text of the Sino-French-Vietnamese Treaty and Agreed Protocol Attachments - After Five Years of Repeated Consultations, Agreement Finally Reached; Schedules A and B of the Protocol Signed This Year; Exchange of Notes in France the Day Before Yesterday; Implementation to be Announced Soon 74

The Sino-French Agreement on Relations Between Vietnam and the Border Provinces of China, previously signed on May 16, 1930, by the former Minister of Foreign Affairs, Wang Zhengting, and the former French Minister to China, Comte de Martel, could not be implemented because Schedules A and B of the first annex were not agreed upon, and the procedures were incomplete. After five years of repeated consultations, Schedules A and B were finally completely agreed upon recently, and other relevant annexes were also agreed upon at the same time. At 4:00 PM on May 4th of this year, Acting Foreign Minister Wang and French Minister to China, Wilden, at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, formally signed the "Protocol on the Establishment of Schedules A and B," and exchanged notes on other annexes simultaneously. After the case was completely resolved, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs immediately submitted the treaty text to the Executive Yuan for transfer to the Legislative Yuan for review. At the same time, the French Minister also sent the documents to his home government. The treaty has been passed by the Legislative Yuan of our country and has been approved and recorded by the National Government. The French side has also passed it through its parliament. On May 20th, in Paris, the French capital, Xiao Jirong, the plenipotentiary representative of our government for the exchange of the Sino-French-Vietnamese treaty and acting chargé d'affaires in France, signed the Process Verbal exchange of notes with the French side and agreed to simultaneously announce and implement it in Nanjing and Paris on the 22nd. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs specifically announced the full text of the "Sino-French Agreement on Relations Between Vietnam and the Border Provinces of China" and the "Protocol on the Establishment of Schedules A and B" and other annexes on the 21st, as follows:

(1) Sino-French Agreement on Relations Between Vietnam and the Border Provinces of China

The National Government of the Republic of China and the Government of the French Republic, desiring to strengthen the friendly relations existing between the two countries and to develop commercial relations between China and Vietnam, have decided to conclude a new treaty for this purpose and have appointed as their plenipotentiaries: The Chairman of the National Government of the Republic of China, His Excellency Wang Zhengting, the Minister of Foreign Affairs of the National Government of the Republic of China; The President of France, His Excellency Comte de Martel, the Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of the French Republic to China; Who, having communicated to each other their full powers, found in good and due form, have agreed upon the following articles: (Article 1) The Sino-French Land Trade Regulations concluded in Tianjin on March 22nd of the twelfth year of Guangxu (April 25, 1886), the Supplementary Commercial Treaty concluded in Beijing on May 6th of the thirteenth year of Guangxu (June 26, 1887), the exchange of notes regarding the Supplementary Commercial Treaty exchanged in Beijing on May 3rd of the thirteenth year of Guangxu (June 23, 1887), and the appendix to the Commercial Treaty concluded in Beijing on May 28th of the twenty-first year of Guangxu (June 20, 1895) are hereby abolished and their effect terminated. The provisions contained in Articles 4, 5, and 6 of the Sino-French New Treaty concluded in Tianjin on April 27th of the eleventh year of Guangxu (June 9, 1885) are also hereby abolished. (Article 2) Longzhou City in Guangxi Province, Simao City, Hekou City, and Mengzi City in Yunnan Province shall continue to serve as land border trade locations between China and Vietnam. (Article 3) The Chinese government may station consuls in Hanoi or Haiphong and Saigon in Vietnam. The French government may continue to station consuls in the locations listed in the preceding article. The heads of consulates, vice-consulates, and acting consular officers, as well as other consular staff, shall be nationals of the sending country and shall not engage in industrial or commercial activities. (Article 4) Chinese citizens traveling to Vietnam and French citizens of Vietnam traveling to China must hold passports issued by their respective competent authorities. These passports shall be visaed by the consular office of the country of destination or other officials designated by the country of destination to visa passports. Regarding (1) the passport system, (2) the visa system for inland travel permits and exit permits, and (3) all required procedures for Chinese citizens entering and leaving Vietnam and French citizens of Vietnam entering and leaving the three provinces of Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong, including procedures for proving identity, the two contracting parties agree to grant each other most-favored-nation treatment in accordance with their respective laws and regulations. The system of issuing temporary or permanent passes to residents of the two border areas who need to reside temporarily or frequently travel within each other's neighboring border areas for work or business purposes shall remain unchanged. (Article 5) Chinese citizens in Vietnam and French citizens in the above-mentioned Chinese locations shall enjoy the right to reside, travel, and engage in industrial and commercial activities. The treatment afforded to such citizens in the exercise of these rights in accordance with the current regulations and laws of Vietnam or China shall not be less favorable than that enjoyed by the citizens of any other country. The taxes or other levies paid by Chinese citizens in Vietnam and French citizens in the above-mentioned Chinese locations shall not be different from or higher than those paid by citizens of the most-favored nation. (Article 6) Chinese goods exported from any Chinese port, passing through Tonkin, and directly transported to the three provinces of Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong, or holding direct bills of lading, shall enjoy preferential treatment. The transit tax in the general tariff shall not apply. Such goods shall only pay a tax of one percent ad valorem. Chinese goods exported from the three provinces of Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong, passing through Tonkin, and transported to any specified location shall also enjoy preferential treatment. The transit tax in the general tariff shall not apply. All kinds of minerals, tin ingots, raw hides, and various goods currently or in the future listed in Schedule A of this treaty shall enjoy complete tax exemption. Other kinds of goods shall pay a tax of one percent ad valorem. All military supplies and military equipment transported by the Chinese government passing through Tonkin shall be exempt from any taxes. Vietnamese vessels, except warships and vessels carrying troops, military equipment, and military supplies, may travel via the Song Chi River and the Gao Ping River connecting Lang Son and Longzhou and Gao Ping, navigating between Lang Son and Gao Ping. These vessels and their cargo passing through the Chinese border shall be exempt from any taxes upon entry. (Article 7) The governments of the two contracting parties mutually agree not to establish in Vietnam and the three provinces of Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong import and export or transit prohibitions and restrictions that do not apply to other countries at the same time. However, with regard to national defense, civilian food, protection of artistic and scientific products, prevention of human and animal infectious diseases, protection of harvests, national patents, and maintenance of good morals, the two governments may establish import and export or transit prohibitions or restrictions on goods imported or exported to each other, but only to the extent that there is an absolute necessity and that they apply uniformly to all countries in similar circumstances. (Article 8) The Chinese government in the three provinces of Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong, and the French government in Vietnam shall not, on any pretext, levy on goods imported or exported by French or Chinese citizens higher or different consumption taxes or inland taxes than those that should be paid by their own citizens or the citizens of any other country. (Article 9) Chinese citizens who have committed serious or minor crimes in China, or who have been accused of committing serious or minor crimes, and who have fled into Vietnam, and French citizens who have committed serious or minor crimes in Vietnam, or who have been accused of committing serious or minor crimes, and who have fled into Chinese territory, shall, upon request by the relevant authorities to the other party's officials, after proof of the crime, be investigated, arrested, and extradited, unless extradition is not allowed in accordance with international practice. (Article 10) This treaty shall be valid for five years. Six months before the expiration of the term, either of the two contracting parties may notify the other party to modify or abolish this treaty. If neither party notifies the other party of modification or abolition within the above-mentioned period, this treaty shall continue to be effective, but after the expiration of the above-mentioned five-year term, either of the two contracting parties may notify the modification or abolition at any time. This treaty shall become invalid one year after the date of notification. This treaty and its attached documents shall be ratified as soon as possible. The ratification documents shall be exchanged in Paris. This treaty and its attached documents shall be announced in Vietnam and shall take effect simultaneously in Vietnam and the three provinces of Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong two months after the date of exchange of ratification documents. (Article 11) This treaty is written in Chinese and French. Both texts have been carefully reviewed. Therefore, the two plenipotentiaries have signed and sealed this treaty in duplicate to attest to its credibility. Done in Nanjing on May 16, 1930, the nineteenth year of the Republic of China, May 16, 1930. [Seal of Wang Zhengting] [Seal of Comte de Martel]

(2) Annex 1 (A) Note from French Minister Comte de Martel

Comte de Martel, Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of the French Republic to China, for the matter of a note. Regarding Article 8 of the Sino-French Treaty signed today, the Minister hereby declares to Your Excellency that, for the purpose of developing commercial relations between China and Vietnam, Chinese goods from Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong, as specified in Schedule A of this note, and Chinese goods specified in the schedule of the Sino-French Customs Treaty of December 22, 1928, transported to Vietnam, either directly or holding direct bills of lading, shall be taxed at the lowest rate.

The period during which the above-mentioned Chinese goods enjoy this tax rate shall be the period during which China does not increase the tax rate of the 1929 Chinese National Tariff for French and Vietnamese goods listed in Schedule B of this note, exported from Vietnam, or directly transported to the three provinces of Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong, or holding direct bills of lading. It is appropriate to inform Your Excellency Minister for reference. To the Note, to His Excellency Wang, Minister of Foreign Affairs of the National Government of the Republic of China, May 16, 1930.

(3) Annex 1 (B) Reply Note from Minister Wang

Wang, Minister of Foreign Affairs of the National Government of the Republic of China, for the matter of a reply note. Received Your Excellency Minister's note today, "Regarding Article 8 of the Sino-French Treaty signed today, the Minister hereby declares to Your Excellency that, for the purpose of developing commercial relations between China and Vietnam, Chinese goods from Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong, as specified in Schedule A of this note, and Chinese goods specified in the schedule of the Sino-French Customs Treaty of December 22, 1928, transported to Vietnam, either directly

Page 9

transported, or holding direct bills of lading, shall be taxed at the lowest rate. "The period during which the above-mentioned Chinese goods enjoy this tax rate shall be the period during which China does not increase the tax rate of the 1929 Chinese National Tariff for French and Vietnamese goods listed in Schedule B of this note, exported from Vietnam, or directly transported to the three provinces of Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong, or holding direct bills of lading," etc. The Minister completely agrees with Your Excellency Minister on this matter. It is appropriate to reply to Your Excellency Minister for reference. To the Note, to His Excellency Comte de Martel, Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of the French Republic to China, May 16, 1930, the nineteenth year of the Republic of China.

It is appropriate to request Your Excellency Minister for reference. (10) Note from Minister Wang

Wang, Minister of Foreign Affairs of the National Government of the Republic of China, for the matter of a note. Regarding the Sino-French Yunnan-Vietnam Railway Contract concluded on October 29, 1903, the Police Regulations concluded on March 15, 1910, and the Military Transportation Regulations supplementing the Police Regulations concluded on September 7, 1914, April 7, 1915, and June 18, 1925, the Minister hereby proposes to Your Excellency Minister that certain provisions of these regulations and contracts be appropriately amended after agreement by the relevant parties. This is for the convenience of the implementation of these regulations and contracts, and the validity of these regulations and contracts is not a matter for discussion. The Minister therefore proposes that the governments of our two countries each send a representative to begin discussions on this issue within three months after the implementation of the Sino-French Agreement on Relations Between Vietnam and the Border Provinces of China. The draft agreement negotiated by the representatives of both parties shall be submitted to the governments of our two countries for approval before it becomes effective. It is appropriate to request Your Excellency Minister for reference. To the Note, to His Excellency Comte de Martel, Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of the French Republic to China, May 16, 1930, the nineteenth year of the Republic of China.

Comte de Martel, Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of the French Republic to China, for the matter of a reply note. Received Your Excellency Minister's note today, "Regarding the various treaties, regulations, and contracts that stipulate the current system of wired and wireless telecommunications between Vietnam and the three border provinces of China, the Minister hereby proposes to Your Excellency Minister that certain provisions of these treaties, regulations, and contracts be appropriately amended after agreement by the relevant parties. This is for the modification of details only, for the purpose of facilitating the implementation of the above-mentioned documents, and the validity of the above-mentioned documents is not a matter for discussion. "The Minister therefore proposes that the governments of our two countries each send a representative to begin discussions on this issue within three months after the implementation of the Sino-French Agreement on Relations Between Vietnam and the Border Provinces of China. The draft agreement negotiated by the representatives of both parties shall be submitted to the governments of our two countries for approval before it becomes effective," etc. The Minister expresses his agreement to all the points mentioned in the note. It is appropriate to reply to Your Excellency Minister for reference. To the Note, to His Excellency Wang, Minister of Foreign Affairs of the National Government of the Republic of China, May 16, 1930.

(16) Protocol on the Establishment of Schedules A and B

Protocol: In accordance with the provisions contained in the following exchanges of notes: (1) The exchange of notes between the Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Republic of China and the Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of France to China attached to the Sino-French Agreement on Relations Between Vietnam and the Border Provinces of China of May 16, 1930, on the same day; (2) The exchange of notes between the Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Republic of China and the Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of France to China on September 2 and September 5, 1933, regarding the taxation of imported Vietnamese white coal; (3) The exchange of notes between the Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Republic of China and the Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of France to China on May 4, 1935, regarding the replacement of the 1929 tariff with the current Chinese National Tariff for the first five items in Schedule B, Schedules A and B are established as follows:

Schedule A

Part 1: The following Chinese goods from Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong shall enjoy the lowest tax rate when imported into French Vietnam, if directly transported or holding direct bills of lading:

Part 9: Sheep,

Part 17, Part 1: Ham,

Numbers 21 and 22: Raw hides, tanned hides,

Part 25, Part 1: Pig bristles,

Number 33: Wax,

Part 61, Part 1: Musk,

Number 67: Cattle and sheep horns,

Part 77, Part 1: Chinese noodles,

Number 83: Yams,

Numbers 84 (A) and (B): Fresh fruits for the table,

Number 85: Dried fruits for the table,

Number 142 (2): Coarsely made, finely woven, peeled and rolled

Hemp, combed hemp,

Number 143: Hemp,

Numbers 175 and 175 (2): Marble,

Stone,

Part 222, Part 1: Lead ore, raw lead ingots, lead containing antimony or not containing antimony, ingots, strips,

Part 223, Part 1: Tin ingots, ingots, strips, pure or mixed with other metals,

Part 0381, Part 1 (5): Insecticides made from plants of the chrysanthemum family,

Part 299, Part 1: Chinese ink,

Part 316, Part 1: Medicines commonly used in Chinese and Vietnamese medicine,

Part 330, Part 1: Incense and incense powder,

Numbers 347 (A) and (B): Porcelain,

Part 379 and 380, Part 1: Raw silk,

Part 461, Part 1: Non-decorated machine-made paper or cardboard, and handmade paper or cardboard (excluding cigarette paper, graph paper, and articles made of paper or cardboard, and paper for printing newspapers or books), decorated paper or cardboard (excluding paper for printing newspapers or books),

Numbers 476 (A) and (B): Tanned leather,

Number 6412: Fans,

Part 644 (2), Part 1: Writing brushes,

Part 2: The following Chinese goods shall enjoy the lowest tax rate when imported into French Cochinchina, if directly transported or holding direct bills of lading:

Number 99: Pepper,

Number 100: Chili peppers,

Number 102: Cinnamon,

Number 104: Nutmeg with and without shells,

Number 106: Cloves,

Number 108: Tea,

Part 459, Part 1: Pure silk fabrics, pure silk items, pure silk crepe, pure silk nets, pure silk lace,

Schedule B

During the period in which the current Chinese National Tariff has not increased the tax rate for the following first five items, and the tax rate for the following last item stipulated in the note from the Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Republic of China to the French Minister on September 5, 1933, has not been changed, the Chinese goods listed in Schedule A shall enjoy the lowest tax rate when imported into French Vietnam. However, the above-mentioned following items, whether produced in France or French Vietnam, must be directly transported from Vietnam to Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong, or hold direct bills of lading when transported from Vietnam to Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong:

Numbers 346 to 348: Cardamom, amomum,

Number 353: Cinnamon,

Part 567, Part 1: Untanned hides (excluding goat hides, sheep hides, and wolf hides),

Number 601 (C): Wooden furniture,

Part 615, Part 1: Empty glass bottles,

Number 603 (A): Anthracite coal with a ratio of carbonaceous components to volatile components (combustion rate) of 5 or more,

This protocol is written in Chinese and French, and both texts have been carefully reviewed. Done in Nanjing on May 4, 1935, the twenty-fourth year of the Republic of China, May 4, 1935. [Seal of Wang Zhaoming] [Seal of Wilden]

(17) Statement

The three provinces of Yunnan, Guangxi, and Guangdong, or restrict the quantity of their import. This statement shall be valid for two years from the date of implementation of the treaty of May 16, 1930, and may be abolished after the expiration of the term, provided that notice is given three months in advance. (18) Note from French Minister Wilden

Wilden, Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of the French Republic to China, for the matter of a note. The Chinese government has recently increased the tax rate for all imported foreign coal, including Vietnamese white coal. The Minister hereby informs Your Excellency Minister that, during our recent discussions, it was agreed to include Vietnamese white coal (for which we have reached a consensus on the definition) in Schedule B of the treaty of May 16, 1930. The tax rate levied on the import of this item shall not be higher than the tax rate of the 1932 tariff, which is 0.89 gold units per ton. Your Excellency Minister is aware that increasing the tax rate of 1932 would seriously hinder the progress of the current negotiations, and the two schedules A and B may not be able to obtain the agreement desired by the governments of our two countries. For this reason, please confirm to the Minister that, as soon as the agreement on the two schedules is signed and the treaty is implemented, the import tax levied on white coal, that is, anthracite coal with a ratio of carbonaceous components to volatile components (combustion rate) of 5 or more, shall not be higher than 0.89 gold units per ton. It is appropriate to request Your Excellency Minister for reference. To the Note, to His Excellency Wang, Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Republic of China, September 2, 1933.

(19) Reply Note from Acting Minister Wang

Wang, Acting Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Republic of China, for the matter of a reply note. Regarding the import tax on white coal, Your Excellency Minister's note of September 2, 1933, has been read carefully. The Minister hereby replies to Your Excellency Minister that, as soon as the agreement on the two schedules currently under negotiation is signed and the treaty is implemented, the import tax levied on white coal, that is, anthracite coal with a ratio of carbonaceous components to volatile components (combustion rate) of 5 or more, shall not be higher than 0.89 gold units per ton. It is appropriate to reply to Your Excellency Minister for reference. To the Note, to His Excellency Wilden, Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of the French Republic to China, September 5, 1933, the twenty-second year of the Republic of China.

Water Conservancy Personnel in Jinan Discuss Water Management Measures, Upper Yellow River in Shanzhou Reports Another Rise in Water Level 78

Jinan Correspondence: The Yellow River in Shandong Province, since the breach at Dongzhuang and Linpuji in the upper reaches, has been overflowing for ten days. The Yellow River is flowing horizontally, and its momentum is extremely fierce. Dozens of counties, including Zoucheng, Juye, Jiaxiang, and Jining, have been flooded. Recently, due to heavy rainfall, all rivers have risen, and the floodwaters have entered Nanyang Lake, with signs of further southward movement. Dingtao and Chengwu have already seen water, and Jinxiang and Yutai will also inevitably be affected. With the situation in southern Shandong being so dire, northern Jiangsu is even more at risk. Therefore, Li Yi, Chairman of the Yellow River Water Conservancy Commission, Zhang Hanying, Secretary-General, Puteli, a water conservancy expert from the League of Nations and advisor to the National Economic Commission, and Wan Lifu, an engineer from the Central Hydraulic Engineering Experiment Institute, have all come to Jinan together. They were originally scheduled to inspect the breach on the 20th and inspect the Jindi embankment, but this was canceled due to rain. It was rescheduled to depart on the 21st to the breaches between Juancheng, Dong, and Lin. The breaches at numbers one, two, three, and four have gradually silted up, and the amount of water passing through them is very small. The water outflow from numbers five and six accounts for nearly 70-80% of the main river. Therefore, the most urgent task is to close the breaches and divert the floodwaters. Li, Zhang, Puteli, and others, along with Kong Lingrong, Director of the Shandong Canal Engineering Bureau, Song Wentian, a technician from the Construction Department, and Pan Jianfen, Chief of the Engineering Section of the River Affairs Bureau, held discussions. They all believed that since the river water is currently at its peak and the breach closure project cannot be started yet, the disaster area will inevitably expand daily if a solution to the flood discharge problem is not sought quickly. Therefore, it is proposed to divert the Yellow River into two streams. One stream will move north into Dongping Lake and return to the main river through the canal, and the other stream will move south into Weishan Lake and into the Liutang River. However, due to the need for the water entering Dongping Lake to pass through the dikes at the border of Dongping and Shouzhang, there are still many difficulties. There are also difficulties with the stream entering Liutang, so a decision could not be made. After the meeting adjourned at 10:00 a.m., they went to the Construction Department and the River Affairs Bureau to investigate the terrain of the disaster area and nearby rivers and lakes in detail. They scheduled another meeting at 8:00 p.m. to discuss further.

The water level and flow rate of the Yellow River this year are different from previous years. Therefore, as soon as a dangerous situation was reported, immediate blocking was attempted. As a result, the dikes collapsed and flooded unimpeded. On the 19th, Zhang Lianjia, Director of the Shandong River Affairs Bureau, reported to Han Fuqu, Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, that Shanzhou in the upper reaches had reported another rise in water level, reaching 293.44 meters, with a flow rate of 4,500 cubic meters per second. From the 15th to the 18th, the flow rate of the Yellow River's main and tributaries increased sharply, reaching 9,300 cubic meters per second. The floodwaters are vast and will soon reach Shandong. In addition to reporting to the Provincial Government, Zhang also issued a general order to all sections of the river to strengthen flood prevention. Therefore, there are still many hidden worries ahead. (20th)

Songjiang 79

Radio Bureau Handles Radio Registration

Recently, with the advancement of science, radios have become popular everywhere. According to regulations, users should apply for registration, but many users are unaware of the laws and regulations and have not applied. Since the Ministry sent personnel to Songjiang last month to investigate transmitters, they have realized the need to register radios and have applied to the Songjiang Telegraph Bureau. The bureau has submitted the matter to the Ministry of Communications and has been issued registration forms, allowing radio users to fill out and register. No handling fees will be charged within two weeks. Those who fail to register after the deadline will be fined according to regulations.

Post Office Investigates Private Transportation of Letters

Local people's bureaus are not allowed to transport letters. The Ministry of Communications has previously ordered local post offices to investigate in order to avoid hindering state-run operations. Although the people's bureaus jointly petitioned, their request was not approved. Recently, Yan Xiaolu, Director of the Zhangyan Post Office, learned that Wang Xieyuan Store in Tinglin and others were suspected of privately transporting letters. After investigation, two pieces of evidence were found. The store owner, Gu Binfu, was bedridden due to illness and was ordered by the Public Security First Branch to post bail. The bail documents were sent to the local court for investigation.

Wuxi 80

Repercussions of Police Arbitrarily Arresting Civilians

At about 10 p.m. on the 19th of this month, a sudden violent wind and rain struck the city. All the city's electric lights suddenly went out. Zhu Jiannan, a shop assistant at Qingxin Hat and Shoe Store under the North Suspension Bridge, used a flashlight to illuminate and ordered apprentices to go out and buy candles. Due to carelessness, the light shone on the face of Zhao Lunshan, a policeman at the Fifth Branch of the Public Security Bureau. The policeman cursed without asking the reason, and a dispute arose. Somehow, the policeman was beaten and immediately returned to the bureau to report. The bureau sent police officers to detain Zhu Jiannan, Zhu Shankang, Cai Jinliang, and others. They were beaten with fists and tied with ropes on the way. The next day, they were transferred to the County Public Security Bureau. Because it was Sunday, the case was scheduled to be transferred to the court for trial today. However, local merchants, because the police arbitrarily arrested merchants that night and beat and tied them, causing merchants to lose face, specifically requested the County Chamber of Commerce from various trade guilds to forward a letter to the County Government, ordering the Public Security Bureau to restrain its subordinates and prevent similar actions from happening again in the future in order to maintain the business community. The Da'an Township Office also sent a letter to the First District Office to forward to the county for handling in order to appease merchants and civilians.

Another Impersonator Arrested

The Sixth Company of the Second Battalion of the Second Regiment of the Garrison in Wuxi previously cracked a case involving Wu Yushan, Zhang Ling, Jiang Jun, and others impersonating military officers. They were sent to the Capital Garrison Command and the Suzhou Battalion Headquarters for interrogation. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. Now, it is learned that Zhong Ruilin, the company commander of the company, recently discovered that Wang Xiaoxian (nicknamed Wang Datou), from Anhui, was also impersonating the leader of the Seventh Group of the Fifth Recruiting Office of the Military Commission. He established a recruiting office in the Sanyi Temple in Chong'an Temple, luring and threatening the ignorant to join the army, extorting money under various pretexts, and colluding with Wu Yushan. The company sent troops to arrest Wang, together with the Supervision Office of the Public Security Bureau, on the morning of the previous day. Many pieces of evidence were seized and temporarily detained in the company. Yesterday, they were sent to the Second Battalion Headquarters in Suzhou for interrogation.

Yangzhou 81

Establishing Canal Flood Prevention Office

Regarding the issue of Yellow River water invading the canal, the Jiangbei Canal Engineering Bureau reported that the situation was as calm as before. The bureau recently received an instruction from the Provincial Government, jointly signed by the Civil, Finance, and Construction Departments, ordering it to establish the Jiangbei Canal Area Flood Prevention Office in Huaiyin. It is scheduled to start operations on the 22nd. All summer flood prevention and rescue work and defense matters in the Huaipi, Gaobao, and Jiangdu sections of this year, as well as the flood prevention and inspection responsibilities in Weishan Lake and Hongze Lake, are under the full command of the office. The embankment repairs in the Weishan Lake, Hongze Lake, Central Canal, and Li Canal areas are still the responsibility of the bureau.

Nantong 82

Two Murderers Sentenced to Death

Wei Cai, a widow from Yudong, resented her uncle, Wei Dade, for exposing her adultery. She spent 400 yuan to buy off He Derong and Jiang Sanlaohu, local gangsters, to break into Wei Dade's house at night and kill Wei and his wife and their second son, Wei Shifang. After the case was discovered, Wei Cai was sent to the court and sentenced to death. Recently, He Derong and Jiang Sanlaohu were also arrested. On the 20th, the criminal court concluded the trial and sentenced them all to death.

Conscription for River Dredging Completed

Nantong County has implemented conscription for dredging large and small rivers. All the projects have now been completed. Wang Zisheng, a member of the Construction Department, inspected and accepted the projects. The total cost of the projects was over 80,000 yuan. In addition to the 10,000 yuan each allocated by the provincial and county treasuries, the rest was raised locally.

Hangzhou 83

Security Office Executes Two Notorious Bandits by Firing Squad

The Zhejiang Provincial Security Office received four notorious bandits, Pan Yanlin, Zhang Changfa, Fang Buqing, and Xu Donglin, who were sent by the Jiande County Government. After interrogation, it was found that Pan and Zhang had committed multiple robberies, murders, kidnappings, and extortions in the county. Witnesses also testified against them. Except for Fang and Xu, who were transferred to the court for handling due to their lesser involvement, Pan and Zhang were taken from the military prison at 9:00 a.m. yesterday (the 21st), identified, and escorted to the execution ground outside Qingtai Gate for execution by firing squad.

Foil Monopoly to be Implemented Next Month

The Zhejiang Finance Department issued a notice regarding the monopoly of foil in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, ordering foil merchants to jointly organize a Foil Monopoly Company. The founding meeting was held in Shaoxing on the previous day and reported to the Provincial Government for record. It was also reported to the Ministry of Industry for registration. The monopoly will begin in August. In order to provide relief to workers in the foil industry, the Finance Department also stipulated that the company should set aside a certain percentage of its annual profits to be used for relief funds. The government's tax revenue can increase by 200,000 to 300,000 yuan per year.

Xiaoxian County 84

Land Survey Completed and Reported to the Province

Yao Xuehuai, the magistrate of Xiaoxian County, and Bao Fu, the chief accountant, sent a telegram to the Provincial Government and the Finance Department reporting the completion of the land survey. The following is an excerpt from the original report from the county: "The land survey in this county began in early April. Although there were difficulties in the process, it was completed by July 10. The compilation, survey, review, re-examination, and statistics have been completed in order. Preliminary statistics show that the total area of the county is 2,724,290 mu, 9 fen, 4 li, and 6 hao. Excluding 261,100 mu of mountains and hills, 22,792 mu and 5 li and 5 hao of rivers, 5,484 mu, 6 fen, 3 li, and 1 hao of highways, 27 mu, 2 fen, and 5 li of city walls, and 1,328 mu, 5 fen, and 4 li and 5 hao of railways, the area of cultivated land is 2,433,758 mu, 4 fen, and 3 li and 5 hao. Compared with the 1,332,081 mu, 3 fen, 6 li, 5 hao, and 3 si of land originally taxed in previous years, there is an excess of 1,101,477 mu, 6 li, 9 hao, and 7 si. We are currently rushing to create household registers and plot maps, investigating land beyond boundaries, and organizing a general surveying team to conduct a comprehensive survey in the townships to ensure that no inch is hidden." It is said that the Provincial Government has issued an order to commend the county and will issue separate awards after the entire project is completed.

Mingguang 85

Giant Snake Discovered in Xuyi's Liantang

A giant python was discovered in Liantang Fort, Xuyi County. According to eyewitnesses, its head was as big as a dou, and its body was over a zhang long, with bluish-black markings. It has been appearing in Wanjia Lake, Beishan, and Luchaigou in recent days. Nearby residents are on alert and have hired many snake catchers, but they all say that the snake is too large and they dare not take action.

Letter 86

To the Editor, We recently read the news about the Public Security Bureau of Haimen County interrogating Baozhang merchants in the "Local Correspondence" column of your newspaper on July 9. The current Inspector General of our bureau, Sun Junmou, was the director of the Sanyangzhen Public Security Sub-bureau. Because the gambling atmosphere in the town was rampant and the worst in the county, gamblers and hooligans ran rampant. Our bureau secretly ordered a deadline for suppression, and the law should be prohibited, and no leniency should be given. As for the fines for gambling, there are always joint receipts, which are reported to the county government by the bureau on a monthly basis. The drama in your publication that the job was lost because the receipts were not given for catching gambling is completely untrue. He Shudong, the former Inspector General of our bureau, resigned, and the officer was specially transferred to take over. It is also a very common thing in official affairs. Yin Xinbo, the acting director of the sub-bureau, was also manipulated by Zhou and other powerful gamblers in the town because of the strict prohibition of gambling and prostitution, and the market was closed. The handling beyond the rules and stimulating merchants and people to close the market as described in your publication is also untrue. Regarding the arrest of Gu Wugao, Li Bu'ao, Feng Furong, Ding Cailang, Shen Qinhe, etc., (Li Bu'ao is on the run and has not been captured) it is a major suspicion that they were arrested and investigated by the Nantong Commissioner's Office under a secret order. The injuries caused by interrogation are just that Gu and Ding were fined for gambling before, and they made false accusations to vent their personal anger. Otherwise, why have we not heard of any interrogation injuries to Feng and Shen, who were arrested in the same case at the same time? The Shishan Daily in our county has already confirmed it and does not need to be explained. Our bureau enforces the law strictly, impartially, and selflessly. It is inevitable that the villains hate it. Those who openly obstruct official duties and destroy reputation have violated the criminal law. Your publication is one of the leading newspapers in the country, and its records are known to be detailed and accurate. We should ask you to correct it immediately to match the facts, to fulfill the public interest. To the Shenbao Newspaper Office Outlying Area Communications Editorial Department, Director Dai Hongtao.

City Federation of Associations Plans to Organize Propaganda Team for Urgent Relief to Flood-Stricken Provinces; Establishment of 38 Sub-Teams; Scheduled Meeting to Discuss Progress 88

Dagon News: The Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Federation of Associations, in light of the massive floods affecting the provinces of Shandong, Anhui, Henan, Hubei, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Hunan, and Jiangxi, covering an area of over one million square li and affecting over thirty million compatriots, with cries of despair heard everywhere and a tragic disaster situation, resolved at its fourth congress to contact various public organizations in the city to launch an urgent relief association for the flood-stricken provinces. The federation will first establish a flood relief appeal team to conduct propaganda to promote the will of the citizens of the city and to encourage generous donations to save the disaster victims. In light of the disaster telegrams from various provinces arriving like snowflakes, there is no time to delay disaster relief. The propaganda department of the federation has scheduled a meeting of propaganda members from various district sub-associations for 2 p.m. this Friday to discuss progress. It has also been decided that each district sub-association will establish a team, totaling 38 teams, with each team consisting of six to ten propaganda members. They will be assigned to various districts to conduct propaganda to promote citizen awareness and rescue the disaster victims.

Mu Ouchu Requests Rectification: Letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Seeking Justice 92

Mu Ouchu's letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce reads: Respected Sirs, I am writing concerning recent reports in the local evening paper of the 9th of this month and the daily newspaper of the 10th, regarding the case of *New Life Weekly* tried by the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court, and the publication of the court's verdict in various newspapers on the 16th. The verdict sentenced Du Chongyuan, the editor and publisher of the publication, to one year and two months of imprisonment, and announced in court on the 9th that no appeal would be permitted, with immediate detention and execution. I, Xiangyue, am not well-versed in the law, but upon investigation of the old and new penal codes, I find discrepancies with the court's pronouncements. I respectfully present my humble opinions as follows:

(1) The declaration "no appeal permitted" is illegal. According to Article 367 of the Criminal Procedure Law, "Anyone who disagrees with the second instance or first instance judgment of the High Court and appeals shall appeal to the Supreme Court." Furthermore, "The Supreme Court's trial of appeals against the first instance judgment of the High Court also applies the third instance procedure." Article 368 states, "Cases involving crimes listed in Article 61 of the Criminal Law, which have been judged in the second instance, may not be appealed to the Third Instance Court," explicitly stating "after the second instance," not "after the High Court." In this case, only the first instance of the High Court has been conducted. How can the court force the defendant to accept the verdict? The declaration of "no appeal permitted" clearly deprives the defendant of the right to appeal, violating the explicit text of the law.

(2) Failure to adopt a lighter penal code intentionally aggravates the harm to the actor. The author of the article "Idle Talk about the Emperor" is Yi Shui, who should bear the responsibility for the imprisonment. Du is the editor and publisher. On the day the article was published, Du was away in another city (as evidenced by various facts) and did not review the article. It was published due to the negligence of another editor of the publication. This cannot prove that Du was a joint actor. The circumstances are lighter, and should be punished with a fine of less than 1,000 yuan according to Article 325 of the old penal code and Article 310 of the new penal code. The purpose of a fine in the penal code is precisely for this reason. The court's abandonment of the lighter penalty that should have been applied and its decision on a heavier penalty that should not have been applied is, what else can it be, intentionally aggravating the harm to the actor?

(3) Not granting probation is inhumane. According to Article 74 of the New Criminal Law, "Anyone who has been sentenced to imprisonment, detention, or fines for a term of two years or less and who meets one of the following conditions, where it is deemed appropriate to temporarily suspend execution, may be granted probation for a period of two to five years, calculated from the date of final judgment: (1) has never been sentenced to imprisonment; (2) has previously been sentenced to imprisonment or a more severe punishment, and within five years after the completion of the sentence or pardon, has not been sentenced to imprisonment or a more severe punishment." Du is a self-respecting gentleman who meets both of the above conditions, and the author, Yi Shui, has not been arrested and brought to justice. It is entirely possible to "declare probation for two to five years." Moreover, Du has devoted himself to industry in recent years, sparing no effort, and is currently undertaking the important task of improving Jiangxi national porcelain. The law is ultimately rooted in human sentiment. The court's inhumane judgment of not granting "probation" is simply intolerable.

The above three points are not for Du Chongyuan alone to seek justice, but for the welfare of the three million citizens of Shanghai in the future, and I dare not remain silent. Recalling before 1927, our citizens suffered under the foreign-controlled Mixed Court. After much struggle and outcry, on January 1, 1927, we regained the Mixed Court and reorganized it into a provisional court. Furthermore, on April 1, 1930, we achieved the establishment of today's formal court. Unexpectedly, at the beginning of the implementation of the new penal code, a judgment depriving the right of appeal has occurred, intentionally depriving rights permitted by law. To tolerate this and not correct it would leave the property and lives of our three million citizens with no protection. If this is extended to the whole country, the depth of the future harm is unimaginable. Your esteemed association must be paying close attention to this case. My reason for not hesitating to state these points is merely to contribute to your association's research. If you would uphold justice and clearly indicate a method of rectification, the citizens would be greatly fortunate. Respectfully addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Mu Xiangyue, July 19, 1935.

Sino-Philippine Relations Grow Friendlier: Overseas Chinese Welcome to Develop Mindanao: Overseas Chinese Entry Fees Reduced by Three-Quarters; Chinese Chamber of Commerce Decides to Assist in Protecting Local Products 93

The New Voice News Agency reports that Sino-Philippine relations in the Far East have become more harmonious and friendly in recent years, thanks to frequent visits between officials and people of the two countries. Yesterday, the reporter learned from the Shanghai Overseas Chinese Association about the friendly relations between China and the Philippines, and the welcome extended by Filipinos to overseas Chinese to enter the Philippines and develop Mindanao. Details are recorded below:

Entry Fees Reduced to Five Pesos

Based on a special recommendation from the Governor-General to the Senate, Philippine Finance Minister Senator Quirino proposed to the Senate to reduce the immigration tax (i.e., entry fee) for overseas Chinese entering the Philippines from 20 pesos to 5 pesos. Mr. Quirino stated that China and the United States had recently agreed to reduce the visa fee for Chinese and American passports to 5 pesos per person, so the entry fee for overseas Chinese to the Philippines should also be reduced. He also said that the entry fee for Chinese coming to the Philippines was too expensive, and many tried their best to avoid it and move elsewhere.

Recruiting Chinese Laborers to Cultivate Mindanao

Philippine Chief of Staff General Basilio Valdes and Senator Mariano Cuenco recently visited Mindanao. General Manager of the Bureau of Non-Christian Tribes, Jose G. Generoso met with General Valdes. Cooperation to Assist Economic Revival

Overseas Chinese in the Philippines are pleased that the Philippine authorities have repeatedly expressed goodwill towards them, and they have decided to assist in protecting the national economy of the island. The Chinese Chamber of Commerce in Manila recently issued a notice stating: "The purpose of the Philippine National Economic Protection Association is purely to promote local products, reclaim rights and interests, and support the development of Philippine industry and commerce, consolidating the position of the national economy. The objectives are far-reaching. As it gradually expands in the future, the economic future of the Philippines will depend on it. Overseas Chinese doing business in this country, the advancement or decline of their business depends entirely on the strength or weakness of the Philippine national economic capacity. If we look at the situation in the Philippines a few years ago, when Philippine local products were thriving, all the large and small overseas Chinese merchants were full of vitality. As local product prices declined and production decreased in recent years, the overseas Chinese business also declined sharply. This is an obvious fact. It can be seen that the rise and fall of overseas Chinese business is closely related to the Philippine national economy. The association has recently received a letter from the Association expressing its sincere desire to cooperate with the overseas Chinese to jointly promote progress. Therefore, the association informs all overseas Chinese to provide practical cooperation and assistance."

He Fu, Liquidator of American United and Two Other Companies, Issues Statement: Poor Management of the Three Companies Created an Extremely Bad Situation 95

The *North-China Daily News* reports that Mr. He Fu, the liquidator of the American United Bank and two other companies, issued a formal statement on Saturday (July 20th), stating that the liquidation process was proving difficult. The current commercial situation in Shanghai and the rest of China was not an insurmountable obstacle. The difficulties were due to the internal situation of the three companies and the poor management over the years. Taking American United Bank as an example, some of the external debts listed as assets were loans to affiliated companies. Those in charge of the bank must have known long ago that they were worthless. In addition, there were many external loans listed as assets that should have been written off as bad debts years ago based on ordinary commercial knowledge. Many loans had no collateral, or the collateral was worthless paper. Attributing the failure of the three companies to a poor business environment or Roosevelt's silver purchase policy was merely an excuse. The instability of the three companies' internal situation had been apparent for years. In his opinion, even if the general commercial situation today was good, the three companies would still have been forced into liquidation. The liquidation process cannot be completed quickly because the three companies created the current state of affairs over many years. The liquidation work cannot be completed in a short period of time. He often heard that American United Bank was an American bank, but it was actually a bank established in Shanghai by an American. It had no connection with any American bank and did not comply with American banking laws. Thousands of people who deposited money in the bank must have thought it was an American bank. The Tianjin branch was smaller in scope and in better condition. Except for a loan of 1 million yuan to the American Carpet Company, the remaining debts were being collected. Since Mr. Rook took over the liquidation, he has remitted 96,000 yuan. Even if the debts owed to the Universal Savings Society could be repaid, they would be few. The company had a very large amount of deposits, so the loss to creditors was terrifying. The amount of money that several companies owed to the American United Bank was nearly 2 million yuan. This money was wasted on useless places in the Universal Savings Society and the American Eastern Banking Corporation. As for the American Eastern Banking Corporation, it was a problem. The amount that creditors could recover in the future would be very small, because the securities pledged by the company were often re-pledged to other banks and a certain company in New York, resulting in an extremely bad situation. Those who owed money to the American Eastern Banking Corporation, even if they were willing to pay, could not get their pledged securities back. Since these securities had been re-pledged to other banks, the liquidator could not recover the securities to be returned to the original owners, even if he wanted to collect the money. In other words, the American Eastern Banking Corporation had no cash available for the liquidator to withdraw securities from other banks and return them to the original owners in order to settle the outstanding debts. Accountant Fold and his assistant are currently auditing and announcing the account books of the three companies and the Universal Real Estate Company. The actual situation of the four companies will be announced in detail within two months. According to the investigation, the amount of money that American United Bank invested in various projects on the day of closing was approximately 11,100,200 yuan. Since the liquidation, only 355,655.20 yuan has been recovered. The figures for the bank's investment in various projects proved that the commercial situation in Shanghai and Roosevelt's silver policy had little impact on the three companies. The failure was mostly due to poor management policies. Before the liquidation, the monthly expenses of the three companies were approximately 31,850 yuan. Since the start of the liquidation work, some of the employees of the three companies must be retained to assist in the process. The current monthly expenses are 9,709 yuan, including the salaries of Mr. Fold and his assistant. This is the minimum that can be saved. However, the remuneration of the liquidator's lawyer, Mr. Schuyler, and the liquidator himself will be determined by Chief Judge Hilemik of the American Court after the liquidation work is completed.

New Theory of Dada: Trial Run in Wusong Yesterday, Reception for Visitors; Perfect Equipment, Management System Eliminates Bad Habits; Maiden Voyage Tonight, Non-Commercial Traffic on Tongyang Line 96

The Dada Shipping Company's new ship, Dada, had a trial run to and from Wusong at 1:00 p.m. yesterday and will host visitors this morning. The maiden voyage will be on the Tongyang line tonight, without carrying passengers or cargo. It is scheduled to officially open on the 26th. The previously leased Datong ship will be taken out of service. Details are recorded below.

Trial Run Ceremony

After the Dada new ship was completed by the Great China Shipbuilding & Engineering Company, it sailed to Dada Wharf No. 5 on the 16th Pier and docked. The trial run ceremony was held at 1:00 p.m. yesterday. All the guest firms, colleagues, and journalists were invited to visit the ship. A temporary decorative archway was built at Wharf No. 5. More than 1,000 people, including Wang Bofen, Chen Shuntong, Li Yunliang, Penghu, Chen Yisheng, etc., attended. The company's managers Ma Shuren, Zhao Hansheng, Li Yunhou, Wu Bangsheng, General Manager Zhang Xiaoruo, Manager Yang Guanbei, and Shipping Section Chief Yang Qingbang, etc., welcomed the guests and provided tea and refreshments. Commemorative fans for the maiden voyage were distributed. The trial run started at 1:30 p.m. and arrived outside the Wusong estuary at 3:00 p.m. It then sailed back and docked at Wharf No. 5 at 4:30 p.m. The result of the trial run was very good.

Welcome Speech

General Manager Zhang Xiaoruo delivered a welcome speech on the ship, saying: "In this autumn of economic panic and the decline of all industries, our company still spared no expense to build a new ship at a huge cost of 500,000 yuan. Can the critics say that we do not understand the situation and that it is not in line with economic principles? But they do not know the company's hard work for transportation and its purpose of serving society, which does not slacken due to the adverse environment. Moreover, the business of the recent era is like a boat sailing against the current. If it does not have special strengths, it will inevitably fail. Our company is in this special environment. Although we want to work hard within the scope of our own business to seek development, external threats are constantly increasing and never ending, making it difficult to fully develop our strengths. It is difficult to improve and difficult to maintain the status quo. There is nothing more heartbreaking than this. However, our company will never be discouraged by this. With the spirit of struggling through hardships and fulfilling our most faithful responsibilities, we will make further contributions to the public and transportation. We resolutely decided to build this new ship to align the ranks of our company's ships. Today, the great success is announced. We are honored to have Chinese and foreign guests to guide us. It is a great occasion. In addition to our company's gratitude, we will briefly describe the structure, equipment, and management of the new ship Dada below, and humbly seek guidance.

Complete Equipment

The structure and machinery of the ship have already been reported in the newspapers, so I will omit the details. As for the equipment, it is very complete. (1) The special-class rooms and dining rooms are all decorated in Western style, painted with gold and colorful, magnificent and resplendent. The berths are Simmons flat steel beds, which are extremely comfortable. The sofas are all made of thick velvet, and hot and cold running water, dressing tables, coffee tables, bed blankets, and velvet bedding are all suitably matched. (2) The light and air in all levels of cabins are very sufficient. There are mosquito nets in summer and radiators in winter. The special-class rooms even have skylights with glass covers. (3) There are several men's and women's rooms on the upper, middle, and lower levels. The locations are appropriate and the boundaries are different, so they are never mixed. Flush toilets are used. (4) Hot water vapor pipes are installed in the front and rear cargo holds. In the event of a fire, the mechanism can be opened and hot steam will be sprayed from the pipes. Watchmen are hired to patrol to prevent accidents. Regarding life-saving equipment, there are four lifeboats and more than 1,000 life jackets, all made of high-quality materials. (5) To prevent pirate robberies, movable iron grilles are placed in the driving cabin and at the key points of each cabin, which can be closed immediately. The above equipment is the only one on the inner harbor route.

Management System

(1) The business management of this ship implements the abolition of the comprador system. One clerk is set up to manage passenger meals, teahouse reception, and the hygiene of the entire ship. A separate cargo handling department is set up to manage the loading and unloading of goods along the way and management matters. With this method, the head office can directly exercise its powers on each ship, which can thoroughly reform the business. (2) The teahouse staff of this ship are selected from the original teahouse staff of each ship and are strictly trained. They are attentive and quick in their work. They wear uniforms when serving on the ship to show neatness and magnificence. They are absolutely allowed to be rewarded by the guests for the liquor, and are never allowed to ask for a penny. (3) All levels of cabins are numbered in accordance with the railway method. Passengers can book seats by telephone and purchase tickets and board the ship at the company's ticket office on the pier before departure. They can board the ship according to the seat number. There is no bad habit of teahouse staff monopolizing berths like on the Yangtze River steamers. (4) Top-class chefs are hired for food, striving for cleanliness and deliciousness. The drinking water is filtered with fine sand leaks, which is more beneficial to hygiene than using alum to precipitate the water.

Reception for Visitors

Starting at 9:00 a.m. today, tea and refreshments will be prepared on the ship to welcome Wu Tiecheng, the mayor of Shanghai, the heads of various bureaus under his command, the heads of security departments, and industry leaders Chen Guangfu, Qin Runqing, Liu Hongsheng, Yu Zuoting, Lin Kanghou, Zheng Zenan, Wang Yansong, Yu Qiaqing, and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and other organizations. Chairman Du Yuesheng will personally host the event. The ship will dock at Wharf No. 5 on the 16th Pier. As for the crew, Zhang Shusheng has been appointed as the captain, Wu Shicai as the first mate, Zhu Lianqing as the second mate, Shen Liansheng as the chief engineer, Liu Yexing as the first engineer, Wang Shaofu as the second engineer, Zhou Shengdong as the third engineer, Bao Jinzhang as the cargo handler, and Jin Maoliang as the clerk. The comprador system will be abolished, a clerk will be set up, and a total of 34 teahouse staff will be hired. The company will pay them wages and prohibit them from extorting tips. The ship has six special-class cabins, each for two people, sixteen second-class cabins, each for two people, and 125 general-class seats, accommodating a total of 1,350 passengers.

Sailing to Tongyang

The ship is scheduled to make its maiden voyage from Shanghai to the Tongyang line at 12:00 tonight, temporarily without loading cargo or passengers. Manager Yang Guanbei, Shipping Section Chief Yang Qingbang, etc., will all travel with the ship. It will pass through Yaogang and Rengang without stopping. It is scheduled to arrive at Tianshenggang at 8:00 a.m. tomorrow, welcoming the Tongzhou community to board the ship for a visit. It will sail again that night, passing through Xinsheng, Zhanghuang, Xingang, Jiangyin, Liuxu, Dongxin, and Tianxingqiao without stopping. It is scheduled to arrive at the port of entry at 4:00 a.m. on the 24th. After stopping, it will sail again, passing through Sanjiangying and Bajiangkou without stopping. It is scheduled to arrive at Huojiaqiao at 9:00 a.m. on the same day and will begin loading cargo and passengers. It will depart from Huojiaqiao at 1:00 p.m. that afternoon and is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 12:00 p.m. on the 25th.

Passenger Ticket Prices

It has been decided that the ship will officially start carrying cargo and passengers from Shanghai to the Tongyang line at 12:00 p.m. on the 26th, stopping at all ports of entry. The ship will depart from Shanghai every Monday and Friday. As for the passenger ticket prices, (1) special-class cabin is 4 yuan per person, (2) special-class dining room is 1.50 yuan per person, (3) first-class cabin is 1.50 yuan per person, (4) second-floor dining room is 1 yuan per person, (5) second-floor dining room cabin is 1 yuan per person, (6) second-class cabin is 75 cents per person, (7) general-class cabin is 50 cents per person. The above are all the ticket prices from Shanghai to Tongzhou. The prices to Yangzhou will be slightly higher. On the day that the Dada new ship starts service, the Datong ship of the Yixiang Shipping Bureau, which was previously represented by the Ping An Company, will be taken out of service and the lease will be terminated when the contract expires next year.

Rice Dealers Association: Important Notice to Colleagues Regarding the Inspection of Measuring Instruments 97

The Shanghai Rice Dealers Association issued a special notice to all colleagues in the city yesterday regarding the inspection of measuring instruments, stating: "This notice concerns the inspection of measuring instruments for the rice industry throughout the city by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Weights and Measures. Because the measuring instruments of various rice dealers have been altered, the Bureau of Weights and Measures has published a notice in the newspaper, requesting that the measuring instruments be sent to the Bureau for inspection within one month from June 20th. At the same time, the Association received instructions from the Bureau of Social Affairs. After repeated meetings of the executive and supervisory committees of the Association and repeated discussions, it was decided that if each rice dealer sends their own instruments for inspection, not only will there be no instruments available for sale, but the back-and-forth process will take a lot of time. If the measuring instruments are found to be unqualified, it will be impossible to modify them immediately. In order to facilitate the convenience of colleagues, the Association has sought and been granted permission from the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs to instruct the Bureau of Weights and Measures to send personnel to the Association to inspect the instruments. On the one hand, the Association will prepare replacement measuring instruments and send personnel to receive and issue them. If any measuring instruments are found to be unqualified after being altered, they will be corrected on the spot. The Association has also sought and been granted permission from the Bureau of Weights and Measures to exempt all altered measuring instruments from punishment during the inspection period. The notice has been filed with the entire organization. The inspection was officially started on July 9th. However, after this inspection, in order to prevent abuses, the Bureau of Weights and Measures will first divide all colleagues in the city, whether members or non-members, into districts in order by the Association, and number and mark each store as a unit. Then, the edge of each measuring instrument will be printed with a code, and then the inspection will be carried out. It is also stipulated that a qualified certificate for the inspection of measuring instruments with a hard seal will be issued by the Association along with the instrument, indicating that it is to be transferred by the Shanghai Rice Dealers Association. This certificate will classify each item and record the number and code. In the future, colleagues must bring the certificate to the Association when purchasing measuring instruments. If there is any damage, theft, transfer, etc., they must also bring the certificate to the Association to cancel the number and report the loss of the certificate to apply for a replacement. Otherwise, if the instrument number and quantity recorded on the certificate do not match, they will be dealt with according to law if discovered. All measuring instruments and certificates that were previously sent directly to the Bureau for inspection by each store number will be re-inspected and numbered by the Association, and the certificates will be replaced to ensure uniformity. After this major inspection, all of our colleagues must not alter the measuring instruments again, so as not to violate the law. You must know that the Association has taken great pains to protect its colleagues in order to have the convenience of today. However, in recent days, the Association has sent personnel to receive and issue measuring instruments, and it has been found that a small number of stores have altered too many measuring instruments and cannot be corrected. The Bureau of Weights and Measures found them to be unqualified and ordered that they must not be used again. Considering the situation, it is necessary to impose fines on each item. The Association has also requested exemption, but a small number of stores do not understand the situation and have forcibly detained the replacement measuring instruments of the Association, which is a great loss to the Association's intention to take care of its colleagues. Although these detained measuring instruments have been recovered by the Association one after another, it is feared that this will happen again in the future. The Association can only allow the Bureau of Weights and Measures to impose penalties on each item. Do not say that the Association has not fulfilled its responsibility to protect you. This notice is hereby given."
