Jijiang Ends Business

The Jijiang Steam Navigation Company sold all of its ships, totaling 6,800 tons, including (1) five ships on the Shanghai-Yichang line: Yifeng, Qitai, Yixing, Xietan, and Yijiang; (2) five ships on the Shanghai-Chongqing line: Yian, Yiping, Qiping, Yichang, and Qichun, all handled by the American Huizhong Banking Corporation. They have all been handed over to the British Butterfield & Swire Company and the private Minsheng Company. The company and its branch agencies in Zhangjiang ports have all been closed.

Minsheng Receives Vessels: Minsheng Industrial Company purchased seven ships: Gongtai, Yixing, Yijiang, Yian, Yichang, Gongchun, and Xietan. The names were changed and repainted. Now the Minyi wheel (formerly Yichang) has been repainted and set sail from Shanghai to Chongqing on the 19th. It is stipulated that it will make a round trip every twenty days. The remaining ships will be operating on the Shenyi, Yishen, Yuyi, Yuhan, Tonghe, Jiarong, Fuwan, Rongjia, Yuhe, and Yufu routes, respectively.

Butterfield & Swire Expands: Butterfield & Swire Steamship Company, which operates the Shanghai-Yichang line and the Shanghai-Chongqing line, was originally limited to Changsha, Shashi, Wuxue, and Yanhai. After purchasing Yifeng (2,605 tons), Yiping (654 tons), and Gongping (522 tons), etc., it decided to expand the upper reaches of the Yangtze River line and join the Shanghai-Yichang and Shanghai-Chongqing routes, as a regular direct release ship for loading cargo and passengers.

Ministry of Finance Plans to Aid the Economic Conditions of Overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia 99

The economic conditions of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, once holding a superior position, have been declining in recent years due to the impact of the global economic downturn, far from their former state. Kong Xiangxi, the Minister of Finance, previously sent Xu Jianping, the Director of the General Affairs Department of the Ministry, to Southeast Asia to investigate the current state of economic decline among overseas Chinese, in order to provide assistance. After returning to China, Xu compiled a report on his findings and submitted it to the Ministry of Finance for instructions. It is now known that the Ministry of Finance has thoroughly studied Xu's report, formulated measures, and plans to implement relief efforts in the near future.

Heavy Rain in Shanghai Yesterday, Clearing Up in the Evening, Pests in the Fields Gone, Pacific Hurricane Loitering East of Taiwan 104

After 9 p.m. yesterday, it rained again in Shanghai, continuing steadily until midnight, stopping only after 2 a.m. this morning. Yesterday morning, a gentle breeze caressed people, and wisps of clouds brought coolness. However, by noon yesterday, dark clouds gathered again, and the climate was stifling. From 3 p.m. onwards, there were sudden showers five times. As of 4:30 p.m., it was still alternately sunny and rainy. After 4:45 p.m., it cleared up completely, and the climate dropped by more than four degrees compared to the previous day. Many pests in the cotton and rice fields in the suburbs were eliminated. Details are recorded as follows:

Five Showers

At 3 p.m. yesterday, a sudden torrential rain fell in the Shanghai concession areas. The raindrops were larger than the previous night. Because the wind direction was quite stable, the raindrops fell from the sky in straight lines. It lessened slightly at 3:15 p.m., and after three minutes, it became heavier again, reaching its heaviest at 3:23 p.m. By 3:30 p.m., it subsided again, and at 3:35 p.m., the rain passed and the sun came out from the clouds. At 4 p.m., it suddenly rained again, and by 4:10 p.m., the rain was as large as beans. It had not completely stopped by 4:30 p.m. After 4:45 p.m., the rain finally stopped and the sky cleared. Although thunderclouds had not dissipated in the northeast corner in the evening, the climate turned cooler, and there was no sign of rain. According to the Observatory's report, the highest temperature yesterday was 92.1 degrees, and the lowest was 75.6 degrees, a difference of 4.7 degrees compared to the previous day's 96.8 degrees, and a decrease of 8.7 degrees from the hottest temperature of 100.8 degrees.

Pests Eliminated

It is reported that yesterday's rain greatly benefited the cotton and rice fields in the suburbs. In the past week, after the climate turned hot, black larvae grew in the rice paddies (the water in the rice fields also became hot after the heat, so these insects grew, commonly known as oil bugs). There were also fireflies in the cotton fields, which, although not causing great damage, also hindered the growth of cotton. Since yesterday's rain, most of the insects that were about to grow and spread were knocked down by the raindrops.

Hurricane Update

According to the Xujiahui Observatory's report at 2 p.m. yesterday, the hurricane that originated in the Pacific Ocean on the 17th has been loitering east of Taiwan for four days. At 2 p.m. yesterday, it was located between 24.5 degrees north latitude and 125 degrees east longitude, with its direction being west-northwest, and its circumference still being 60 nautical miles.

Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Works Installs Traffic Lights in South Shanghai, to be Implemented on August 1st 105

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Works, in order to improve land traffic in Shanghai and facilitate the flow of vehicles, installed traffic lights in densely populated areas such as Laoximen to maintain order and provide convenience for travelers. Two Children Playing with a Bomb Causes a Tragedy, the Bomb Falls on the Cement Ground with a Loud Explosion, One Child Dies and One is Injured, a Very Tragic Situation 108

Zhang Bingsheng, a native of Zhejiang, eleven years old, works as a small apprentice in a silver furnace on Yongxing Road, Zhabei. Yesterday morning, at around 9 a.m., Zhang and several neighborhood children were playing in a nearby wasteland when they accidentally found an egg-shaped bomb in the bushes. Zhang Bingsheng did not recognize what it was and happily took it home. It happened to be seen by a Sheng child named Jingsheng (ten years old) from No. 2 Yongxing Lane, who regarded it as a rare object and insisted on taking it from Bingsheng. While they were playing with it, they inadvertently dropped the bomb on the cement ground. Upon impact, it exploded with a loud bang, and iron fragments and flesh flew everywhere, smoke filled the air, and the smell of sulfur was pungent. Residents in the lane suddenly heard the loud noise and rushed out to investigate, seeing two children injured and lying in the lane. Sheng Jingsheng was covered in blood and gore, a gruesome sight, and died on the spot from severe injuries. Zhang Bingsheng's hands and feet were also injured by the explosion, and blood flowed profusely. The police officers on duty in the area also arrived at the scene upon hearing the noise. After seeing the situation, they reported to the Fire Brigade, which transported the dead and injured children to the Coroner's Office and the Chinese Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road for treatment. However, Zhang Bingsheng's injuries are also very serious, and his life may be in danger. The source of the bomb, after investigation and research by the police station in charge, is suspected to be left over from wartime.

Compilation of Rent Reduction Movement News 110

Shanghai East District Rent Reduction Association: The Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee held a joint representative meeting of its branch associations at its meeting place at Chengxin Lane, Huade Road, at 9 a.m. yesterday. Attendees included Zheng Jianbo, Chen Jiufeng, Ma Yuanbai, Jin Wen, Su Guohun, Du Chunxun, Xiang Jianxiang, Liu Xiuchun, Yan Zuliang, Zhong Guifu, Yang Zhenchun, Shi Baoyan, Zhou Liankui, Fang Baolin, Zhang De, Lin Shaoyu, and representatives from Chengxin Lane Branch Association, Sida Lane Branch Association, Hongyuan Lane Branch Association, Tongle Lane Branch Association, Huaxing Lane Branch Association, etc., totaling more than 60 people. Zheng Jianbo, Bai Jinwen, Du Chunxun, Qiu Yaoshan, and Ma Yuan were publicly elected as the presidium of the meeting, and Wang Bingcheng was the secretary. After the rituals were performed, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that "Today is the joint representative meeting of the branch associations of our Shanghai East District Rent Reduction Committee. We are very honored to have the enthusiastic participation of all representatives and branch associations. However, since the organization of the Rent Reduction Committee, it has been many months, and we feel that we have not achieved any results, which is truly regrettable. Now, because the social economy is in a slump and the decline of industry and commerce has reached its extreme, property prices have plummeted, and rents should be appropriately reduced. Therefore, we have called all of you representatives here today to discuss together how to alleviate the burden on tenants and to seek a support for the revival of the market. We hope that all of our representatives will pool their efforts to facilitate progress." Proposals decided upon: (1) Sida Lane representative proposed: This lane requests a reduction in rent and has repeatedly requested it from the landlord, but the landlord is not only unwilling to accommodate but also resolutely refuses to acknowledge it. The association should assist in this case. Resolved: The association will send a letter and dispatch Committee Member Cheng Juetian to directly negotiate with the landlord to alleviate the burden on tenants. Passed. (2) Committee Member Zheng proposed: The Chengxin Lane owner, Sincere Company, has agreed to reduce store rents by five yuan and lane rents by three yuan. Should the lawsuit be withdrawn? Resolved: The lawsuit will continue, and the association's legal counsel will appear in court to defend. Passed. (3) Jinyu Lane, Tangshan Road, requests to organize a branch association to participate in this case. Resolved: Permission is granted to organize and participate. Passed. (4) Huaxing Lane representative proposed: This lane requests a rent reduction and has already negotiated with the landlord, but there has been no result. The association should assist in this case. Resolved: Committee Members Bai Jinwen and Zhao Yongjun will be dispatched to negotiate directly with the landlord. (5) Committee Member Du Chunxun proposed: How should the association's publicity work be carried out? Resolved: Slogans will be printed and posted in each lane to promote awareness. Passed. (6) Committee Member Chen Jiufeng proposed: The association is also a complete organization of citizens and should be registered with the General Association, and then each lane should organize its own branch association to facilitate progress. Resolved: The matter will be handled by the Secretariat. (7) Committee Member Ma Yuan proposed: In addition to publicity slogans, it would be more beneficial to add a special publication on rent reduction in the Shanghai Fruits District. The public should decide on this. Resolved: It will be carried out as proposed. Passed. (8) The association plans to expand its organization. How should it be handled? Resolved: Ten more committee members will be added to facilitate expansion. Passed. (9) Committee Member Qiu Yaoshan proposed: How should the association's finances be managed? Resolved: Committee Member Zheng will draft a budget, which will be passed at the next Executive Committee meeting. The meeting adjourned at 11 a.m.

Tenant Representatives of Dean Lane: Since the January 28th Incident, the market in the Hongkou District of Shanghai has not recovered. Recently, shops and residents along Suzhou Road, North Shanxi Road, and Tiantong Road have united to organize a rent reduction movement due to the sluggish market conditions and heavy burden, especially the large expense of rent. They have requested the assistance of the 15th and 36th Branch Associations of the Municipal Federation to achieve the goal of rent reduction. As a result of the efforts of the two branch associations, Mr. Bei Runsheng, the owner of Xintai'an Lane, has agreed to a 20% discount on store rents and a 10% discount on residential rents. The association, considering that Xintai'an Lane has made a clear statement, will seek the opinions of the majority. Yesterday, it notified all shops and residents in the lane that if they are not satisfied with the degree of rent reduction offered by the owner, they can submit their opinions to the association. As for the residents of Dean Lane on Suzhou Road, because the owner has not made a clear statement, an emergency meeting of Dean Lane representatives was convened at 3 p.m. yesterday. More than 20 representatives, including Shen Anqing, Tian Daiting, Qiu Minzhong, Ye Ping, Wang Yucheng, Jiang Zonghai, Zong Hai, Lu Rongtang, Yang Runsheng, Song Wenzheng, and Fan Sunfu, were present. Xu Kaixian was publicly elected as chairman. Four measures were decided upon: (1) Rent will not be paid until the goal of rent reduction is achieved. (2) The minimum rent reduction should be 30%. (3) Rent money will be deposited in a bank for safekeeping. (4) The owner of the neighboring Xintai'an Lane has offered an 20% rent reduction, while the owner of this lane is simply procrastinating. The Municipal Federation should be requested to seriously step in to alleviate the burden. The meeting adjourned at 5 p.m.

(3) If necessary, representatives will be sent to discuss with the owner in person to avoid escalating the situation. (4) "Confidential" Other matters were not discussed, and the meeting adjourned.

Continued Trial of the Murder of a Gatekeeper and Policeman in Fuxili, Tianjin Road - The Deceased Took a Woman into an Empty House, and the Murderer Argued for Locking It, Leading to a Dispute - Another Policeman Testifies in Court 111

Wang Tongchun, a thirty-five-year-old native of Haizhou and gatekeeper and policeman at No. 35 Fuxili, Tianjin Road, had a minor quarrel with Shen Lianfa, a native of Shandong and gatekeeper at Qingcheng Qianzhuang No. 1589 in the lane. Wang immediately drew his gun and fired four shots, killing Shen. Wang was detained by Chief Detective Wu Yaozu and Detective Zhu Wanjun of the General Patrol Room and handed over to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. This was previously reported in this newspaper. The trial was continued in the First Criminal Court by Chief Criminal Judge Qian Hongye of the First Special Court. First, the police lawyer Jiang Baolian stated that during the adjournment, the police had inspected the handgun worn by the deceased, and the results proved that it had not been fired recently. Next, Witness Bu Ganting, policeman No. 996, testified that one or two days before the incident, the deceased had taken five or six women into an empty house at No. 6 in the lane. After being seen by the defendant, the defendant ordered Shen Gengsheng, the lane manager, to lock the empty house, causing a disagreement between the two. I intervened to mediate, so at the time of the incident, I advised the defendant not to lock the empty house, because the weather was hot, and if the house was locked, colleagues would have no place to rest. While we were talking, the deceased happened to arrive, and his face was not very good. The defendant snorted, and the deceased turned back, his face even worse. The defendant also stepped forward, and soon after, several gunshots were heard. I did not see the deceased fire his gun at that time. When questioned, the defendant stated that the deceased cursed at me first, then put his hand on his gun holster, as if he wanted to draw his gun and shoot me, so I preemptively shot him. He also hired lawyer Jiang Chiping to defend him, saying that the defendant also had several wounds on his body and may have been involved in a mutual fight at the time. The court ordered a postponement to further investigate whether Wang Tongchun had any injuries and should be sent for forensic examination.

Unable to Support His Family After Being Unemployed for a Long Time, Wang Afu Commits Suicide, Separated from His Legal Wife for a Long Time, and Often Quarrels with His Concubine 112

Wang Afu, a native of Zhenhai, Ningbo, thirty-one years old this year, married a fellow villager Zhu (twenty-six years old this year) as his wife and had three children. Wang used to be a fireman on a ship, but he has been unemployed for many years. Because of discord between husband and wife, Zhu led her children to live at No. 3 Xiangshan Lane, Yanjia Pavilion Road, Zhabei, and worked in a printing factory to make a living. Wang had an affair with Pan Meixiao (twenty-three years old this year) from Xiashi, and they lived together at No. 11 Yinyu Lane, Bafang Bridge, French Concession. Pan was originally a prostitute and now raises several young prostitutes as private prostitutes for a living. Wang was supported by Pan. Recently, because he had been unemployed for a long time and had no money to subsidize his family, he often quarreled with his concubine. Wang had a sudden impulse to commit suicide. At 4:30 a.m. on the 20th, he suddenly got up and went outside, secretly swallowing poison to commit suicide. About half an hour after taking the poison, he still went home and lay down, crying incessantly. Only then was he discovered by his concubine, Pan MeiQing, who immediately sent him to Renji Hospital. Because he had been poisoned too deeply, the rescue was ineffective, and he died at 0:30 p.m. that afternoon. The hospital reported to the police station, which sent detectives to investigate the cause of the deceased's suicide. At the same time, the body was taken to the Tongren Funeral Home for autopsy. The concubine notified the deceased's wife and brother, Wang Genlin, to come. Yesterday, the police station reported to the Special Court, and Prosecutor Wang Ren and a forensic medical examiner went to the funeral home in the morning to examine the body. The court was set up after the case was reported by the Bao detective. The official asked the deceased's wife and concubine about the cause and course of the deceased's suicide. The deceased's wife, Wang Zhu, wished to claim the body for burial. The official then announced that Wang Afu had indeed died by taking poison before his death. The body was handed over to the deceased's wife for burial after she signed a guarantee.

New Shanghai County Magistrate Takes Office Today 113

Pan Zhongjia, the Shanghai County Magistrate, has been approved to resign, and Ye Zhendong, the Magistrate of Zhenjiang County, has been transferred to succeed him by the provincial capital. Wu Huanru of the Bureau of Social Affairs Discusses the Shortening of the Pledge Period, Which Has Been Carefully Considered. The Decline of the Pawnshop Industry in the Urban Area in Recent Years is True, and the Investigation Will Be Signed and Submitted to the Bureau Chief for Decision 114

The Shanghai Pawnshop Association, in order to reduce the operating losses of pawnshops at all nine levels, has specially submitted a request to the Bureau of Social Affairs for permission to shorten the pledge period from eighteen months to twelve months in order to maintain operations. The submission has been made and representatives have been sent to petition, hoping to achieve this as soon as possible. A reporter from Dagong Newspaper met with Wu Huanru, the section chief of the Second Section of the Bureau of Social Affairs, yesterday and asked about the latest developments in the case and whether it was possible to approve it. According to Wu, the proposal of the Pawnshop Association to shorten the pledge period had been submitted to the Bureau half a year ago. This move would have a great impact on the livelihood of the poor. Without careful consideration and understanding of the livelihood of the poor in both the Chinese and foreign concession areas, it would have a great impact. There are two views among the industry on shortening the pledge period: one insists on maintaining the original period (i.e., eighteen months, mostly industry in the concession area), and the other insists on changing it to twelve months. In the future, if the government approves twelve months, then the industry will have the freedom to operate, either according to eighteen months or fifteen months, which should not be a problem. If the government orders the original pledge period to be followed, then the industry cannot arbitrarily shorten the number of months. Therefore, the Bureau has truly understood the decline and significant losses of the pawnshop industry, but it cannot be denied that once the pledge period is shortened, the harm to the poor will be unavoidable. The details have been signed and submitted to the Bureau Chief for review and approval, and a direct reply will be given in the future, or it will be submitted to the Municipal Affairs Conference for discussion, and the decision will be made in accordance with the Bureau Chief's decision.

The Civil and Criminal Divisions of the Higher Court Third Branch Will Each Have a Presiding Judge 115

When the Third Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court was established in August 1931, it originally had civil and criminal divisions, each with two presiding judges and judges working. Since the January 28th Incident, the changes have been changed to civil and criminal divisions, with one presiding judge and three judges handling civil and criminal appeal cases. It is heard that since the implementation of the three-level three-trial system on July 1st of this year, the number of civil and criminal appeal cases will inevitably increase, and the original method of establishing separate civil and criminal divisions, each with its own presiding judge, will be changed. The presiding judge of the civil division will be Mr. Guo Dezhang, the current presiding judge, and the presiding judge of the criminal division will be concurrently held by President Liang. Now, because Judge Sun Honglin of the Criminal Division has been transferred to the Supreme Court for three months and has not yet returned, the old rules will be temporarily maintained. Presiding Judge Guo will concurrently serve as the presiding judge of the criminal division. Roughly from August 1st, after Mr. Sun returns to Shanghai, Mr. Guo will serve as the presiding judge of the civil division, and Mr. Sun will serve as the presiding judge of the criminal division. The two judges in each division will remain unchanged.

Epidemic Prevention Campaign Intensified: Municipal Health Bureau Actively Prevents Epidemics; Recent Focus on Slums and Factories for Injections; Disinfection of Riverbanks and Stagnant Water Continues 116

Since the beginning of summer, the municipal health authorities have been actively engaged in epidemic prevention. Personnel have been dispatched by the Municipal Health Bureau to administer injections in schools throughout the city. As schools have now closed for the summer vacation this month, the focus has shifted to administering injections in factories and slums. According to sources at the bureau, there have been very few epidemic diseases in the city since the beginning of summer, and no cases of cholera have been discovered. There were rumors of cholera cases in the Songjiang area, but these have not been confirmed. The bureau has instructed the Caohejing area in western Shanghai to pay special attention to epidemic prevention to prevent the disease from entering the city. The weather has been cooler recently, and the number of heatstroke cases has decreased compared to before. Therefore, this summer can be considered very peaceful. The bureau's epidemic prevention campaign is currently focused on administering injections in factories and slums, and the work is extremely intensive. Recently, from the 16th to the 20th of this month, injections were administered in 81 factories. Including those injected previously, the total number exceeds 200. The British-American Tobacco Company in Pudong and Hongkou has sent letters to the bureau requesting that personnel be dispatched to administer injections. The bureau is currently planning to implement this within the week. The disinfection of riverbanks and stagnant water in the city is continuing, using kerosene and glass fragments as disinfectants. Personnel are dispatched daily to disinfect, to prevent the breeding of mosquitoes and other bacteria that endanger the health of citizens.

The French Municipal Council of this city, finding that the original building at the site of the Big Ben on Avenue Edward VII is old and insufficient for its needs, plans to build a new building at the junction of Avenue Joffre and Rue Henri-Rivière. Clothing Industry Complies with Advice to Renovate, But is Still Sued for Illegal Roadside Display; Citizens' Association Sends Letter to First Special District Court Requesting Exemption from Punishment Due to Unreasonable Oppression by Municipal Council 120

The Second Branch of the Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Association, on behalf of its members Tong Zhenhe and 17 other stores, states that they have complied with the Municipal Council's notice and removed and renovated their clothes racks and signs within the deadline of the 14th. However, the Municipal Council has sued them in the First Special District Court for illegal roadside display, which is considered unreasonable oppression. The association has sent a letter to the First Special District Court requesting exemption from punishment to alleviate the hardship of businesses, and plans to request assistance from the Chinese Ratepayers Association and the Citizens' General Association. The original letter is transcribed below: "We have received letters from our members Tong Zhenhe, Yuan Fengsheng, Yuan Shun, Yuan Changsheng, Tong Fengsheng, Sanhe, Tong Yonghe, Yuan Tai, Yuan Sen, Rui Shengxiang, Sen Yuanxiang, Hua Zhang, Sen Hexiang, Shuang Sheng, Heng Fengqin, Pinghe, Tong Shunhe, and Xu Fengtai, stating that on the 11th and 12th of this month, they received a notice from the Works Department of the Municipal Council stating that the clothes racks and signs installed in front of their stores extended beyond the building line, violating the land regulations. They were given 14 days to remove or renovate them according to the notice, or face fines. After receiving the notice, our members complied and completed the removal and renovation within the deadline. We thought the matter was over. However, on the 20th, they suddenly received summons from the First Special District Court, stating that the police station was suing them for displaying too many clothes on the sidewalk, causing an illegal roadside display. The court summonsed them for trial on the 23rd and 24th of this month. After receiving the summons, they were very surprised. Our members complied with the notice and renovated and retracted their displays within the deadline, without exceeding the deadline. Why would the Municipal Council suddenly sue them in court? This is deeply suspicious. Our members operate clothing stores and originally displayed clothing samples to facilitate customer selection and purchase. This has been the practice for decades. Now, suddenly being prohibited from displaying clothes will greatly affect their business. Moreover, in this time of extreme economic depression, businesses are collapsing and in danger. It is difficult to operate a business. However, the Municipal Council authorities do not understand the hardship of the citizens within the concession and repeatedly interfere, prohibiting the display of clothes and signs, making it difficult for our members. The police station's accusation of displaying too many clothes is an advertising matter in business. It is difficult to construct a case of illegal roadside display. The height of the display is appropriate and does not cause any obstruction. Why should it be prohibited? Moreover, the court summons on the 23rd and 24th of July will punish them for illegal display, indirectly affecting their business and directly imposing fines. How can they bear this unexpected burden? Your association is a citizens' organization dedicated to promoting the welfare of citizens. Therefore, we earnestly request that you negotiate with the Municipal Council to allow the display of clothing samples in front of their stores, as long as it does not obstruct pedestrians, and to request the court to exempt them from punishment. The above is the situation presented. In view of the fact that these stores complied and automatically renovated and retracted their displays within the 14-day deadline, and did not exceed the deadline, they should not be subject to punishment for illegal display. Correspondingly, we request your court to order the police court to exempt them from punishment to alleviate the hardship of businesses and benefit the community. We extend our public friendship. This is addressed to Guo, President of the Shanghai First Special District Local Court (remaining text omitted)."

Unexpectedly, after several months, Zhu Lie and the others have recently sued Shi Muzhao, the station manager of Zhoupu Station of the Shangnan Transportation Company, for assault and obstruction of freedom in the local court. (After this incident, the board of directors of the Shangnan Transportation Company suspended the station manager Shi Muzhao for three months for negligence. He has now completed his suspension and has resumed his duties.) Yesterday, Prosecutor Li Fen ordered Patrol Officer Zhou Yuguang of the First Sub-Precinct of Zhoupu and Patrol Officer Xiao Jingfu of the Yangsiqiao Sub-Precinct to appear in court to be questioned separately about the circumstances of the incident. The questioning was very detailed. As a result, the two patrol officers were ordered to return to their posts. If necessary, they will be summoned again.

Chinese-Owned Xiang Sheng Automobile Company: Compiles Secret Codes for Telephone Taxi Hailing; Simple to Use, A Win-Win Situation 127

The Chinese-owned Xiang Sheng Automobile Company in the city, founded by Mr. Zhou Xiang Sheng, is large in scale and has branches throughout the city. To facilitate taxi hailing for customers, the company has compiled secret codes for telephone taxi hailing. The codes are printed on yellow hard cards measuring three and three-quarters inches long and two and three-quarters inches wide. Personnel are sent to distribute the cards to various users. When users receive the cards, they write their addresses next to the pre-compiled numbers in the company's number book. This means that the number is directly assigned to the user. To use the service, dial the company's telephone number and report the secret code number. The company will immediately dispatch a taxi from the nearest branch. Users can save time and avoid the hassle of reporting detailed addresses over the telephone, and avoid errors. It is truly a win-win situation.

Special Article Simple Life Insurance and Social Insurance (3) 140

— Zhang Mingxin

(1) State Monopoly: Japan, in light of the fact that the British simple life insurance was not exclusively operated by the state, leading to its decline and failure, took into consideration its own national conditions from the outset and made changes. It was designated as a state-run enterprise, utilizing the existing 7,000-plus post offices throughout the country to handle this business. This saved expenses and made the business easier to popularize. Therefore, since its inception, it has progressed extremely rapidly, becoming a successful example of state-run simple life insurance.

(2) Purpose Not for Profit: Simple life insurance is a social undertaking. The insured are mostly middle and lower-class people with limited financial resources. Although the premiums paid are not much, every drop comes from savings from hard work. In addition to operating expenses, ordinary life insurance companies must also consider the dividends for their shareholders, which increases the burden on the insured, contrary to the original purpose of simple life insurance. Therefore, the huge profits earned by companies in various European and American countries that also operate simple life insurance are a major reason for criticizing private simple life insurance. Furthermore, the result of their mutual competition is that the less-informed public does not know what to do, and premiums increase, causing more contracts to lapse, which inevitably affects the business itself and poses a danger. Therefore, state-run simple life insurance, not aiming for profit and having no additional expenses, can naturally reduce the burden on policyholders. If there is a surplus, it can all be used for the welfare of policyholders. This is why Japan, at its inception, based it on the realization of social policies and designated it as a non-profit business.

(3) Regulations on the Use of Accumulated Funds: Accumulated funds are the premiums collected from the efforts of many policyholders to save money. They are kept by the insurer to generate interest, in preparation for future payment of insurance amounts. Ordinary life insurance companies often use their accumulated funds for investments with high interest rates, but do not consider whether the investments are beneficial to policyholders. Japanese simple life insurance, being state-run and aiming not for profit, naturally has a different approach to the use of its accumulated funds. Therefore, at the time of its establishment, it was stipulated that it should be used for investments that are beneficial to the public, and an investment committee was established to oversee it. The method of returning funds to their source is also used to avoid concentrating them in one place. This is to take from the people and use for the people. The scope of investment includes elementary schools, hospitals, public housing, rural projects, water conservancy projects, public employment agencies, nurseries, and more. Simple life insurance can directly foster a spirit of thrift and savings among the public, and obtain insurance benefits with a small amount of money. Indirectly, it can also promote national economic and material construction, and promote social prosperity, which is very clear.

(4) Independent Accounting: In order to solidify the foundation of the business and prevent it from being affected by other national finances, the accounting of Japanese simple life insurance is stipulated to be independent and not mixed with other national accounts. In 1916, the Simple Life Insurance Special Accounting Act passed by the Imperial Parliament stipulated that the revenue of simple life insurance should be used to cover its expenditures. The revenue items are insurance premiums and income generated from accumulated funds, while the expenditures are insurance payments, redemption fees, business expenses, and other expenses. It is also stipulated that when the revenue is insufficient, it can be subsidized by the accumulated funds. Except for the first year (actually six months) when the contract performance exceeded the forecast by more than double, resulting in a budget deficit and a subsidy of more than 60,000 yuan from the accumulated funds preserved by the national treasury, the growth of its accumulated funds is truly amazing. Over the years, the terms and conditions for policyholders have also become increasingly favorable, which is enough to prove that its accumulated funds have exceeded the reserve liability.

(5) Health Facilities: The main purpose of life insurance, in addition to protecting against family economic losses and increasing social wealth, is also to extend the life of the insured. Modern life insurance companies in various countries spend huge sums of money each year to improve the health of policyholders. Extending the life of the insured reduces the mortality rate, while also increasing the productivity of society, which is of great benefit to the life insurance business itself. From its inception, Japanese simple life insurance paid attention to the health of the insured and actively researched various appropriate facilities. By 1922, as its business had become stable and developed, it first established seven health examination centers throughout the country. By 1934, it had gradually increased to 175 centers. More than 4.2 million people have used these facilities. The types of facilities are divided into five categories: (1) health examination centers, (2) printing of health publications, (3) health and hygiene propaganda, (4) creation of national health exercises, and (5) cooperation in tuberculosis prevention campaigns. The Central Health Examination Center is located in the Simple Insurance Bureau and is the largest in scale. Its nature is no different from the local examination centers, but it does not provide home nursing services because the center is actually responsible for handling matters that are difficult to implement locally, such as expensive medical equipment, blood serum tests, and various testing facilities. Currently, counting all 175 centers nationwide, there are 203 doctors, 417 nurses, 22 X-ray staff, and 154 other employees. The annual expenditure for each center is set at 10,000 yuan, for a total annual expenditure of 1.75 million yuan, which is undoubtedly a huge benefit to policyholders.

6. The Process of Preparing for Simple Life Insurance in Our Country

Our country is an economically backward country. Since being affected by the global recession, industry and commerce have declined daily, and the rural areas are on the verge of bankruptcy. Furthermore, foreign troubles are frequent, without a single peaceful day. Natural disasters such as floods and droughts come one after another, and the precarious situation is like a pile of eggs. Fortunately, in recent years, the campaign to suppress bandits is about to be completed, local order is gradually becoming peaceful, and construction projects are progressing daily. It is the awakening and arduous struggle of the Chinese people. Overcoming difficulties and building the country is not an unachievable goal. As the ancients said, "Three years of farming yields one year of savings, and nine years of labor yields three years of storage." Then, the simple life insurance business cultivates the people's virtue of thrift and embodies savings in insurance, benefiting the national economy, people's livelihood, and material construction. How can we give up eating because of choking and not quickly plan to do it? Understanding this, the significance of our country's preparation for simple life insurance is more than half understood. Now, let us briefly describe the reasons for state operation and its process as follows:

(1) Why Simple Life Insurance Should Be Exclusively Operated by the State: The purpose of operating simple life insurance has been stated repeatedly, but the reasons why it should be exclusively operated by the state are briefly described below. First, the foundation is solid. Simple life insurance targets the majority of the public as the insured, and the premiums paid come from hard work and thrift. They must also be paid monthly. If the foundation of the insurance business is shaken, it will cause great pain in spirit and material. In particular, the members of companies and factories are mostly group contracts. If they encounter misfortune, the number of people is large and the appeal is strong. If private companies are allowed to operate, there will inevitably be profit competition. If unfortunately there is a shake-up, it will affect the people and cause great harm. Therefore, it should be classified as a state monopoly, with the accumulated funds preserved by the national treasury as a guarantee. With reliable protection, the foundation can be consolidated. Second, the purpose is non-profit. Simple life insurance is a social undertaking, and its purpose is based on non-profit. Due to the special nature of the business, the expenditure on operating expenses is also relatively large. At the same time, premiums must be kept low. Therefore, it is necessary to use the existing and widespread postal agencies and their personnel to handle this business. Only then can it be expected to reduce costs and use the accumulated funds to generate interest according to the direction of social policies, in order to improve the welfare of the people. This is especially beyond the operating direction and capabilities of private life insurance companies. Third, the business is popular. If the simple life insurance business is operated by private companies, due to the relationship between income and expenditure, they will inevitably focus on cities as the important operating areas. They will mostly ignore other cities, making it difficult to achieve popularity. However, with state monopoly, it can be planned and taken care of as a whole, making it popular throughout the country, so that people in remote areas have the opportunity to use it, so that the purpose of the business can be implemented and achieve twice the result with half the effort.

(2) On the Formulation of the Simple Life Insurance Law: In the second year after its opening, in the autumn of the 10th year of the Republic of China, the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, considering the importance of simple life insurance to the national economy and people's livelihood, drafted the Simple Life Insurance Law, which was submitted to the Ministry of Transportation for review and forwarded to the Legislative Yuan for review. The process was interrupted due to the September 18th and January 28th incidents. When Mr. Zhu Jiahua took office as Minister of Transportation, he believed that the simple life insurance business made a great contribution to the country and society and should be prepared to increase national welfare. He submitted it to the Executive Yuan for transfer to the Legislative Yuan for continued review, and at the same time ordered the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau to quickly prepare and draft an implementation plan for submission to the Ministry for approval. Subsequently, the Legislative Yuan handed over the draft to the Legal and Economic Committees for review. After several reviews, it was passed by the 14th General Assembly this year (24th year). It was subsequently promulgated by the National Government on May 10 of the same year, and the Savings and Remittance Bureau was ordered to draft subsidiary regulations, which have also been submitted to the Ministry for approval.

(3) Dispatching Personnel to Japan to Investigate Simple Life Insurance Matters: The state-run simple life insurance business is most successful in Japan, as mentioned earlier. The social situation in our country is also relatively similar to that of Japan. Mr. Zuo, who specialized in human insurance in the United States in the past, has been responsible for preparing for simple life insurance matters since joining the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau. Fortunately, Minister Zhu Gongfeng was spared no effort and sent him to Japan last autumn to investigate all matters related to simple life insurance. After arriving in Japan, he went to the Simple Insurance Bureau (the general bureau handling the national simple insurance business), the Postal Savings Bureau (the Postal Savings Bureau), and its first, second, and third-class post offices and the Simple Life Insurance Central Health Examination Center to conduct detailed investigations. He not only sought details of internal handling procedures, but also explored them in detail, and discussed them with experts, lasting more than two months. He also collected more than 400 kinds of materials for our reference.

(4) Recent Preparations: The state-run simple life insurance is a great undertaking. To adapt to the needs of the people and promote business, the procedures are simplified externally, while the internal procedures are quite complicated. Sufficient preparations must be made before it can be expected to proceed smoothly. Therefore, the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau is currently making every effort to prepare for the initial launch in Shanghai, Nanjing, and Hankou, and then gradually extend it to the whole country. However, the success of Japanese simple life insurance depends not only on the diligence and dedication of the staff, but also on the support of the community. Simple life insurance cannot be effective without collective efforts. It is hoped that people in our country will promote this emerging social insurance business. Sincerely, with incense and prayers.

7 Conclusion

Due to space limitations, the above description of the functions of simple life insurance and social insurance and their process is only a brief outline. However, the life insurance business is a necessary organization for social economy. The development of this business is linked to the progress of national civilization, and simple life insurance is a facility to realize social policies, benefit the national economy and people's livelihood, and relieve the economic losses suffered by the general public. The law is good and the intention is beautiful, and nothing surpasses it. Although the methods of various countries are different, their important principles are the same. Ordinary life insurance has been circulating in our country for decades. In terms of progress, it is very slow. There are few life insurance companies at present. It is worrying that it is not enough to handle ordinary life insurance, let alone simple life insurance. This is why the government authorities have prepared simple life insurance to meet the needs of the people. However, the main purpose of the business is not to compete with private life insurance companies. Because its insurance has certain restrictions, such as policyholders who want to enrich their economic protection because of better customs, they can re-apply to private life insurance companies for a larger amount of life insurance. Moreover, because simple Tao insurance has universal publicity to popularize insurance ideas, it can also increase the business of private life insurance companies. It is beneficial to private life insurance companies both directly and indirectly. Mingxin, July 15, 24th year, (End)

Spring and Autumn

Jottings 141

— Shoujuan

Mourning Mr. Zheng Zhengqiu

Oh, heavens! What kind of era has it been for these three years? Internal troubles, foreign aggression, natural disasters, and human disasters are all pressing down on this poor China, leaving it riddled with holes and in a terrible state. The loss of territory, the loss of economy, the loss of talent, and the loss of culture cannot all be listed in a table or cleared up with numbers. Oh, heavens! Is this due to the unkindness of heaven or the inadequacy of human plans?

In these three years, the successive deaths of relatives, elders, teachers, and friends have made me disheartened with the world after grief. But I did not expect that my old friend of twenty years, Mr. Zheng Zhengqiu, would also leave us. This is another very important item in the list of talent losses, which has left me dumbfounded for several days. Not only has the Mingxing Film Company lost a cornerstone, the film industry has lost a mentor, but China has also lost a fighting warrior in art and culture.

Recalling his contributions to the stage and screen over the past twenty years, how great they were. Every May, I could often see him appear on stage to speak out, performing "Hidden Pain" and "Old Man Huang's Dream," crying bitterly, wanting to awaken the Chinese people from their delusions. Who knew that times would change, the situation would deteriorate, and Zheng Zhengqiu, although the universe is vast, there is no place for you to cry bitterly now. Even if you don't die of illness, you will be suffocated alive! Therefore, while mourning Zhengqiu, I am also fortunate for Zhengqiu, because once it's over, what is there to miss in this world?

Zhengqiu, although you died quietly, your spirit is immortal, and your soul is immortal. When the autumn graves sing with ghosts, we can still see your "Hidden Pain" and hear your "Old Man Huang's Dream."

Pavilion 142

— Rongyu

Along a long official road, there is always a pavilion standing every ten or eight miles. Although it is dilapidated and there is no scenery to admire, it is still a great merit to give people traveling long distances a place to rest their feet and get some fresh air. Especially in the hot weather, people walking under the scorching sun, with no shade from trees on either side, with sweat beads hanging down like yellow beans, resting in that pavilion is as refreshing as eating ginseng fruit. Therefore, this pavilion is not just an ornament in the countryside, but a philanthropist who helps travelers.

The structure of the pavilions, although not uniform in size, is always like this: pointed top, surrounded by bird-wing-like corrugated tiles, with square, hexagonal, octagonal, and rectangular shapes. Short retaining walls are built around the perimeter, and you can see the scenery in all four directions while sitting inside. The long stone strips are the easy chairs for travelers. The rough stone surface has been smoothed and oiled by people sitting on it, showing how many people competing for fame and fortune pass by on this road every day, sitting on the stone sweating and panting. I think that if the stone strip had knowledge, it would be secretly laughing at the busy lives of people, wondering what they are for!

Those who rest in the pavilion are always peddlers, porters, and frustrated friends. Noble people have cars and boats and will never patronize here. People sit here without having to ask each other's names. If you like peace and quiet, sit alone for a while and run away. If you like to chat, you can chat with the people sitting next to you, talking nonsense to relieve boredom. Besides, you don't know when or if you will meet the people you meet again, so there is a feeling of "meeting by chance" and "why bother to know each other when we meet"!

"The pavilion is good, but it is not a place to linger for long." This is true: people come here, rest for a while and leave, and never stay for ten or eight days. However, there are also pavilions that are taken over by beggars, who set up shop in the corners of the pavilion, building ten stoves, blackening the walls with smoke. The stone benches are their beds, and the straw mats, bamboo poles, and broken baskets are spread all over the ground. When you encounter this situation, it makes travelers afraid to rest!

Tropical Sentiment 143

— Yiqiu

Moonlit night, under dense coconut trees, on the soft green grass, young girls sit, leisurely playing with their moon lutes (or pipa). The beautiful sound and scenery attract many passing youths, who run to sit beside them. Embracing, singing, and soon, pairs of them go home. These girls have slightly brown skin, but they are delicate and beautiful. All young people find them lovely. This is the special sentiment of the Dutch East Indies island of Java.

The river water is not deep but very clear. Many women ride on the backs of giant elephants to cross the river. Some elephants even have small canopies on their backs to avoid the scorching sun. The strangest thing is that their full and beautiful breasts are on display for everyone to see, without being covered by clothes. It is said that they worship virgins, so they open their chests and bare their breasts to show that they are still virgins and are not afraid of being inspected. This is a custom near Siam.

These two tropical sentiments were told to me in a letter from Miss Pan Wenjuan, who is currently a popular entertainer in Nanyang. I found them interesting and I am passing them on to the readers of Spring and Autumn.

Random Musings on Bedbugs 144

— Drunkard Student

Recently, I read Mr. You Aimei's "Broken Clouds and Scattered Rain Records." It mentions a story about Baoying County: regardless of which shop it is, none of them are willing to exterminate bedbugs. Moreover, they avoid calling them bedbugs, instead calling them "money bugs," and so on. This reminded me of a friend, Mr. Huang, more than ten years ago. He was a big fellow who opened a very large shop in the northern part of the city. In the summer, the employees were disturbed by bedbugs and couldn't sleep well at night, so they wanted to find a way to exterminate them. However, this boss (Mr. Huang) remained calm and indifferent. He even defended the bedbugs, saying: these bedbugs are "wealth bugs," only wealthy families have them. Unlike the lice on poor people's bodies, which are hateful. Think about it, Shanghai has a large population and thriving commerce, so there are so many bedbugs. If there were no "wealth bugs," how could the market be so prosperous? People laughed so hard they couldn't stand up straight when they heard what he said. Now his shop has long since failed and closed down. As for the economic downturn, it has reached its extreme. I wonder what he thinks of wealth bugs now. Furthermore, Mr. Aimei said: Suzhou has a special custom. When a woman gets married, they always catch two bedbugs, wrap them in red paper, and stuff them in the cracks of the bed. Because bedbugs can give birth to nine offspring in one night, it is meant to be a good omen. I wonder if this is true? I have asked several friends from Suzhou, and they all say: there is absolutely no such thing.

In the special supplement of this newspaper on the 15th of last month, there was an article entitled "The Bedbug Extermination Movement": it said, "It is unknown whether there are bedbugs in foreign countries. But from the fact that the Japanese call bedbugs 'Nanjing bugs,' it seems that bedbugs are unique to China." etc. According to my understanding, bedbugs also exist in foreign countries. The "Morning Light" column of the "Morning Post" recently published "European Travel Diary." It said: "In a certain large hotel in Moscow, there are many bedbugs, and one cannot sleep peacefully all night." This shows that bedbugs are not unique to China. However, foreigners are good at concealing their shortcomings, unlike Chinese people who easily show their ugliness. Therefore, there are no elegant names such as "Moscow bugs."

Record of Drifting Fragrance of Royal Incense 145

— Originally written by Princess Deling of Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

This is truly a very serious and shocking report! Although I was standing behind a curtain behind the Empress Dowager's throne, unable to see her face, I clearly saw her back suddenly flinch. From this, I could surmise that Her Old Highness must have felt quite stimulated after hearing this report. I myself paid even more attention to this matter because the Guangdong Governor-General so accused was an old friend of my father's. Although I had not read the accusations against him carefully, I knew a few of them. It seemed that this person had been too autocratic in Guangdong and had neglected the suffering and public opinion of the people he was supposed to govern, to the point that the people resented him bitterly. They privately organized and came to Beijing to file official complaints, this being the fourteenth or fifteenth time, including this last one. The charges against him were very specific, and I still vaguely remember a few:

First charge: Embezzling public funds;

Second charge: Forcibly robbing wealthy merchants in Guangzhou and extorting money;

Third charge: Openly feasting in restaurants and eateries in the market, unbecoming of an official;

Fourth charge: Using violence to force virtuous women from good families in the province to become concubines;

Fifth charge: On one occasion, while patrolling outside the city, an elderly beggar did not avoid the procession and suddenly crossed its path, causing the Governor-General to

Indulge his servants in brutally beating the beggar with whips, who died on the spot;

Sixth charge: Privately hoarding gifts presented to the Empress Dowager from various regions. (371)

He calmly replied with a smile: This matter is easy to resolve. As the saying goes, "Hold this office, perform this rite." Personal Vignettes

Mourning Fragments of Autumn 147

— Wu Jiren

Regarding the passing of my leader, Mr. Zheng Zhengqiu, various newspapers have already tirelessly reported on his virtuous conduct and great virtue. Now that the coffin is sealed, it is concluded that Mr. Zhengqiu was a "good old man". If destiny indeed held sway over lifespan, then it's as if Heaven is jealous of good people?

I stepped into the film industry in 1927. Since the position I held was very humble, Mr. Zhengqiu, with the respect of an Assistant Manager, uniquely promoted and took care of me, even encouraging me earnestly. It appeared that he had high hopes for me, but alas, I am ashamed to say that, "all my peers who were students were not cheap (successful)". Haven’t I remained the same as before? Thinking about it now, I have failed Mr. Zhengqiu's kindness. I myself have not made much progress.

Two years ago, at the passing of my teacher, Mr. Wang Meiqu, I wrote a long eulogy. It is pitiful to say that soon after mourning a guiding teacher who had given much instruction, Mr. Zhengqiu, who was considered a lifelong confidant, passed away after a sudden illness of four or five days. Years of mourning mothers and teachers, one after another, I was born at an unfortunate time, my fate is ill-fated, and it is both shocking and heartbreaking to talk about it.

Over these years, Mr. Zhengqiu often entrusted me with literary matters, so I often went to his residence to serve him. I benefited greatly from discussing principles and doctrines with him, and he also told me much about his history.

... "During the peak period of the 'Minli Daily' in the late Qing Dynasty, because I liked to write articles from a young age, I submitted them to various newspapers. Suddenly, one day, Mr. Yu Youren called me in for a conversation and entrusted me with the responsibility of editing the local edition of the Minli Daily. From then on, I embarked on the path of journalism. Later, I wrote theater reviews for 'Lili Place,' which gained the trust of a wide readership. The management then invited me to compile a special drama section, and thus I embarked on the theater ladder because of my interest in amateur opera. From reviewing dramas to performing in them, and then from performing in Peking Opera to crossing into the world of spoken drama, I felt that the power of spoken drama was more universal than Peking Opera, able to penetrate people's hearts, so it could be used to promote culture, advocate revolution, and achieve far-reaching results. Therefore, even though I spent a large part of my family fortune to save spoken drama from extinction, I actually 'destroyed my family to alleviate the national crisis' and revitalize the drama. During Yuan Shikai's reign, I was arrested in Hankou for performing revolutionary dramas. I have always adhered to the principles of the late Premier Sun Yat-sen, but it is unbelievable that I have never joined the party to this day. After performing in spoken dramas for several years, younger generations who followed my style were willing to become my students, numbering over a thousand. As cinema flourished, I gave up my life as a performer and dedicated myself to the positions of screenwriter and director." ...

It can be seen that Mr. Zhengqiu's moral character and writings were highly respected. As for Mr. Zhengqiu's writing, although it cannot be confined to rules and regulations, with a kind of overflowing talent and a clever mind, not to mention that no one can compare with him, even experienced teachers and scholars would sigh in inferiority and dare not compete with him. Mr. Zhengqiu's thoughts were indeed unique. In terms of qualifications, he would shame gilded PhDs, but he never even went to any school. His clear mind is something that people cannot match.

Mr. Zhengqiu liked the art of raising goldfish. When he had time, he would often go to see the dozen or so tanks of goldfish raised by Little Qiu. For years, he had been eager for a grandson. In the New Year, he happily welcomed a grandson, and he enjoyed the joy of being with grandchildren. His mother was still alive, and Mr. Zhengqiu was very filial to her. Four generations lived together in harmony and happiness.

Mr. Zhengqiu's health was originally weak, and this summer he seemed to be doing well. However, he had suffered from insomnia for a long time. Last month, many fish-raising comrades established a "Chinese Art Fish Society," and Mr. Zhengqiu was also one of the founders. On the evening of the 10th, a comrades' dinner was held at Guanshengyuan. Mr. Zhengqiu, along with Wen Lang and Little Qiu, happily attended. After the meal, he and Mr. Zhu Dake and I discussed the matter of re-establishing a fish garden, and we wanted to restore the "fish enjoyment" proposal. Mr. Zhengqiu took the sole responsibility for raising a large amount of money to promote this group. Who would have known that upon returning home, he would have incessant diarrhea, followed by vomiting? On the 12th, Mr. Chen Youchen and I went to Suzhou. The next evening, Mr. Zhengqiu even entrusted us with purchasing two items from Suzhou, "Songzi Yunpian Cake" and "Fresh Lotus Seeds." How could I have known that when I arrived in Shanghai by train on the 14th, the news of Guang-sheng's death had already been brought by the tea servant! Hearing this shocking news, where could I find the "soul-returning incense"?

At Mr. Zhengqiu's funeral, the mourners numbered no less than three thousand people, and the general movie-loving audience must also remember the great contributions he left behind!

In the midst of grief, I present a couplet as a farewell, which reads:

Little grass is deeply cultivated, looking at each other as friends who have forgotten age.

Swimming fish are startled to lose water, who will privately mourn and lend a helping hand?

I felt it was appropriate and had it written out and sent. A lifetime of knowing each other and being appreciated, once forever separated, alas, alas. How sad.

Qingqi University President Issue Resolved: Liu Shichuan Traveling to Jinan from Beiping 157

First Inspect the Situation and Then Take Office

(Special Dispatch from Beiping) The issue of the president of Qingqi University in Shandong has not been resolved for a long time. After the board of directors recommended Liu Shichuan as president, Liu was modest for many months. Now he has finally agreed. Today (July 22nd) at 3:05 PM, he will take the Pinghu through train from Beiping to Jinan. Before leaving, he made the following statement to reporters: "I have been recommended by the board of directors of Qingqi University to be the president. Because I have been away from my alma mater for eighteen years, I am gradually unfamiliar with the situation there. However, due to the repeated invitations from the board of directors and the urging from alumni everywhere, I have no choice but to first go to Jinan to inspect the situation of the school. If my personal ability is sufficient, I will naturally be willing to serve my alma mater. However, my personal talent is limited, and if I cannot cope, there is nothing I can do."
