Annual Meeting of Six Academic Societies Scheduled for Next Month Starting on the 11th in Guilin 159

Discounted Fares for Boat and Train Travel to Guilin Confirmed

Members from Various Locations Scheduled to Depart for Guilin at the End of This Month

The Chinese Science Society, the Chinese Institute of Engineers, the Chinese Chemical Society, the Geographical Society of China, the Zoological Society of China, and the Botanical Society of China, six organizations in total, have scheduled a joint annual meeting to be held in Guilin starting on the 11th of next month. All arrangements for travel to Guilin, local hospitality, conference staff, schedule, etc., have been properly prepared. Members in Shanghai are also scheduled to depart at the end of the month. Details are as follows:

Travel to Guilin

There are three routes to Guilin: (1) Water route: A. Via sea through Hong Kong, Guangzhou, Sanshui, Wuzhou, Guixian to Nanning. B. From Shanghai through Hong Kong, Wuzhou, Guixian to Nanning. (2) Land route: From Hankou through Changsha, Yizhang, Lechang, Guangzhou, Sanshui, Wuzhou, Guixian to Nanning. Those traveling by water should depart from Shanghai on the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Hai Yuan Wheel on July 31, arriving in Hong Kong on the 4th, taking the Kowloon-Canton Railway on the 5th to Guangzhou, and then taking a train from Guangzhou to Sanshui on the 6th, and then take a Hong Kong-Wuzhou steamer to Wuzhou. Those traveling by land should gather in Hankou on August 2, and take a train from Wuchang on the 3rd to Changsha, then take a highway bus from Changsha to Yizhang and Lechang, and then transfer to a train to arrive in Guangzhou on August 5.

Discounted Boat and Train Fares

The preparatory committee has negotiated discounted fares with the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Minsheng Industrial Company, Dala Company, Changxing Company, and Jardine Matheson for participating members. Within the Guangxi province, the Guangxi Provincial Government will cover all expenses for members, including food, lodging, tours, travel, etc., upon presentation of the annual meeting badge.

Local Hospitality

(1) Hong Kong: After arriving in Hong Kong, members can inquire about all matters from Zeng Qixin, the president of Guangxi Bank, and Zhang Zhaotang, the vice president. Currency exchange can also be handled by the bank, and the China Travel Service will arrange ship connections. The Metropole Hotel and the New Asia Hotel have been designated as accommodations. (2) Guangzhou: After arriving in Guangzhou, inquiries about travel to Wuzhou can be made at the Fourth Group Army's office in Guangdong. (3) Wuzhou: Upon arrival in Wuzhou, everything will be taken care of by the reception staff. Subsequent activities will be the responsibility of the Wuzhou office. (4) Nanning: After arriving in Nanning, members will immediately register. The conference venue is the Provincial Government's Great Hall. Male members will stay in the newly built Provincial Government Staff Dormitory, and female members will stay in the building used by the Provincial Government to host foreign guests.

Tours

The tours for this joint annual meeting are slightly different from previous years. Because the meeting place is in Nanning, which is far from the tourist area of Guilin, the focus will be on meetings in Nanning. After the annual meeting is over, they will go to Liuzhou and Guilin for tours. All travel, food, and lodging from Nanning to Liuzhou and Guilin and back to Wuzhou will be provided by the Guangxi Provincial Government, with guides and hospitality.

Annual Meeting Staff

The staff of the joint annual meeting has been determined as follows: Honorary Chairman Huang Xuchu, Chairman of the Annual Meeting General Committee Lei Peihong, Secretary Ma Minghai, Committee Members Ma Junwu, Su Cheng, Li Yunhua, Deng Xiangyun, Qiu Junxie, Zou Enyong, Yang Xiaoshu, Fang Ziwei, Lu Zidao, Liu Xian, Qian Chongshu, He Bingsong, Wu Haoran, Shen Xiongqing, Committee on Papers Zhu Kezhen, Shen Yi, Hu Huanyong, Tang Yuanji, etc., Committee on Program Ren Hongjun, Weng Wenhao, Yun Zhen, Hu Gangfu, etc., Committee on Lectures Gu Yuxiu, Zhang Qiyun, etc., Hospitality Committee Kuai Youqin, Xie Wufan, etc., Social Committee Shen Yue, Wei Xin, etc.

Annual Meeting Schedule

The annual meeting schedule is as follows: August 11, from 10:00 AM, registration; August 12, 9:00 AM, opening ceremony of the annual meeting; 1:00 PM, Chinese Science Society business meeting; 5:00 PM, public lecture; 7:00 PM, banquet by the Guangxi Provincial Government; August 13, 9:00 AM, specialized paper presentations in groups; 1:00 PM, business meetings of the five societies of engineering, chemistry, zoology, botany, and geography; 5:00 PM, public lecture; 7:00 PM, banquet by the headquarters of the Fourth Group Army; August 14, 9:00 AM, general paper presentations and discussions; 2:00 PM, Chinese Science Society business meeting; 5:00 PM, public lecture; August 15, 9:00 AM, specialized paper presentations in groups; 2:00 PM, business meetings of the five societies of engineering, chemistry, zoology, botany, and geography; 5:00 PM, public lecture; 7:00 PM, annual meeting banquet; August 16, departure for Guilin for tours.

Berlin Chinese Art Exhibition Hosts Banquet for Liu Haisu 160

The Preparatory Committee of the Berlin Chinese Art Exhibition believes that representative Liu Haisu's trip to Europe to promote art has been highly respected by various countries and fields, and has had an unprecedentedly great and profound impact on the European academic community. His outstanding work has brought him great honor on his return to the East. All exhibits have been checked and returned to the Preparatory Office for distribution. All proceeds from the sold works will be periodically returned to Mr. Liu by the Preparatory Office through accountant Pan Xulun. All reports are ready. Yesterday, the Preparatory Committee held a banquet for Representative Liu on the eighth floor of the Cathay Hotel and asked him to report on the exhibition. The details are as follows:

Attendees

Cai Yuanpei, Li Shihui, Ye Gongchuo, Wu Tiecheng, Li Dachao, Wang Zhen, Huang Binhong, Qian Xinzhi, Pan Gongbi, Pan Xulun, Liu Haisu, Huang Binhong, Zhang Daqian, Wang Jiyuan, Wu Hufan, Xie Gongzhan, Zhang Ze, Wu Dongmai, Wang Geyi, Zheng Wuchang, Xu Zhengzi, Yan Kechang, Ma Chonggan, Xu Ze, Li Zikuan, Qian Cangshuo and dozens of others.

Cai Yuanpei Reports

The banquet started at 7:00 PM. Chairman Cai Yuanpei reported that Mr. Liu Haisu, representing our country to hold a Chinese modern art exhibition in Germany, has gained supreme glory and great success. After the exhibition in Berlin, it has attracted the attention of various countries. He has toured more than ten places in Europe, shaking the whole of Europe and making Europeans understand that our country's art is still constantly advancing, changing Europeans' previous misunderstandings. He has promoted art to various countries in other aspects, positioning himself as a representative of Oriental art. Our country did not pay attention to it before. After this art exhibition, the focus of Europeans has shifted. This is solid evidence of the strength of our national artists and the honor they have won. Thanks to Mr. Haisu's efforts and struggles, and without fear of hardship, there is this result. Such achievements and great spirit really make us admire and thank him. Our country has had many misfortunes in recent years, and we have not had time to pay attention to foreign cultural promotion, and we feel economic difficulties. After the Executive Yuan decided on this art exhibition, it also decided to allocate 45,000 yuan. The whole thing was accomplished by Mr. Ye YuFu's hard work. At the same time, Mr. Ye presided over all the affairs of the association in China without fear of hard work. We should express our gratitude to Mr. Ye. However, the funds allocated by the Executive Yuan are only for the Berlin exhibition in Germany. After the opening of the Berlin exhibition, all provinces in Germany and other countries warmly welcomed and requested continued exhibitions. Although the funds were allocated and subsidized by local governments or art academies, Mr. Liu's personal expenses for returning to Sichuan were all paid for by the proceeds from his sales and private loans. It seems that the government has achieved great success with a small amount of funds, which is really beyond our expectations. However, Mr. Liu's personal burden is too heavy, and we cannot fail to find a way to rescue him. Now that Mr. Liu has returned with honor, he has published a notice asking all the writers to take back all the unsold works from the Preparatory Office, and he has entrusted accountant Pan to return all the sold paintings. He is worthy of praise for his careful planning. Please raise your glasses to show our respect to Mr. Liu.

Liu Haisu Reports

Chairman Cai asked me to report on the European art exhibition. I have prepared a written outline of the general situation, which is recorded here. The success of my trip to Europe to exhibit paintings is due to the support of Mr. Cai, Mr. Ye, and all the members of the preparatory committee. At the same time, I have also received the assistance of my colleagues in the art world, who have contributed their transcendent and great works of art. As a result, Haisu is only serving the country, society, and all his comrades. On November 13, 1933, I hurried to Europe on the Italian ship Contifanter. On the evening of December 8, I arrived in Berlin. The German committee members Kou Meier, Kong Wei, and Laiteman, and the secretary Tan Zhuangfu and Zhang Jing in the Chinese Embassy in Germany, welcomed us and said that the German side had held several committee meetings and had urged China to come because the opening date was approaching. At that time, Mr. Kou made an appointment to hold a joint meeting of the executive committees of China and Germany at the Oriental Art Museum on the 13th. On the morning of the 13th, I attended the meeting with Mr. Zhang Zengji. The German committee members who attended were Klinboer, Kou Meier, Lin Chi, Kong Wei, and Laiteman, 11 people in total. Klinboer was the chairman. The chairman first gave a welcome speech and reported the opening date. It had been decided to open on January 13 and close on March 4. I thought the time was too short, and the various procedures and printed materials were not prepared in time. After repeated discussions, it was decided to open on January 20 and close on March 4. At that time, we opened the boxes together and checked the works. Everyone was very satisfied. However, the catalog was too simple. After a brief discussion, it was decided to rewrite it, and each painting should be marked with paper or silk core, the content of the poem, the year of production, and the author's address for viewers to study. Mr. Liu was also asked to write a long preface detailing the characteristics of Chinese books and the origin of various schools, which would be published at the beginning of the catalog. Starting on the 14th, he went to the Oriental Art Museum to work every day. At 5:00 PM on February 5, another joint meeting of the executive committees of China and Germany was held. The German side was attended by Shaer Wuklinboer, Amisdao Qukou Meier and more than ten other people. Shaer Wu, the president of the Oriental Art Society, chaired the meeting and decided on the following matters: (1) Please ask the Prussian Academy of Fine Arts to be responsible for sending letters to diplomatic corps, government offices, local governments, academic institutions and celebrities and reporters. (2) Invite reporters from various countries to visit on the 19th. (3) Opening day program. (4) 100,000 roadside advertisements, tram advertisements and subway advertisements, radio broadcasts, and train advertisements in Germany. At the same time, we will print a book of modern Chinese paintings, with an article on Chinese painting schools, and prepare to distribute it to German institutions and scholars at the meeting. After Haisu arrived in Germany, many reporters from various newspapers visited every day. Each newspaper published my talks and news about the art exhibition. The German government and the public paid great attention to this matter. At 10:00 AM on January 20, the Chinese Painting Exhibition officially opened at the Prussian Academy of Fine Arts on Paris Square in Berlin. The number of people attending that day was unprecedented for previous art exhibitions in various countries. The Germans called it the most magnificent spectacle of the modern European art scene. It is estimated that more than 3,500 people attended that day, including ambassadors from various countries, representatives from local governments, celebrities, scholars, and nobles. During the 45 days of the exhibition, there were 4,500 visitors every day. All German newspapers praised the exhibition, saying that the Chinese modern paintings were vivid and full of charm, and that they were a transcendent ideal world that could not be reached by all countries. The sensation was not only praised by the German government and the public, but also attracted the attention of European countries. Hamburg, Minxing, the Rhine provinces, the Netherlands, Switzerland, Czechoslovakia, France, Italy, Britain, and Poland all sent letters and telegrams one after another, inviting them to exhibit, and some sent people to Berlin to discuss with Su. The great impact and shock on Europeans can be imagined. Haisu asked the domestic government for instructions and was successively allowed. He then went to various places for touring exhibitions. However, all the expenses, including the Berlin exhibition, were allocated 35,000 marks by the Executive Yuan. According to the budget of the Preparatory Office, it was used up in Berlin. The exhibition expenses in other countries and regions were allocated and subsidized by local art academies or municipal governments. As for the two-year period, Haisu's personal travel expenses, in addition to the paintings, were all borrowed privately, and he is still heavily in debt. Although the country is in trouble, he has no complaints because of his volunteerism. Because Su has been thinking about promoting our country's art and science for more than 20 years, it is like shouting blindly in a dark room, but now he can see the light suddenly. He should use all his strength to complete his mission, so that our country's culture can shine among the stars, so that Europeans can change their prejudice that Qin has no one. He has completed his mission with one breath, so he does not care about hardships and dangers. As a result, he has been warmly welcomed wherever he has gone. This glorious deed still shines on the European continent and can be a great page in our country's cultural history. Until the day Haisu returned, the United States, Turkey, Austria, and Poland still sent telegrams of welcome. Su will send ten of his own works and a part of his friends' masterpieces to Mr. Jiang Chongya, a lecturer at the School of Oriental Studies at the University of London in England. In two years, he has held large-scale exhibitions in various countries up to 15 times, with hundreds of thousands of visitors, and has sold more than 100 works. The Berlin Academy of Fine Arts in Germany has also specially opened a Chinese modern painting hall to permanently display modern masterpieces of our country for scholars to study. This is also a pioneering work.

Huang Boqiao and Others Speak

Then Huang Boqiao, director of the two railways, spoke, briefly stating that he had a few major thoughts on the Berlin Chinese Painting Exhibition. Boqiao was ordered to go to Europe to inspect the road administration. Most of the countries he passed through were the places where Mr. Haisu exhibited his paintings. After I met Haisu in Paris last October, we went our separate ways. However, wherever I went, local government officials, scholars, celebrities, or diplomatic corps praised the success of the Chinese Painting Exhibition and gave Europeans a very deep and widespread impression of Haisu. I have been to Germany, the Netherlands, the Czech Republic, France, and Britain, and they all praised him. Then Pan Gongbi, Li Dachao, Xie Gongzhan and others spoke.

Great Mathematician Wu Zaiyuan Passes Away 162

Mathematical expert Mr. Wu Zaiyuan, from Wujin, Jiangsu, served as a professor at the Beijing Translation Academy, Tsinghua University, and other schools. In the first year of the Republic of China, he gathered comrades Zhu Xiangwan, Hu Dunfu, Ping Hailan, Cao Liangyuan, and others to found Datong University in Shanghai. For more than 20 years, he worked hard and spared no effort. Mr. Wu's contribution to Datong University's achievements today is not small. Mr. Wu was tireless in learning and teaching, and his students were all over the country. His morality and knowledge shook China and foreign countries. His writings were prolific, and the academic community regarded him as a standard. In recent years, he has been overly concerned and overworked, but he has never stopped his education and writing. In May of this year, his illness suddenly worsened, and he was admitted to the Sacred Heart Hospital for treatment. The medicine was ineffective, and he passed away at his residence in Shanghai at 10:30 AM on July 21, at the age of 51. Everyone who heard the news felt sad. His son, Xue Linjun, was sent to the United States by Tsinghua last summer to specialize in steel. His daughter, Xue Min, is proficient in both literature and mathematics and is currently a professor at Datong University.

The examination period and location in Shanghai are the same as those of Shanghai Jiaotong University, so all enrollment matters will be handled by Shanghai Jiaotong University. However, the examination questions will still be prepared by professors from Tangshan University. As for Beiping, this year's affairs will be handled by Professor Lin Si and Huang Shouheng, and the director of general affairs Hua Chengwen. The examination period is the same as that of Shanghai from July 28 to 31.

Again, Director Cai Huigang, Supervisor Yin Junzhi, Director Zhang Yagong, and others gave speeches in succession, describing Xu's hard work in rectifying education and his reluctance to leave. Later, Xu thanked everyone for their kindness and hoped to continue his efforts to complete the unfinished business and make Shishan education a unique feature. After the tea and snacks, the photo was taken and the meeting was dismissed.

Shen Bao Medical Weekly

Introducing Zhenjiang Rural Nurse School 169

— Yin Jinquan

Since ancient times, our country has been known as an agricultural nation, with farmers accounting for more than 85 percent of the population. Therefore, rural revitalization is an urgent matter for governance. Currently, in the slogans of most people, the bankruptcy of rural areas is often a concern. However, to solve this problem, it is necessary to first understand what the reasons are. These reasons are indeed too complex. From a health perspective, the lack of widespread rural health services is a major cause of rural bankruptcy. Therefore, we should actively build up health services. Now, to operate rural health services, many trained and hardworking individuals are needed. However, in our country, where health services are in their infancy, there is a real shortage of health personnel. Therefore, to save rural health services, it is necessary to cultivate a group of health personnel who grew up in rural areas (rural nurses) to be effective. In today's rural areas, plagued by poverty and disease and lacking scientific physicians, the establishment of such rural nurse schools is necessary for the improvement of health services and the future of new medicine. I will now briefly describe the general situation of Zhenjiang Rural Nurse School for the reference of those in our country who are concerned about rural health services:

In the autumn of the year before last, gentlemen such as Leng Yuqiu and Zhang Yiyun, due to the need to spread health services to rural areas and the fact that rural areas could not afford doctors, established the Rural Nurse School in the environment of a shortage of rural doctors. It was established within the Zhenjiang Hongren Hospital. After graduation, they were sent to areas lacking health knowledge, unable to afford doctors, to treat diseases, promote health education, and guide public health work to provide relief. Therefore, it was named the Rural Nurse School.

Because the school was being piloted, enrollment was limited to Zhenjiang County. The district chiefs of each district selected two outstanding individuals who grew up in the countryside, who were admitted to the school after passing the examination. They were afraid of recruiting a group of young masters who could not be used after training, so the most important thing in the recruitment examination was to have a spirit of hard work and endurance. Because those who grew up in the countryside know the situation and suffering of the countryside, they will be willing to work enthusiastically in the future.

The training method for rural nurses is: (1) Moral Education: The goal of moral education in the school is "diligence" and "thrift". Students are always asked to do what they should do, and they are always asked to save money wherever they can. They try their best to avoid urbanization so that they can serve the countryside after graduation. (2) Education: The teaching method of the school is to practice immediately after learning so that they can understand step by step. In the first academic year, they supplement general science, followed by half a year of study and half a year of practice so that they can apply what they have learned after graduation. The subjects taught are anatomy, physiology, bacteriology, dietetics, bandaging, nursing ethics, public health, general nursing, internal medicine nursing, surgical nursing, ophthalmology nursing, urology and obstetrics and gynecology nursing, dermatology nursing, pediatric nursing, psychiatric nursing, family nursing, Party doctrine, Chinese, mathematics, chemistry, physics, botany, zoology, foreign languages, etc. The books used for each subject are determined separately according to the needs of the actual situation.

The above is an overview of the school. If we think about it carefully, in this situation where health is in its infancy, scientific physicians are lacking and unwilling to go to the countryside, and farmers cannot find doctors to treat them, this kind of talent can really treat diseases and reduce the suffering of farmers. At the same time, it can popularize health education and make people believe in scientific medicine as a pioneer. I think rural nurses are very suitable for meeting the needs of rural health services.

Q&A on Common Disease Knowledge 170

— Cheng Hanzhang

(61) Neurogenic Intestinal Disorder and Mucous Colic

(Q) What is called neurogenic intestinal disorder?

(A) This is a disease in which there are no substantial changes in the intestinal tract, but intestinal symptoms such as colic or diarrhea occur for no reason. There are distinctions between sensory, motor, and secretory intestinal neuroses.

(Q) What is sensory intestinal neurosis like?

(A) Sensory intestinal neurosis is mostly a complication of intestinal spasms.

(Q) What phenomena occur?

(A) Patients suddenly develop hernias, which are often seen in lead poisoning. There are also attacks of colic, which are common in arteriosclerosis. There are also intestinal episodic pains, which are often encountered in spinal tuberculosis (syphilis).

(Q) What is motor intestinal neurosis like?

(A) In motor intestinal neurosis, the patient has intestinal peristaltic anxiety, especially in the non-intestinal part, which is found in neurotic individuals. There are also certain constipation, spasmodic intestinal obstruction, neurogenic diarrhea, and reflex diarrhea. This is seen in women or men with prostate disease. There are mental diarrheas and anal sphincter spasms. This is seen in anal fissures or hemorrhoids.

(Q) What is secretory intestinal neurosis like?

(A) Secretory intestinal neurosis is mucous colic, also known as membranous colic.

(Q) In what kind of constitution does mucous colic occur?

(A) Mucous colic mainly occurs in middle-aged neurotic individuals; it is more common in women.

(Q) What are the symptoms of mucous colic?

(A) When mucous colic occurs, mucus is excreted along with the stool. Some of this mucus is mixed with the stool, and some is excreted alone without colic. After the mucus is excreted, the colic disappears. It will definitely occur again after a few days or weeks.

(Q) What is the shape of this excreted mucus?

(A) The shape of this mucus is not fixed; the texture is transparent, mostly like a film. It often resembles a cast of the large intestine.

(Q) How long does this disease last?

(A) Very slow; the disease progresses and regresses, and treatment is very difficult.

(Q) Is there any danger to the life of a patient with mucous colic?

(A) There is no danger to life.

(Q) What is the treatment for neurogenic intestinal disorders?

(A) Usually, it is to rest, apply warm compresses to the abdomen, and take tonic and astringent medications internally.

(Q) What medicine should be taken when mucous colic occurs?

(A) Internally take belladonna extract, atropine, and other anesthetics.

(Q) How should the patient be treated when not experiencing an attack?

(A) Give food with less residue to prevent constipation. Do not use laxatives, only use oil enemas.

(Q) What other methods are there?

(A) Internally take sedatives such as bromine preparations and iodine preparations. Massage, galvanic therapy, and hydrotherapy can also be used. (End)

Foxglove Leaves and Heart Disease 171

— Dan Qi

Medical Story Five

Today, the medical community generally recognizes that foxglove leaves are a specific medicine for treating heart disease. How it came to be used as a medicine is an interesting and instructive story. In a beautiful booklet published in 1785, we find an early historical record of this story. The author of this booklet, named William Withering, was a medical doctor in Birmingham, England, with a natural perseverance and a sound mind.

In this booklet (titled: An Account of the Foxglove and Some of its Medicinal Uses: with Practical Remarks on Dropsy and Other Diseases), Withering detailed the origin of the use of foxglove leaves as a medicine. Foxglove is a summer herbaceous plant that grows in the cold and humid climates and soils of the solid parts. Withering had previously heard that an old woman in Shropshire could cure dropsy with a decoction of herbal tea. He really thought this was just an unreliable rumor that only the gullible would believe. Later, he personally saw a patient with dropsy, after all the doctors were helpless, cured by the old woman with a secret herbal tea, which aroused his determination to explore and experiment.

The story goes like this. The head of Brasenose College, Oxford, suffered from dropsy and consulted many doctors. They could not alleviate his symptoms, so his anxious family suggested asking the old woman from Shropshire to treat his illness. In a helpless situation, he drank a few bowls of the herbal tea given to him by the old woman. Sure enough, his dropsy completely subsided.

This is the visible fact that made Withering determined to explore. His first step was to obtain the prescription for the herbal tea. This was certainly not easy. The old woman made a living from this and would not reveal her secret. But Withering used all means - it is said that he bought it with heavy money - and finally got the prescription.

He found that the prescription contained a variety of herbs; based on his knowledge of medicine, he determined that the most important one was foxglove. He also tested whether the stem, leaves, or flowers of foxglove were more effective than its roots. The method of testing was, of course, to have patients take them separately. Based on the results of the experiment, he determined that foxglove leaves were the most effective part for treating dropsy. He continued to determine the distribution of the medicine and the steps for taking it. He said that when the patient's pulse became even and slow, or when the patient developed chest discomfort and nausea, the medicine could be stopped.

Let us distinguish the difference between Withering's knowledge and the knowledge of the old woman from Shropshire. Withering's contribution represents the second step in the progress of any medicinal knowledge. The old woman only knew that herbal tea made in a certain way was beneficial to the disease. She strictly adhered to a certain prescription passed down from her ancestors, without variation or experimentation. Withering did it this way. He found which herb was the most important in the prescription, which part of this herb was the most effective, what was the most appropriate amount of medicine to take, and what was the most appropriate step to take the medicine. In other words, he rationalized the use of this medicine. But his knowledge was still incomplete, he was not clear about the nature of the disease. He would never have thought that this medicine would act on the heart. He did not know the precise anatomy of the heart - at that time no one knew. This is not surprising because the complex microscopes applicable at that time had not yet been invented. Therefore, the theory that animal tissues are composed of cells, and that each cell has a certain chemical reaction, had not yet been conceived. The pharmacology of foxglove had to go through more than a hundred years of progress in medical knowledge to be fully understood.

So, what is the real situation of foxglove treating heart disease? The heartbeat is a contractile wave that begins at the top of the heart—the auricle—and moves down to the bottom—the ventricle. The track through which the wave passes is a small bundle of muscle and nerve tissue—called the "Bundle of His." When heart disease occurs, the auricle vibrates. The vibration of the auricle passes through the "Bundle of His" so quickly that the ventricles that are prepared to be driven out respond very irregularly and inflexibly. As a result, the amount of blood actually flowing is greatly reduced, and the blood accumulates in the blood vessels, which is the cause of dropsy. Foxglove leaves contain a chemical component. When the Bundle of His absorbs this chemical component, a chemical reaction occurs, which results in it not being affected by the vibration of the auricle, indirectly protecting the ventricles, making the pulse average again, and the blood moving again. Since the accumulated blood is circulating, the edema naturally subsides.

Common Sense of Ear, Nose, Throat and Eye Hygiene 172

— Tang Renjin

(56) Ozena (Continued)

(2) Formation of Crusts: Crusts often form in the nasal cavity of patients with this disease. These crusts are formed by the drying of purulent secretions. When we use a rhinoscope to examine the nasal cavity, we see that the nasal cavity is abnormally wide. Its walls are covered with dirty gray-white or greenish purulent crusts. The surface of the purulent crust is very dry and has a foul odor. If the purulent crust is removed, the atrophic and thin mucous membrane can be seen.

(3) Atrophy of the Nasal Mucosa: The mucosa of the nasal cavity is mostly atrophic and thin, and appears pale white, firmly attached to the bone, and not easily separated. The most obvious part of the atrophy is the inferior turbinate. At this time, if an anterior rhinoscopy is performed, it is easy to see the posterior wall of the nasopharynx from the front. This is because the mucosa of the turbinate has atrophied and thinned, and the nasal cavity is abnormally wide.

In addition, what can be noted in this disease is that the external shape of the nose is mostly flat. Patients often feel nasal congestion, loss of smell, headache, heavy head, indigestion, dry throat, listlessness, and lack of pleasure, etc.

Complications of this disease include dry pharyngitis, chronic catarrh, and suppurative otitis media. Sometimes it can be complicated by suppuration of the paranasal sinuses. Sometimes the inflammation can spread to the eye socket through the lacrimal duct.

Speaking of the treatment of ozena, the most important thing is (1) to find a way to eliminate the formation of crusts. (2) To make the foul odor of the secretions disappear. (3) To hope to cure the atrophy of the nasal mucosa and bone. But in fact, this is very difficult. (4) To explore the cause of this disease and treat it. (5) To enhance the nutrition of the whole body. (6) To treat the various symptoms that come with it. Therefore, its treatment can be divided into local treatment, causal treatment, and systemic treatment. Local treatments include nasal irrigation, Cott's cotton swab method, nasal mucosa vibration massage, quince solution application, medicinal powder insufflation, electrical analysis, congestion therapy, and submucosal paraffin injection, etc. Causal treatment must be performed after the pathogen has been identified. "Vaccine" therapy has recently been reported to be effective and can be tried. As for the most effective systemic treatment, it is the internal administration or injection of cod liver oil or vitamin preparations.

Popular Lecture on Modern Venereology (10) 173

— Chen Shengbai (Compiled) Yin Muqiang (Proofread)

Part 2 Gonorrhea

Clinically, the part from the external urethral opening to the posterior sphincter of the bulb is called the anterior urethra. The part from the membranous part, the prostatic part to the internal sphincter is called the posterior urethra.

2. Female Urethra and Vagina

A. Urethra: The female urethra is shallower, shorter, and straighter than the male urethra. Its structure is also simpler. However, on the posterior margin of the external urethral opening, there are usually two small tubes, the so-called Skene's glands. These small tubes are easily infected with early gonorrhea.

B. Vagina: Since the vagina is the place of intercourse, its clinical significance is more important than other parts. The vagina is an expandable tube, rich in folds. Its upper end embraces the cervix, and its lower end opens into the vulva, that is, the vaginal opening. On the left and right sides of the vaginal opening are the bulbs of the vestibule. This corresponds to the male corpus spongiosum. Around the vaginal opening are countless mucous glands, called the lesser vestibular glands. At the posterior end of the vestibular bulbs is the greater vestibular gland, that is, the Bartholin's gland.

The vagina is located behind the bladder and urethra, and in front of the rectum. It receives the vaginal part of the uterus and begins at the vaginal fornix. The anterior vaginal wall is tightly attached to the urethral wall, and their tissues are mutually fused. The posterior vaginal wall is closely attached to the anterior wall of the rectum. This is very different from the male urethra, because in men, the relationship between the urethra and the rectum does not present a fused state.

Chapter 5 General Course and Symptoms of Gonorrhea

Section 1 General Course of Gonorrhea

A. Progression of Gonorrhea

The course of gonorrhea can be divided into acute and chronic. Generally, two or three days after infection, the disease is limited to the superficial external urethral opening and its vicinity. At this time, the invasion of gonorrhea is only on the surface of the mucous membrane. After about two weeks, the disease progresses and reaches its peak. At this time, the lesion invades the deep part of the mucous membrane, and the number of gonorrhea is much more than in the initial stage. The course of acute gonococcal anterior urethritis - if treated immediately, the course is good, and the symptoms gradually disappear at the end of three or four weeks. However, commonly two or three weeks after the occurrence of anterior urethritis, it spreads to the posterior urethra, especially due to excessive movement, sexual intercourse, erection, spermatorrhea, the use of irritating foods, or the use of urethral probes, catheters, and careless injection of drugs by patients, which induces acute gonococcal posterior urethritis.

After the acute gonorrhea has passed, if the patient does not pay attention to health care, stops treatment, or the treatment is not appropriate, the bacteria will not be eliminated and the secretions will not be reduced. It will further invade the submucosa and related glands and nearby organs. At this time, the effect of drugs is very difficult. Therefore, in the long course, it may occur or stop. Especially due to labor, drinking, sexual intercourse, and other unhealthy habits, there may be recurring acute symptoms. As for invading the glands and nearby organs, causing paraurethritis, periurethral infiltration, Cowper's glanditis, prostatitis, seminal vesiculitis, epididymitis, cystitis, pyelitis, etc., there are too many to list. In women, due to anatomical and physiological relationships, there are more occurrences of Skene's glanditis and Bartholin's glanditis, and proctitis.

Moreover, it is said that gonorrhea can also be transferred to distant places through blood or lymph, causing gonococcal inflammation. The most common is the joints, followed by the tendon sheath. Other possible transfers include the endocardium, bones, muscles, nerves, middle ear, peritoneum, pleura, and pericardium.

Medical Treatment for Pain Relief (24) 174

— Li Xing

Cancer Pain

In European and American countries with advanced science, due to the widespread use of scientific medicine and the improvement of public health administration, the general mortality rate has been significantly reduced. For example, tuberculosis, which accounts for the highest mortality rate, has dropped to a low ranking. Cholera, the most terrible of acute infectious diseases, is now almost extinct. The author has never seen or heard of a case of cholera in more than seven years of traveling in the United States. Furthermore, typhoid fever, which has a very high mortality rate, has now been reduced by more than 95%. The rest, such as direct infectious diseases and infant mortality, have also been reduced to a very low level. The greatness of the efficacy of scientific medicine is really amazing, and its benefits to the people cannot be considered small.

The age of the people is inversely proportional to the mortality rate, that is, a high mortality rate means a low life expectancy for the people, and a low mortality rate means a high life expectancy for the people. In the most developed European and American countries with scientific medicine, the average life expectancy of the people has reached more than 50 years, which is more than twice the average life expectancy of the people in our country. As a result of the increase in the age of the people, there is also a kind of mortality rate that is rapidly increasing, which is terrible, and scientific medicine has almost lost its effectiveness. What is this disease? It is cancer (various cancers and malignant tumors). Various cancers are directly proportional to the age of the people, that is, the more elderly people there are, the more people who develop cancer, so cancer is the great enemy of the elderly. How can it be said that scientific medicine has almost lost its use for this frequent disease? Its meaning is that various cancers can cause the death of the patient. Except for the early stages of cancer, which can be saved, scientific medicine is completely powerless to save the rest, which are slightly later. Therefore, once a person suffers from cancer and enters a more serious state, it is equivalent to a death sentence, and doctors all over the world are completely helpless. At present, countries around the world spend large sums of money every year to study methods to save late-stage cancers, but no significant results have been seen. As for whether it will be completely successful in the future, no one can say. The causes of cancer are still not very clear and must continue to be studied.

Cancers are divided into two major categories. The first category, which accounts for the largest part, is carcinoma, and the smaller part is sarcoma. The most common parts of the body to develop cancer are: stomach, women's breasts, uterus, cervix, ovaries, male and female large intestine, rectum, face, etc. The methods of treating cancer now are: early-stage cancers can be cut off, or treated with radium, or electrocauterized, or irradiated with X-rays, and there is assurance that they can be cured. There is no assurance that more severe cancers can be treated with the above methods. Late-stage cancers cannot be saved because they can spread to other parts of the body. The danger of cancer is due to its metastatic nature.

Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (60) 175

— Hu Jiayan

Section 6 Renal Tuberculosis

The prognosis of this disease is very difficult to predict decisively; but it is not absolutely bad, as previously expected. There is also no way to deal with the ulcerated state. Sometimes, due to artificial pneumothorax surgery, the reduction of cough and sputum, and throat diseases, a turning point towards recovery may occur. As for the pulmonary tuberculosis itself, how far has it progressed? The general state of the patient, etc., are closely related to the prognosis of this disease.

In addition to laryngeal tuberculosis, nasal tuberculosis can also be seen from time to time; however, it is far less numerous than the former! Since its symptoms are not very many, and there is no special treatment that can be proposed, it will not be discussed here.

Renal tuberculosis is a type of local tuberculosis, a venereal disease. It mostly occurs after pulmonary tuberculosis. The origin of its formation is due to the spread from the vascular system. This situation has already been described in Chapter 4 above! In the kidney, it initially develops caseous lesions, which are mostly limited to a part of the kidney. If this caseous lesion collapses, it can also form a cavity state, just like the situation in the lungs. In addition, it is possible for connective tissue to develop around the lesion, resulting in a healed state, and calcareous sclerosis. Sometimes, it even causes complete obstruction of the urethra.

Economic Supplement

An Analysis of Chinese Disasters and Famines 176

I. A Few Heartbreaking Words Before the Discussion

The bankruptcy of the agricultural economy has become widespread in China, and no province can escape this whirlpool. In some places, increased grain harvests and small consumer markets have led to the phenomenon of "cheap grain hurting farmers." In other places, crop failures have led to soaring grain prices, resulting in unprecedented grain shortages. In still other places, there have been no harvests for several years, and tens of millions of farmers live a life of displacement, teetering between life and death. Therefore, the collapse of China's agricultural economy is a fact, whether in the "wealthiest in the world" Zhejiang and Guangdong, or in Shanxi and Gansu, where "bumper years do not provide warmth and sustenance." It has probably reached the end of its rope.

It must be understood that the causes of these phenomena, which have led to the bankruptcy of China's rural areas, can be traced back to the following three points:

(1) The insatiable, cruel exploitation and oppression of international imperialism;

(2) The various forms of exploitation and harm by domestic feudal forces;

(3) The serious threat and destruction of natural disasters.

The first two points will not be discussed for the time being. In this year of loudly proclaiming "reviving the countryside" and "relieving the countryside," news of natural disasters, one of the fatal wounds mentioned above, is also pouring in from various provinces and counties. Flooding from the Yangtze River has already begun to attack Shashi, Hankou, and the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. The recent few days of sunny weather have slightly eased its threat. However, there are already talks of a flood like the one in the twentieth year of the Republic of China [1931]. As for the provinces of North China, such as Hebei, Shandong, and Shanxi, they will still not escape flooding this year. The Yellow River has once again breached its banks, and the water from the breach is said to be threatening to divert its course and seize the Huai River. The provinces of Zhejiang, Fujian, Guangdong, and Guangxi have all suffered considerable flood damage. It can be said that last year was a year of great drought, and this year is a year of great floods. With such recurring droughts and floods, it is easy to understand how China's agricultural economy is accelerating its bankruptcy.

The above is considered the introduction to this article.

II. Let's Look at the "Land of Famine"

Speaking of China's disasters and famines, it has a very long history.

Originally, someone said that China is a "Land of Famine." According to the "Tongzhi" and "Xu Tongzhi," from the year of Duke Huan of Lu in the Spring and Autumn period to the fourteenth year of Chongzhen at the end of the Ming Dynasty, just considering floods and droughts alone, there were more than 1,323 incidents. And the occurrences happening several times in a year were not calculated. In addition, disasters such as locust plagues, windstorms, hailstorms, insect plagues, earthquakes, and various other disasters were not included. If they were included, the number would be even more staggering. In the 264 years of the Qing Dynasty, there were disasters and famines every year: from the third year of Shunzhi (1644) to the third year of Xuantong (1911), an average of about 60 counties were affected each year, accounting for 3.73% of the counties in the eighteen provinces of the country (according to the eighteen provinces, there are a total of 1,607 counties). According to the book "China, Land of Famine" by Walter Mallory, he created a table based on the scope of each famine. This table is based on historical materials written by Chinese people. According to his statistics, from 620 BC to 1900 AD, there were a total of 1,506 disasters in China that encompassed entire provinces. Therefore, China can be called a "Land of Famine."

There are records upon records in history, which we will not elaborate on. Let's just talk about the facts of recent years. However, in recent years – now when China's economy is totally bankrupt – isn't every year a struggle under the disasters and famines? If we talk about the types of disasters and famines, there are floods, droughts, rice borers, locusts, wild beasts, field mice, frost, hail, earthquakes, landslides, plagues, and large fires. If we talk about the scope of disasters and famines, they span more than twenty-five provinces. If we talk about the severity of the disasters and famines, the most severe was the drought in the Northwest from the 17th to the 20th years of the Republic of China [1928-1931], where the land was barren for over a thousand miles, with tens of thousands dying. Starving corpses littered the roads, and villages were empty. The floods in sixteen provinces in the 20th year of the Republic of China [1931], in the area of the Yangtze and Huai rivers, many people, livestock, and houses were submerged, and much land was washed away, causing the local vitality to be difficult to recover even after a long period of time. According to the investigation and summary of the disaster situation by the Relief Committee from the 17th to the 20th years of the Republic of China [1928-1931]: In the 17th year of the Republic of China [1928], 203 counties across the country were affected, compared to 1,936 counties in the country, accounting for 10.4%. In the 18th year of the Republic of China [1929], the number of affected counties suddenly increased to 841. In the 20th year of the Republic of China [1931], there were 519 affected counties. The 21st year of the Republic of China [1932] can be said to be a year with lighter disasters, but there were floods in provinces such as Jilin, Heilongjiang, Shanxi, and Yunnan, years of water, drought, wind, and hail disasters in Shaanxi, and breaches in the rivers of Hebei, and water followed by drought in Jiangxi. As many as seven provinces suffered from disasters and famines. Among them, the four provinces of Jilin, Heilongjiang, Shanxi, and Shaanxi were more severely affected. According to the survey report of the South Manchuria Railway Company, 80% of the cultivated land in Jilin and Heilongjiang provinces was completely submerged by floods, and the loss of agricultural products accounted for more than 70% of the total annual harvest. Sixty-eight counties in Shanxi suffered from floods, and more than ninety counties in Shaanxi suffered from ice, hail, and wind disasters, but statistics on the losses are lacking. As for the disasters and famines in the 22nd year of the Republic of China [1933], although the extent of the disaster area and the severity of the disaster were not as severe as the great flood in the 20th year of the Republic of China [1931], the locust plague alone was a very serious disaster. According to the report of the Shen Bao Yearbook: the disasters and famines in the 22nd year of the Republic of China [1933] shook the country. In Henan, Shandong, Hebei, and Jiangsu, there were more than 53 counties affected by the Yellow River flood. Other disasters include floods in Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, Hebei, and Guizhou (excluding the Yellow River flood); banditry in Hunan, Henan, Shaanxi, Hubei, Gansu, Jiangxi, Fujian, Sichuan, and Qinghai; windstorms in Henan, Shaanxi, Anhui, and Guizhou; hailstorms in Henan, Shaanxi, Anhui, Guizhou, and Jiangsu; frost damage in Henan and Shaanxi; and other disasters such as earthquakes and rat plagues also affected various provinces in Shaanxi and Gansu. The locust plague in the 22nd year of the Republic of China [1933] covered as many as ten provinces, and if calculated by county, there were as many as 231 counties. In total, in the 22nd year of the Republic of China [1933], 476 counties across the country were affected by various disasters. In a nutshell, the entire China is under the threat of disasters and famines. If we add the various exploitative relationships of imperialism and feudal forces, it will further increase the persecution of peasants by natural forces. If we do not obliterate the facts, we will certainly see tens of millions of farmers and women, as well as their sick and elderly parents and young children, struggling on the line of death with miserable wails, desperate cries, howls, and hungry cries! The past was like this, the present is like this, can the future not be like this?

III. A Glimpse of the Disasters and Famines of Last Year

The previous disasters and famines were like this, let's look at the most recent year! The 23rd year of the Republic of China [1934]! Regarding the statistics on drought, according to the recent agricultural information reports of the Central Agricultural Experiment Station of the Ministry of Industry (Issues 9-11 of the second year), the disaster-stricken provinces and fields can be extracted as follows: (Unit: 1,000 acres)

IV. A Picture of Disaster Victims

In short, these facts are all reflections of the bankruptcy of the rural economy. If we do not obliterate these facts, we should witness all kinds of facts such as "starving captives filling the roads" and "people eating each other in hunger, more than half of whom die"!

Here, we can introduce a picture of tens of millions of people in miserable desperate cries, howls, and starvation. According to the Relief Committee's investigation of fourteen provinces including Henan, Jiangsu, and Guangdong, the total number of disaster victims displaced by natural and man-made disasters reached as many as 65,665,170 people. A Simple Explanation of Traditional Bookkeeping 177

— Wang Hongjing

I. Introduction

Bookkeeping is the recording of the inflow and outflow of goods or money, clarifying assets, liabilities, and thoroughly calculating profits and losses. Therefore, regardless of whether the style is new or old, and no matter the difference between Chinese and Western methods, simplicity and clarity are paramount. Only clarity can minimize errors and prevent fraud; only simplicity can facilitate verification and save labor. This matter seems easy at first glance, but it is actually difficult to master. Beginners, if they do not have a solid foundation in arithmetic and abacus, will not be able to fully understand it. If they only know the superficial aspects—merely imitating without understanding the underlying principles—they will be controlled by the bookkeeping system instead of controlling it. Consequently, there are cases where businesses suffer losses, so caution is necessary.

II. Categories

Western bookkeeping is divided into single-entry and double-entry systems. Traditional bookkeeping does not have specific names. For the sake of easy narration and clarity, the simplest and clearest traditional method is temporarily named the "Dragon Gate Four-Column Method." "Dragon Gate" refers to the four items in a daily cash flow statement: original balance, total receipts, total disbursements, and actual balance. The actual balance should correspond exactly to the cash on hand. (If there are rounding errors, they should be recorded separately.) "Four-Column" refers to the four items used to clarify profits and losses by categorizing assets and liabilities into: old accounts, new receipts, disposals, and actual assets. "Old accounts" include capital and liabilities. "New receipts" include profits and income. "Disposals" include losses, daily expenses, and miscellaneous items. "Actual assets" include debts owed to the business, cash on hand, inventory, and advances. To ensure thorough auditing and clarity and to prevent financial difficulties, the "old accounts" and "actual assets" should be further categorized. The "old accounts" can be divided into "external debts" and "internal debts." "Internal debts" include capital, public bonds for business protection, or temporary or fixed deposits from eastern and western business partners. "External debts" include temporary transactions or fixed-term loans. "Actual assets" are also divided into "internal debts" and "external debts." "Internal debts" include expenses from eastern and western business partners, inventory, and advances. "External debts" include debts owed by customers, temporary or fixed-term loans. In essence, although "old accounts" and "actual assets" are divided into several categories, the urgency of payments and collections, the likelihood of bad debts, all vary depending on the situation, the individual, and must be flexibly handled by the individual. For the sake of clarity, a table is provided below:

The division of deposits into four columns corresponds well with the Western-style balance sheet and profit and loss statement. A comparative table of Chinese and Western account settlements is proposed below:

III. System

(A) Main System: The source of bookkeeping is the "cash flow." Cash flow can be divided into several types: cash flow, goods flow, futures flow, and transfer flow. During busy times, goods flow can be further divided based on wholesale and retail, such as "wholesale goods flow," "retail goods flow," or "retail sales flow," "wholesale goods flow." Cash flow can vary depending on the currency type, such as in Dalian, where merchants may have "banknote flow," "silver note flow," and "small silver coin flow." Relationships arising from cash flow are called "transactions." All debit and credit relationships are recorded in "transaction accounts," which can be further divided into "bank transaction accounts," "customer transaction accounts," and "loan transaction accounts." In short, the complexity of the matter, the number of different account books, and the names all vary depending on the situation, the location, and customs, and cannot be uniform. "Old accounts" are used to record the business's trading goods. Broadly speaking, they can be divided into "spot goods old accounts," "futures goods old accounts," "retail old accounts," "manufacturing old accounts," and "exchange old accounts." The names also vary depending on the location and customs, and are not consistent. "Miscellaneous accounts" record the business's expenditures, daily expenses, public expenses, rent, etc., and are commonly referred to as "expense accounts."

(B) Auxiliary System: Includes documents retained for reference, communication records, entertainment records, employee directories, and guarantee registers. The specific titles depend on the complexity of the matter and the number of accounts. In short, ensure that nothing is omitted due to complexity and that unnecessary non-productive staff are not hired for the sake of detail. This is the key.

IV. Usage

(A) Transcription: All receipts and payments, inflows and outflows of goods, are first recorded in the cash flow. Then, the transcription clerk classifies and transcribes them into the transaction accounts or old accounts. After each transcription, the supervising clerk places a dot on the upper right shoulder of the item's name in the cash flow. In the cash flow, the words "receipt" and "payment" are used to indicate the action. In the transaction accounts or old accounts, the words "coming" and "going" are used, with the month and day written above. The month does not need to be repeated in the same month, and the word "again" is used for the same day. However, if on separate pages, the month and day should be written again for clarity. Busy businesses often transcribe transaction accounts first based on documents and mark the documents with a sign. The cash flow clerk then makes entries based on the documents, and the supervising clerk adds the dot. Small quantities are annotated in detail to the right of the currency name.

(B) Reconciliation: Reconciliation is performed by someone who is not a bookkeeper, such as a bright apprentice, to provide the bookkeeper with rest, to provide a fresh perspective that can easily spot errors, to prevent fraud, and to provide the apprentice with an opportunity to learn accounting. Sometimes, the chief accountant—also known as the general ledger desk or executive—performs this task to show seriousness and prevent fraud. The method uses two stamps: "transcribed" and "reconciled." The person holding the cash flow holds the "transcribed" stamp and calls out, and the person holding the transaction account or old account holds the "reconciled" stamp and acknowledges. After matching, the "transcribed" stamp is placed on the "receipt" or "payment" entry, and the "reconciled" stamp is placed on the month and day of the "coming" or "going" entry.

(C) Account Roots: "Account root" in Shanghai dialect, also called "account file," means setting up a separate account for each transaction partner. For external transactions, account roots are set up by port, categorizing similar transactions together for easier inspection. For example, if there are both out-of-town and local transactions, local transactions should be categorized into Chinese and foreign businesses, with foreign businesses and Chinese businesses listed together in close proximity. For out-of-town transactions from Qingdao, Yantai, and Tianjin, the merchants from each port should be grouped together in close proximity for ease of inspection. Furthermore, if the same business has both fixed deposits and overdraft transactions, separate account roots should be established based on the nature of the transactions. Another example is when a customer commissions many shipments of goods, and the miscellaneous expenses are all recorded in the transaction account, which becomes cumbersome and unclear. A separate account should be set up for each customer, with a separate root for each transaction. After the transaction is completed, it is transferred to the transaction account, making it easier to calculate expenses and making the transaction account clearer. Conversely, large-scale sales of goods within the business should also have separate roots, and the principle is the same as described above. If retail sales within the business are recorded in a single root, it will be messy and unclear, making it impossible to determine profits and losses. Setting up separate roots for each item would be too tedious due to the large variety of goods. The best way is to categorize by type, not by category. For example, different brands of flour such as "Red Sun Dangtian" and "Yuan Bingchuan" can be combined into one root, while different brands of coarse cloth such as "Shepherd Boy" and "Great Wall" can also be combined into one root. For clarity, the best way is to number each transaction. When selling, indicate the purchase number on the month and day of the sale, and next to the purchase number, note how many pieces of a particular number have been sold. When the goods are sold out, the notes should match the purchase quantity.

(D) Closing Accounts: (1) For cash flow accounts: Cash flow is divided into four items: original balance, total receipts, total disbursements, and actual balance. The actual balance must match the cash on hand. If there is an error, such as a missing entry, it should be added. If there is an incorrect entry, it should be matched with the corresponding debit and credit entries before the account can be changed. Remember, remember. Only after the actual balance matches the cash on hand should the account be closed. The date of the next day is then written after it to prevent omissions. (2) For transaction accounts or old accounts, except for immediate cash transactions, which are reconciled and balanced by the end of each month by totaling the debit and credit amounts and writing the total under the month and day, all other accounts with balances, whether debit or credit, should be settled before clearing. The last balance should be listed in the debit or credit balance. In old accounts, the common practice is to use money as the debit and credit, and the goods are attached. Therefore, when closing the account, in addition to indicating the monetary balance, the quantity of goods in stock should also be noted to match the actual inventory. It is best to indicate the average price of the remaining goods. If the payment and the goods are recorded separately, they should be settled and accounted for separately.

(E) Documents: (1) Purchase orders and loan agreements vary depending on the location and customs. There should be written rules to follow. The key is to be clear and unambiguous. (2) Documents related to cash flow and transaction accounts include invoices, transaction statements, cost sheets, and interest statements. In addition to detailed annotations in cash flow and transaction accounts or old accounts, annotations on documents should be concise.

(F) Auditing: The word "auditing" is difficult to describe. For example, large and small errors should be divided by nine, and debit and credit errors should be divided by two.

V. Conclusion

(A) Hiring Bookkeepers: Bookkeepers are entrusted with the responsibility of accurately recording assets, liabilities, and thoroughly calculating profits and losses. Therefore, the selection and training of bookkeepers must be prudent. A quiet and honest person may be easy to direct, but a dull person will not be able to offer advice or contribute. A lively and intelligent person, with spare energy and the ability to contribute, may not be content with a mechanical life. Therefore, they may be suppressed or promoted. It depends on the person in charge to weigh the options. Cultivating talent within the business is not an easy task. However, constantly hiring dull or elderly people with no ambitions as bookkeepers, without rotation, stifles their intelligence, weakens their bodies, and, except for the benefit of obedience, their lack of assistance and contribution can result in losses that outweigh the gains. Moreover, what about those who are not benevolent? When first learning business, it is best to work as a bookkeeper for a short time to understand the business's overall situation. Afterwards, they should be assigned to other positions to learn various aspects, so that when they take on important positions, they will not be limited to social skills and unfamiliar with accounting, resulting in inaccurate calculations. This would be ideal.

(B) Supervising Bookkeepers: As the saying goes, "Use people without suspicion, and if you suspect them, don't use them." This is true. However, even if you use people without suspicion, supervision is essential. Reviewing accounts, counting cash, and checking securities and contracts should be done regularly. Do not use trickery or intelligence against employees. In short, being weak is not acceptable, but arrogance is useless. One must win them over with kindness and restrain them with authority. Even difficult individuals will then comply.

(C) The Qualities a Bookkeeper Should Possess: As mentioned above, bookkeepers have heavy responsibilities and important missions. Therefore, the qualities that a bookkeeper should possess are also essential. In their spare time, they should read books and newspapers to increase their knowledge, communicate with field staff to understand market conditions, exercise to reduce weight, and laugh to aid digestion. They should not be content with fulfilling their duties but should learn and ask questions to have opportunities for promotion. In short, for the sake of career advancement, being a bookkeeper can be temporary, but not permanent. When working, they should not complain about the heavy workload and little credit. When supervising bookkeepers, they should be considerate. The capacity for tolerance varies from person to person, but one should strive to be magnanimous. Furthermore, how to maintain integrity to gain the trust of others, how to be loyal when under the command of others, how to be open and fair when commanding subordinates are all things that cannot be fully described in writing. One must cultivate these qualities in ordinary times to be able to handle situations with ease. The world's customs are no longer what they used to be, and the way of friendship is declining. In both the north and south, the number of people who can work together in harmony and cooperate to build a business is decreasing, leading to the increasing formation of family businesses, which is not a good sign. In family businesses, parents and siblings often spoil their children and fail to discipline them properly. Children also become lazy and unmotivated because they rely on their families. This is not as good as the strict supervision and intensive work of non-family businesses, where there are fewer opportunities for fraud. Therefore, when studying business, one should stay away from parents and siblings to develop themselves. When running a business, one should use more outside talent to avoid bias in rewards and punishments based on personal feelings, and to utilize talent from all regions. However, what is being discussed here is already beyond the scope of bookkeeping.

Cotton Yarn: Overseas Cotton Markets Decline Across the Board 180

Yesterday, US cotton opened lower due to poor news from Liverpool, with widespread selling. Spot traders sold short distant months, and concerns about cotton harvest management and the Senate's slight changes to the Cotton Industry Reorganization Amendment, as well as the Texas court's injunction against the collection of the ginning tax set by Pankhaise, all unsettled the market. Local companies and other industry players bought in slightly during the price declines, but the effect was minimal. As a result, spot cotton fell by 10 points, and futures fell by 11 to 19 points. English cotton spot fell 9 points, and futures fell 8 to 10 points. Indian cotton initially weakened due to long position liquidations but recovered later due to short covering and slight purchases by European exporters.
