Free Talk

Review of "Nora's" Acting 183

— You Na

Having just left the hospital and unable to walk, two residents supported me and dragged me to the Jincheng Grand Theater. There, some friends dragged and pulled me up to the fourth-floor dressing room, where the leading actors all shook hands with me.

This time, I came specifically to see their acting, especially to appreciate Lan Ping, who had left a deep impression on me. After seeing it, I wanted to write some thoughts, but I was too sick to hold a pen. Until a few days ago, I was still leaning on crutches, limping and hobbling to the Carlton to see "Hero and Beauty." I was very satisfied and wanted to express some opinions, but my illness prevented me. Gradually, I saw various positive reviews of these two performances in the newspapers, which made me unable to resist saying a few words.

Mr. Zhou Da, in the Da Mei Evening News, commented on "Nora" and said: "…Especially each actor can accurately express the personality of the characters in the play… The acting level of this performance is catching up with the highest level of international acting art." I feel that Mr. Zhou's criticism is a bit too general; he takes the highest level of international acting art too casually.

With a popular actress playing Ibsen's famous "Nora," and the director doing his best to make the performance a success, it is true that the overall stage arrangement of this "Nora" performance was good, and the performance techniques were quite successful. Among the recent public performances, it can be considered the most successful. But to compare it to the highest level of international acting art is far too much. As for whether it has reached the highest level of domestic drama, I think it is hard to say.

Wasn't the last performance of "Roar, China!" at the Golden Grand Theater last year, the performance of the first two acts of "Storm on the Yangtze River" and "Nora After She Left" by Mailun Middle School, and the performance of the first two acts of "Song of Rejuvenation" and "Under the Mercury Lamp" this year, not very vivid and moving? Can the acting in this performance of "Nora" really surpass the above performances? Even "The Paint is Not Dry," performed by Jida not long ago, could the consideration of personality and the overall compactness be inferior to this performance of "Nora"?

"Nora" is indeed very difficult to play, and there are many shortcomings in this performance. Starting with Ms. Lan Ping, who plays Nora—Lan Ping played in "The Locked Box" last year. Her flexible performance, powerful movements, and especially her sharp and expressive eyes, I think she is the female actress in China who is currently the best at facial expressions.

This time, she played Nora, and from a forceful point of view, it was indeed good. However, she has two major shortcomings. We cannot ignore them just because she is generally good. Precisely because we hope that she will have a deep understanding of acting techniques, we must point out her shortcomings.

The first shortcoming is that her performance of joy and liveliness is very unnatural, forced, and contrived. The contrivance is too trivial, mediocre, and lacks generosity, which makes people feel unhappy. It is not the expression of Nora's childlike, lively, and lovable personality.

The second shortcoming is that her power is too monotonous. There is no change in the high and low levels. When she scolds Krogstad, she is so fierce and powerful. When she discovers that Helmer only loves her as a toy, her performance when she leaves is still the same power as before. Her power stops at the same level. Afterwards, she cannot increase her power and perform it with profound, resolute, and unyielding feeling. This is Ms. Lan Ping's failure. When Nora's borrowing money is discovered by her husband, and Helmer scolds her as a confused woman, how shocked, frightened, and indignant should Nora be? However, Lan Ping did not raise her energy and did not do it properly. When Nora says when she leaves, "I am a person. I want to educate myself. I want to fulfill my responsibilities to myself!" How much power should these words be said with, and the expression should be extremely serious and calm, to show her claim to maintain her independent personality, but Ms. Lan did not perform with any special enthusiasm here, only a consistent flat force, which is not enough. Also, when she says, "Millions of women in the world have sacrificed their reputations for men!" These words should be said with a resentful and indignant tone and expression, and the stage atmosphere at this time should be handled very seriously, but Ms. Lan did not deeply experience it. Furthermore, such as: "I don't believe in laws that don't care about women's interests. I want to see if I am wrong or if the whole world is wrong? - The whole world is wrong! Religion and law are things that protect special interests!" This climax of the top point should be performed with a complete rebellious spirit, seriously and resolutely, to what extent did Lan Ping grasp it here, and did she satisfy the audience very much? I hope that the audience who loves Ms. Lan's art should point out unceremoniously that she performed too weakly in this passage, and her expression was not enough.

In short, Ms. Lan's acting this time is much more powerful than that of ordinary actresses, and she also flexibly handled the position on the stage. It is only a pity that her liveliness is too unnatural, and her arrogance is fierce, sometimes close to frivolous, lacking composure and rhythmic movements; especially her power, from beginning to end, is a flat tone, like a piano without the highest and lowest octaves, unable to play tunes with high and low variations. But she is a promising actress, I hope she works hard!

Zhao Dan's role as Helmer is simply not in line with the personality, and his failure was expected. He is too young and his figure is too small. It is best to play a young man with vigor and firmness. He plays Helmer, a middle-aged gentleman. At the very least, he doesn't have the demeanor of a gentleman, he can't put on the airs of a husband, and he doesn't look like a hypocrite who is deeply involved in accidents. When Helmer discovers his wife's concealment, he is so angry that he reveals his hypocritical mask himself, and nakedly throws out his selfish face, scolding Nora viciously and violently for the sake of his own reputation. This is the key to the transformation of the whole play. How should he understand the plot and make that hateful and abominable appearance? Although Zhao Dan worked very hard here, he didn't seem hateful. When the creditor returned the IOU, Helmer wanted to bring his wife back into his palm to play with. Although Zhao Dan did a good job here, it was like arguing with a little lover and then trying to apologize, not describing the psychology of Helmer, a gentleman and a hypocrite.

Ms. Wu Mei, who plays Mrs. Linton, was so dull and lifeless in the first act, not at all like a woman struggling in hardship, and even less could one see that she was a woman with commercial knowledge. Her shriveled and pitiful appearance simply did not resemble the character in the play. The last two acts were quite in line with the status of a widow, but they were still too dull.

Mr. Wei Heling's Dr. Nan Kai is too hunchbacked and too old and decadent. His unrequited and pitiful psychology can be said to be very well expressed, but he was not very successful, because he did not achieve that timid and laughable state. This is a difficult and thankless role, difficult to play and difficult to succeed. Ms. Wu Ling, who plays the maid, has an air that is too noble. Only Jin Shan played to excellent success.

These words may be seeking flaws in jade, but speaking of acting art with a serious attitude, I feel that I have to say it this way.

A Drunkard 184

— Lin Ni

There is such a person, he has existed in the world, but it seems that he will never exist, until the people who remember him also die. He has no political views, he doesn't know Newton, he doesn't know Edison, but he knows the names of grasses better than me, which grass can cure which disease, and he knows the changes in the weather better. He knows how much grain this field produces, and how much grain that field produces. When a chicken is placed in his hand, he can tell its weight, with little difference. Such a person, I call him "Third Uncle". Third Uncle is the eighteenth generation. People of the twentieth generation must call him "Third Uncle". Third Uncle is the third child. Third Uncle's older brother is Second Uncle, Fukang Uncle—also called Eldest Uncle. But my father calls Third Uncle "Shoukang Uncle". I almost forgot; Third Uncle's own name was originally "Shoukang", arranged according to the three characters of "Fu, Lu, Shou" (Fortune, Prosperity, Longevity). Apart from the name Shoukang, I have never heard any other name for Third Uncle. He probably doesn't have any other alias, unlike Uncle Hongru, who teaches books, whose alias is Lingxiao, also called Qingshan Hermit, with so many variations.

Behind my house is a large road, leading directly from the county town to the border of Jiangxi. It is an important traffic route, and there are quite a few guests coming and going. So, shops were built on both sides of the road. There were eight or nine in total, and because it was a place to rest, the first building on the west side was an inn. Many cargo carriers stopped there every night, which was quite lively. The rest included three or four wine and rice shops, a tailor shop, a grocery store, a opium den, and a closed medicinal materials store. The words "Chang'an Hall熟藥" (Chang'an Hall Prepared Medicine) still remained on the wall.

Counting from the west, the fourth Taian Wine and Rice Store was opened by my uncle. I inherited it from my uncle, and I mostly stayed in the store when I came back from school. During the busy farming season, my family was busy with farming, and my uncle sometimes had to go to the county town or go to market, so I would take a day off and take care of the business in the store. Among the many drinkers, Third Uncle was also a regular customer. Unless my family's wine was sold out, he would not go to other stores. He always praised my uncle's wine for being good, with bubbles filling the cup—real "piled flower liquor". He also praised me, saying that I was so young, but I could write accounts and greet customers. Third Uncle had a fixed amount of alcohol. He didn't say anything, just four taels of liquor and two spiced dried tofu; if you asked him, he would say, "Nephew, you know." Most of the time, I poured the wine for him, but sometimes he would pour it himself. After pouring the wine, he would squat on the bench outside the counter, shrug his shoulders, take a sip of wine, hold it in his mouth for a while, and then slowly swallow it. Then he would bite into a piece of spiced dried tofu, chew it slowly, and then take another sip of wine. I liked Third Uncle, so I poured him a little more when pouring wine. Once, my uncle came out of the study and saw that I had poured too much, he raised his eyebrows and glared at me, and after Third Uncle went out, he said, "Don't pour too much, just fill it up, if you keep doing this, you won't even have enough to sell the fields." "Pour a little more for Third Uncle, it's not the same for others." "Is Third Uncle's money bigger than others'? The bigger it is, the stupider it is." But as long as my uncle was not around, I would secretly pour a little more wine for Third Uncle.

—To be continued—

Wife 185

— Long Gong Gong

When Zhu Wu was losing his mind because of gambling, he would talk to me about lengthy things. Most of those words were about his wives. There was a time when I mistakenly thought he was a three-wives-and-four-concubines character, not a poor and stingy congee shop owner.

"Alas, gambling this thing—no wonder people say that only smart people suffer from gambling, look, today, I've lost again!"

At the kitchen entrance at the stern of the ship, on the hatch covered with thick canvas, or on the deck, he would say those words to me when he met me, as if he had done something wrong to me and had to find a reason to explain to me.

"There is no losing without gambling, you can only see fish when the pond is dry."

"The pond is dry? ... But my boss lady who manages the pond is too stupid!" he said as if he was about to cry, raising his fist and hitting his own temples. "If she understood your words, she wouldn't be fighting with me so desperately, not letting go of a single penny... But, let's talk about something else."

His sad face, shriveled, crooked, would occasionally arouse people's pity, but due to the experience gained on the ship in the past few days, I knew that he probably wouldn't talk about anything else. It would still be about how he married a certain wife at some point, and then married another. His face would flush with a more lovely bright red color, and his yellow waxy skin would be baked by the hot fire, drying up and curling.

The transparent cloud shadows unique to autumn reflected the pure blue, brave, and clean surface of the sea, so there was a kind of grand, dizzying light that enveloped us.

"Knowing what people are not well-meaning towards you, and having guilty consciences that are difficult to explain to you, you must forget them immediately. Then you will be blessed."

Every place on him that could store things was filled with worldly lessons. Some of them were ignorant, unreasonable, and very funny. But for Zhu Wu himself, he was only happy when he took out these reserves and bragged to others.

"I have married three wives. Think about it, if that's the case, how much can a person understand! The first one was called Ajiao Jie, she was a working 'Ama Jie' who went to Beiping with her master. I knew why she wanted to go with her master, but we 'lived together' without negotiating the price, so I didn't ask her, and I didn't wait for her. The second one was called Qiaodi, she was a Ningbo woman of unknown origin, she gave birth to a daughter for me, but she was more noisy than my daughter, so I simply sold them both to Singapore. The third one was also bought with money, she gambled on lottery all day long, I lost a lot of money to her, once I beat her hard, and she hanged herself. Now, what you see is my wife, this is the fourth one; in fact, besides creating trouble for me, there is nothing else, and there will be none."

Sometimes he would add:

"In short, if they want to spend a few of your money and make you suffer a little loss for them, there are so many ways!"

I could not agree with his opinion, painfully opened my mouth and looked at him, unable to find words to refute him. He was very clear about me, knowing that I had never been married and was very poor.

"What do you have to be so proud of? Everything you can do, they can do. Drinking, smoking, what else?" I finally said calmly. "From the first day you were born, you have received the grace of women. No matter what kind of disaster they are in, they are calm and virtuous. How many men drink alcohol? Selling themselves overseas, killing people, or killing themselves, but women always live patiently. Letting themselves not live, and raising you."

"Okay, according to you, what position should we give women to sit in? - I don't understand your words at all, and you don't understand mine."

He simply expressed his doubts like this, and went to the deck to stand blankly next to any gambling game. Sometimes he would stand there for an hour or two before stretching lazily and listlessly crawling down into the hold.

When he won money, he would jump to the side of the ship and shout to the great, boundless blue sea:

"On my head there were originally the two words widower,

Now that I have a wife, and she,

Reaches out to pick them off for me..."

His singing method was very strange, as if he had created it himself with genius. Many "uh-ya, uh-ya" interludes were inserted in the middle of the turbid nasal sounds. Sometimes, listening to it, it felt as if he had quickly patched together pieces of popular stage songs, piece by piece.

Sometimes he would make peculiar moves that others could not imitate, showing the depth to which he was falling into happiness. He would throw away an empty tin can, make a certain athletic posture, and say in his mouth:

"Goodbye for now, we'll meet again in the future, go!" With that, he threw the small piece of waste into the sea. Attracted by the waves, it quickly and involuntarily retreated backwards, and soon disappeared far behind.

Zhu Wu began to explain to me how the friendship between the sea and the ship had deteriorated, and what kind of relationship they now maintained.

"The sea is smart, strong, and gentle," he said, drawing circles in the air with one arm. "But all the ships are sorry for it. - That is, they dump a lot of coal slag on it every day. It can't stand it, so every time it sees a ship passing by, it shows its teeth. Look at these waves, why does the sea have waves? ... The ship still dumps coal slag on it, cunningly passing through the gaps in its teeth, making it so angry that it spits out white foam from its mouth..."

He often used this beautiful imagination to entertain himself, or others that he liked.

Signing 186

— Zheng Hua

In his tearful eyes, he only saw black spots flying around,

A pen, a contract of indenture,

Lifting his heavy hand with tons of strength,

Holding the pen tightly, not daring to breathe!

Quietly pressing against his own heartbeat,

Hot tears dissolved with ink dripping into the inkstone,

Unable to bear to hear his daughter sobbing behind him,

Looking again at the master's majesty, he dared not force himself to look!

Feigning, with a face full of smiles,

Even speaking must include a few auspicious words,

Regardless of the slanting characters he pressed on the contract,

From then on, the relationship between the two of them was severed!

Stuffing a dozen dollars into his empty pocket,

Walking out of the vermilion gate, the only thing sent behind was a dog's bark!

University Days (27) 187

— by German author Storm, translated by Chen Yin Zhi

'A bastard, eh? - His face is indeed that of a bastard!'

'Nelly, then?' I asked, staring at my friend. 'Did she go to the dancing-school of your 'Latins' and caper with this pale-faced knight of her own free will?'

He contracted his brow, and I saw a haze of sleepy cloud pass into his eyes.

'I do not know,' he murmured. - 'You ought not to have dragged the little girl to dance at your 'Latins' school to fill up the number, just as an excuse.'

He stretched his hand out to me. 'Farewell, Philip!' he said, 'The money, I will send back to you; otherwise, you will not hear from me; but a year hence, if God wills, I shall come here again, or return to our home.'

He went away. - I tried to continue the reading of my book, but it was altogether impossible; care for the future fate of this companion of my childhood, occupied my mind. All that had not been plainly spoken by his words, I understood; I knew that his whole soul was filled with the image of that girl, and that this strong head was exerting all its powers for the one object, that his life might be united with hers.

I went down soon after to the apartments of the landlady, with whom I boarded. I was perhaps a little too early, for not one of the other lodgers had yet come; but in the little side-room I found the seamstress, the 'Lame Mary', silently and solitarily sewing among a heap of white linen. - As I often saw her walking with the two whom I now felt so deep an interest in, I told her yesterday's story, in the hope that I might learn from her its true explanation.

'I knew it would be so!' she said, closing her thin lips very tightly; 'the carpenter was indeed good in every way, but too compliant towards the little girl. - Why go with her to the dancing-room?'

I urged her to further explanations.

She laid a portion of the linen aside, and cleared a chair that I might sit down. - 'You perhaps know the little shop in Monk's Alley,' she began, when I, interpreting her look, had sat down on the chair; 'that old Smidten, Nelly's aunt, some years ago bought this cottage of the man who lets out horses in the neighborhood; but the garden behind it, the seller kept back, still uniting it with his own, because he required the open space for his business; the old woman could only wash and bleach her linen in a little space of grass in the middle of the court, but this space was sufficient for her. She was a cousin of my deceased mother, and I used to go out with her to needlework, after my fourteenth year.'

'I remember that, a little before Martinmas last year, I went to the Smidten's after dinner, because we had a lot of silk goods to wash. On the road I met the carpenter, who had been already going to and coming from Nelly, and we talked a few words together, at parting he even said to me, smiling: 'I shall come on the evening before the feast-day, to help you in hanging up the linen that has been washed.' I repeated these words to Nelly, but she did not seem to pay much attention to them.'

Supplement to the Local News of Shen Bao

Talk

Abyssinia Can Console Itself 188

— Xing An

A country must save itself before others save it. The sound of war drums in Abyssinia has recently aroused the sympathy of people from all countries. According to reports, people from all countries who are willing to provide assistance are very enthusiastic.

London: Some retired British officers have organized mercenaries to go to Abyssinia to help fight. Recently, they have been secretly recruiting soldiers in London and other provinces to go to Abyssinia next month.

New York: Hundreds of black people here have volunteered to serve Abyssinia. Although the Abyssinian king has not yet approved of this move by American black people, the black people here have not hesitated in the slightest to support Abyssinia's resistance against Italy.

London: An American company here is willing to provide Abyssinia with 50 skilled pilots and one doctor, and another company is willing to provide a large number of military officers and a large amount of ammunition.

America: Black man Davis, who served as a junior officer during the European War, has recently been recruiting soldiers, preparing to serve Abyssinia when the Italian-Abyssinian War breaks out.

Berlin: Austrian National Socialists who have been expelled from the country are now mobilizing to assist Abyssinia in fighting against Italy.

I often say that there is no justice in today's world. If there is, it is probably the law of the jungle? But are weak nations so easily subdued? Abyssinia's unyielding spirit is enough for the weak to breathe a sigh of relief.

Abyssinia is a small and weak nation. It wants to resist an old-fashioned fascist power, just like a mantis trying to stop a chariot, which is often seen as overestimating its own capabilities. However, the Abyssinian king refuses to give in at all. He delivered an impassioned speech to the Chamber of Nobles the other day, in which he said that warriors should emulate the bravery of their ancestors, regardless of age, and jointly defend against the invaders. If necessary, their king will shed blood on the battlefield for Abyssinia and its independence without hesitation. It is better to die for freedom than to live as a slave for ten thousand years. If a peaceful solution cannot be found at the last minute, Abyssinia will reach out to God for grace. Such a generous and passionate spirit cannot help but make people prostrate themselves.

But strong countries ultimately help strong countries. Even if weak countries have justice and fairness, they cannot eat anything. Therefore, recently, the governments of various countries are discussing refusing to supply Abyssinia with ammunition, which cannot but discourage Abyssinia. However, the world's justice has not completely died after all. Observing that people from all countries are willing to help Abyssinia, they have risen one after another. Abyssinia can also be proud of itself.

Child 189

— Wei Yun

The child has grown even more adorable: wearing a newly bought sailor suit, and my hat, which is twice the size of his head, his eyes and nose are buried in the hat like a watermelon, he raises his hand in a military salute. This is one example. He knows so much, even though he is only two years and two months old.

Today, when he returned from his grandmother's house, the first thing he said when he ran into the house was "Grandma—board—buy—melon—," while stretching out both hands as if I couldn't write an article, circling in the small room. He was also like a great orator, repeating "Grandma, board, buy, melon," over and over, which was quite amusing.

After walking for a while, perhaps suddenly thinking about the taste of the melon that Grandma bought, he threw himself onto my knees, raised his head, his small eyes as big as waxberries, and said, "Daddy, buy—melon—fresh (sweet)!"

I didn't answer him, as I was thinking about something else, a look the child was used to. "Daddy—earn—board," he thought I was going to write an article, so he went under the table and said to his mother:

"Melon—gone!" He raised his small palms to the sky, not knowing where he had learned this gesture.

His wife then coaxed him, "Daddy will buy it tomorrow," while telling me that the child had seen the watermelon his grandmother carried down and had been playing with it, but he couldn't move any of them. When it was time to go home, he even tried to move the biggest watermelon. "We really should buy one tomorrow, it's so hot!" his wife finally said.

"Mom!" the child immediately jumped over, making a circular shape with his little hands, "Fresh—melon—buy!"

He gestured and spun in a circle, suddenly shouting "Hat! Hat!" "Daddy—Hat! Hat!"

This was different from the fresh watermelon; he burst into loud cries.

His wife immediately picked him up and coaxed him: Daddy will buy you watermelon tomorrow, fresh ones, and also, a hat. But the child ignored her, he just kept crying, using his small hands to make a circular shape, shouting "Hat! Hat!"

I felt a little uncomfortable. The child was just being unreasonable, wanting watermelons and hats. There were many more important things we hadn't bought for our house, and perhaps the rice bucket would tell me tonight that we needed money. But the child cried even harder; he had never cried so intensely since he was born. Since he had come into this world as a person, crying couldn't resist the pressure of being wronged!

His wife seemed to be out of options, holding him in one arm and waving a foreign doll at him to coax him.

Last year, when the child turned one, we took him to the department store to buy a set of flannel shirts and pants as a gift. When we got to the toy section, he started babbling excitedly. He saw a large foreign doll on the counter that raised its hand in salute. He cried and wanted to buy it, but after seeing the price tag, I finally carried him away. Naturally, his crying didn't stop, so his wife bought a small toy to coax him home.

From then on, the child learned to salute and often shouted "Doll." His little heart couldn't forget that fun thing. This spring, I mustered my courage several times and bought a bugle-playing foreign doll for him. The child was overjoyed; he wanted the doll as soon as he woke up in the morning and wanted to hug it to sleep at night. His wife specially made a set of small clothes for it, and the child was always holding it in his hands, imitating his mother's attitude. But today, the foreign doll's misfortune had arrived. When his wife handed it to him, the child forcefully threw it down, but he was still not satisfied. He squeezed down from his mother's arms and trampled the foreign doll into a flat pancake.

My anger rose. How could he have such a big temper at such a young age? Didn't he know how hard it was to buy this foreign doll and make a new set of clothes! I jumped up from the chair, wanting to give him a beating; but the child was smart. He immediately threw himself at my knees, waving his little hands and calling "Daddy," wanting me to hold him. His wife, afraid that I would really hit him, coaxed him to go to bed—he still whispered to his wife that he wanted to buy a hat.

This happened a month ago. I was carrying him back from the park, and when we walked past a very large foreign goods store, the glass cabinet was hanging with all kinds of children's hats. The child immediately clamored to buy one. I told him that Daddy didn't have any money, that we would buy a good one in a few days. He nodded in agreement, but he wasn't as agreeable as he had been with the foreign doll. After so many days, I still haven't been able to fulfill his advance wish. The child transferred his anger to the foreign doll—perhaps he understood a little about the ways of the world.

But until other matters are settled, although I sincerely want to buy him a hat, I'm afraid it will never be possible. I just hope he doesn't dream about making hats tonight!

— Hu Kao

Pitiful that she's only thirteen years old and dressed up like this!

On the Ship 190

— Simon

In the sweltering heat of a June day, even disembarking at midnight was oppressively hot. Just getting the luggage settled, large beads of sweat had already soaked my forehead, and even the innermost layer of my undershirt was drenched. And the ship's peculiar odor of kerosene, the musty smell of rust, and the indescribably filthy, mixed stench evaporated in waves around my nose, irritating me. It was almost unbearable enough to make me vomit. So, I had no choice but to temporarily escape this stifling atmosphere, take the handrail, step onto the deck to catch some wind, stand in front of the iron railing, and gaze at the distant night seascape.

From the narrow walkway that connected to the staircase, stretching to the middle of the ship's hull, was entirely the steerage area. Each passenger had already claimed their spot for their mat, spreading them out haphazardly, east and west, lying crowded together, some standing and a few sitting together, chatting idly. Hawkers soliciting business on the ship weaved through the crowds, calling out their wares. Added to this, the sound of the engine turning and the noise of various voices created an extraordinary cacophony.

This symphonic chaos continued until late into the night, gradually quieting down. Now, only the small waves crashed against the ship's hull, one after another, creating light, brittle sounds.

In the silence, a sighing voice suddenly said behind me, speaking to someone:

"Alas, having become such a useless person, how can I face my relatives? Our ancestors didn't leave us three plots of land or two houses, and I have a wife, children, and an old mother to support. Who will feed us? How will we get through the days? It would have been better to have been beaten to death that time."

"Well, whether we live or die, we can't worry about it ourselves. Let's just go back and see what happens. If there's food, we'll all eat together. If there's no food, we'll all go hungry,"

The person answering seemed more optimistic, comforting the other person, but after speaking, they both sighed deeply.

"Damn it, we're human beings too, why should we sacrifice our lives for nothing, letting those dogs and rabbits trample on us, using us as footrests!"

The person speaking became more agitated, his voice filled with extreme resentment.

"Don't talk about it, it's no use. Just blame ourselves for being weak. We're destined to suffer our whole lives."

The conversation between the two gradually became clearer. Then, several people, seemingly awakened from a light sleep, yawned, turned over laboriously, and then someone asked:

"What are you talking about so excitedly? Don't you want to sleep! Isn't it late?"

"You... you're so lucky, you can fall asleep as soon as you lie down."

One of the two answered with a cold laugh.

Sighs escaped from everyone's throats, lingering mournfully in the silent night.

Quarrel 191

— Ling Zixi

The weather is getting hotter day by day: first, the more than half a month of drought in the rice paddies, the sun blazing like fire, from early morning to dusk, as if determined to bake this field into ashes; people worked desperately on the waterwheels during the day for those delicate seedlings, the lifeblood, and in the evening, they stared blankly at a coarse meal, their hearts agitated beyond belief—as if a scorching sun was roasting them. And half a month ago, with difficulty, there were several heavy rains, and people were happy, as if a pile of stones had been removed from their hearts, but unexpectedly, the rain did not stop; rice paddies were not like seedling beds, they were no longer suitable for a large amount of water, and the weather gradually cooled down, and the melons and fruits in the fields were no longer worth much money. The worst thing was that the water kept pouring down, and the low-lying areas had already started to flood; in this way, the hope and joy that people had raised were once again cooled down, and this cold water seemed to have flowed into their hearts, and just thinking about it would make people panic and tremble.

Because of this, people no longer had a sense of peace, but were just going around in circles in worry and anxiety. With an agitated mood and grim faces, everyone just wanted to be temperamental. So, they scolded chickens and dogs, and even lost their pleasant tone.

In the fields, disputes over the arrears of one or two liters of grain were common: faces flushed red, they spoke loudly in the dialect of the fields, saliva spraying like unstoppable raindrops, arguing, cursing, and fighting. In the middle of this, a mixture of resentment, panic, and emotionality was intricately mixed, like a tangled knot.

In the family, people also learned to be rude from their worries, and it was not surprising that wives resented their husbands and husbands beat their wives because life was not going very well. Because the man went out to borrow rice but couldn't, or spent some of the money from selling the only piece of homespun cloth: he bought liquor, drank himself drunk, and came back reeking of alcohol; of course, the wife would not let it go, grabbing the man and making a deadly scene; life was difficult, how could he want to turn the whole family into yellow soup? "You immortal drunkard, I've been married to you my whole life and haven't had a single good day. You still have the heart to pour the money the whole family worked so hard for down your throat! I've had enough of living, I don't want to live anymore, you wretch, I'll fight you to the death..."

Crying,闹ing, and the man, with liquor in his stomach and irritation in his heart, all the unpleasantness of life taught him a kind of terrible barbarity, his eyes turned red, he dragged the woman over without saying a word, grabbed her hair, and punched her body desperately: "I, I... I've had enough of living, you all go to hell!"

"Hit me, hit me, it's okay if you hit me to death, I'll fight you, I'll fight you to the death..."

Crying,闹ing, cursing, and fighting; the long night passed by heavily. When they woke up the next day, they still harbored an unspeakable resentment and anger. Thinking about it carefully, there was no reason for any of this; however, it always stuck in people's hearts like a thorn, how uncomfortable!

In the fields, in the village, daily quarrels followed the difficulties of life, drifting like summer rain: after passing, it happened again. This, like a comedy of life, was being staged intermittently; however, everyone felt that this was definitely not a comedy. Everyone remembered: their original temperament didn't seem to be like this at all, but now, life seemed to have sprinkled a little spicy pepper into people's temperament, making people unknowingly agitated and uncomfortable.

Perhaps, these unprovoked, unpleasant quarrels followed fate and the years; perhaps this was a gust of wind that would soon calm down?

Page 21

Boredom and Loneliness 192

— Lu Sun

Like being bitten in the heart by a venomous snake, like being bound in the limbs by a soft rope, unable to move freely, in short, something indescribable entangled me on all sides; sometimes I simply had no place in this world to put my own body. This kind of suffering relentlessly tormented me day and night, so on rainy days, I would rush out the door in a raincoat, like an office worker going to work; it was as if there were ghosts in my house, and I wanted to escape that kind of torment. However, when the cold raindrops hit me, I felt it was too pointless. What was the point of rushing out the door? I couldn't turn back, so I just followed my feet, but actually, my legs wouldn't have any ideas. Walking along one road after another, so slowly: watching the streetcars drive back and forth on the tracks, watching the rickshaw pullers bend their backs to resist the oncoming wind, perhaps I hoped that a beautiful woman would do a somersault from the car's canopy, which would make me laugh heartily for a while. People seemed like crazy people, without any ideas: but they had too many to be arranged. For example: I passed a friend's house, I thought in my heart, I'll go in and chat for a while. Naturally, I pressed the doorbell, and my friend invited me in, whether they were close or unfamiliar. As soon as I sat down, a second idea scolded me for being meddlesome, and I immediately found a question that they couldn't answer and left them. But as soon as I stepped out the door, I asked myself again, wouldn't it be good to sit for a while?

Although all my actions were a bit abnormal, I often regretted them afterward, and I was determined never to do it again in the future; however, when I was ambushed by that indescribable pain, I was not allowed to have any worries. When these actions fell into my friends' eyes, they all said that I was "bored." I myself didn't admit it, and sometimes this question would cause my long-winded arguments, and even the matter of falling out with my closest friends happened often.

Recently, a classmate from my childhood got married, and many old friends gathered at the wedding feast. Perhaps they were well-intentioned, and they united to attack me: saying that I was perverted, saying that I was probably caught in the web of love again, using various methods to provoke me. I was very annoyed in my heart. Under normal circumstances, I would definitely leave without saying goodbye. It was inexcusable in every way to use such vicious words to make fun of a friend who was tormented by suffering. But that day was my friend's auspicious day, and as the host, I didn't want to spoil their fun like that; so I also seized on everyone's handles and looked for ways to retaliate. Later, almost all of my friends' unmentionable secrets were exposed by me, and I felt more pleased than ever before. When they publicly elected me to be the leader of the wedding night antics, I regained that energy and poured down several glasses of liquor.

That day, I completely changed into a different person, making so much noise, and using all kinds of playful and smiling tricks. I knew from everyone's faces that they were also very happy. They thought that I had been rescued from the abyss of pain. They proposed organizing a progress association or something, so that so many friends would have the opportunity to meet often. They wanted to reform me, and I was also willing to be reformed by them: my heart was saved, my limbs regained their freedom, within those few hours.

But when I bid farewell to the host and returned home, as soon as I stepped into my cramped dwelling, those invisible ropes bound my limbs again. The subtle happiness I had just gained was replaced by more painful memories. It was a moonlit night, plastering the world with a silver light. In this silver light, I could see humans very clearly: they could only unite for their own benefit, otherwise they were all alone. Friends—even my parents and wife were linked together by that kind of relationship. So, that indescribable pain, perhaps it was the loneliness of being alone? I lived so lonely in this world!

Opening "Qin Cao"

Willow Pavilion on the water, peach blossoms and singing fans in the mirror, a flat lake with boundless scenery, ladies and gentlemen like clouds kicking up soft dust, a boat carrying the romantic Su Xuelsi, he was a banished immortal from the Jade Hall to Hangzhou, with leisure from his official duties he traveled with Qin Cao, belonging to the number one in the brothel, chewing flowers and blowing stamens skillful at teasing smiles, carving the moon and tailoring clouds recording new songs, occasionally teasing in the boat, I became an elder examining Qing Qing, Qing Qing tried to meditate and explained the precepts, answering three or four of them well, Dongpo slapped the table and raised his voice, desolate in front of the door, getting older, why doesn't Qiu Niang marry a merchant, Qin Cao suddenly understood in a few words, willingly shaved her head and entered the empty gate, ice from the nine heavens turned into a flower-scattering person, Zen mind already turned into mud-stained catkins, those slanting winds and fine rains are not concerned, burning incense and chanting Buddhist mantras, always picking flowers and avoiding guests, the bell and fish chime echoes in the ancient temple.

News 196

Recently, singing societies have been organized like bamboo shoots after a rain, countless in number, but dissolutions also occur from time to time. Recently, the St. Anna Singing Society, jointly organized by movie company's Xu Wuyi and Feng Han, has been in preparation for more than a month, and it is said that a special program will be broadcast on a major radio station soon.

The "Singing Star Pictorial" published by the Singing Star Pictorial Society is now open for pre-orders. As a discount for readers, it is specially priced at 20% off, with each issue selling for only 16 cents. The content includes over a hundred fine copperplate prints of singing star photos, and the text is also written by the singing stars themselves, totaling more than 30,000 words. The inaugural issue also includes a signed photo of the popular singing star Ms. Bai Hong. Pre-orders are now being accepted from today onwards. The location is the Old West Gate Shu Xin Bookstore, No. 148, Hou Deli, Tang Jiawan, Old West Gate. Please include a 16-cent stamp for mail orders sent to the distribution department of the society. The publication will be sent to you immediately after it is published.

Movie News

New Era News 197

The new era's new film "Mr. Wang Goes to the Countryside" is about to start filming. Yesterday, the entire crew was gathered to discuss the plot. Laughter never stopped during the discussion. When it came to a certain segment, little A Yuan Huang Naishuang clapped and laughed loudly, repeatedly praising it as wonderful.

In "Mr. Wang Goes to the Countryside," because he is living in the countryside, Mr. Wang and his wife and children have all changed into rural attire. Little Chen, because he is playing the role of a relief committee member, has also changed from a Western suit to a Chinese suit in order to match the identity of the character in the play.

"Knowing Person" Lan Ping 198

— Photo by Chen Yaoting

"The Tempest" Arrives in Nanjing 199

The interior scenes for the Yihua talkie "The Tempest," which has been in preparation and filming for more than a year, have finally been completely shot.

In this film: Yuan Meiyun plays the innocent and lively Lingling, Wei Heling plays Wei Mingda, who is struggling in unemployment, Zhu Naidong plays Zhao Baiyun, who is brave and righteous, Cang Yinqiu plays the silly elder sister Xiao Baizi, Qin Tong plays the bitter old man, Jin Yi plays a Turk, Zhang Zhizhi plays the villain who does all kinds of evil, Guan Hongda plays a rogue, child star Liu Li plays a bitter child, and "Fugitive" director Yue Feng plays a Japanese as an exception, and speaks Japanese. The roles are distributed very appropriately, so everyone's acting skills have developed extraordinarily. Yesterday, director Yuan Congmei specially led the entire crew to take the ship that set sail at six o'clock in the morning to Nanjing to take exterior scenes. If the weather is good, they can return to Shanghai within five days.

Mingyue Society's Li Mingjian Stars in "Peanuts" at the New Light Theater 200

A Gift of Peach Blossom Fans 201

The Xinhua Film Company produced "The Peach Blossom Fan," and specially commissioned Mr. Zhang Yuguang to exquisitely paint peach blossom fans to be given to various circles. However, some restrictions had to be put in place. So, Mr. Zhang Shankun came up with a novel idea: Jin Yan, Hu Ping, Tong Yuejuan, Dai Yanwan, Wang Cilong, Gu Menghu, Zhou Fengwen, Zha Tianying, Zhang Zhizhi, and others each had a picture taken of the back of their heads. These were then cast into printing plates and published in the newspaper, allowing people to guess who they were. Those who guessed correctly could win a peach blossom fan, and the winner could designate who would inscribe the fan with a personal message.

"Sea Burial" at Shidao Island 202

(Previous omitted) That day, we arrived at the desolate Shidao Island. The fishermen on the island, for some strange reason, were watching our group, never leaving our side. Our accommodation became a problem, and after some debate, we had to temporarily settle in a dilapidated old house. At night, no one thought about sleeping, and they started talking about ghosts, using this old house as the subject. This was terrible; it caused Misses Li Ying and Fang Pei to dream of ghosts at night, and they suspected that there really were ghosts in this old house.

In this terrifying den, besides the low ceilings and damp ground, it was also filled with the smell of fish. Director Wang Bin, regardless of everything, started talking about the preparations for the filming tomorrow. Fu Baolu and Fang Pei read lines, Chen Tianguo and Tian Fang looked at the script, Wang Bin, Zhou Hekang, Shen Yongshi, and Zhou Yulin researched methods for shooting the sea views and the issues of camera angles, Ma Dongwu, Wei Pengfei, and others prepared everything related to the production affairs. It looked like groups of small, connected meetings.

The sea was howling wildly. It was late at night, and their voices gradually grew quieter. One by one, they gradually started snoring, so exhausted that they forgot everything.
